Salah — Prayer
beginner
6 min
Occasions for Raising Hands in Prayer
Enumeration of places where raising hands is sunnah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the Hanafi occasions for raising hands in prayer and supplication, and distinguish them from the practices of other schools.

Core Idea
In the Hanafi school, raising hands is sunnah only in specific moments—not in every prayer transition.

This passage from Hashiya al-Tahtawi lists the precise occasions where raising the hands is a sunnah action according to the Hanafi school. Understanding these distinctions is crucial for correct practice and appreciating the madhhab's reliance on specific hadith evidence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the general principle
Note the opening statement: 'It is not sunnah except...' This establishes that raising hands is restricted to specific occasions, not generally recommended.
2
List the occasions inside prayer
The passage specifies three occasions within the prayer: opening takbir of every prayer, takbir of qunut in witr, and the extra takbirs of the two 'Eids.
These are the only places inside the formal prayer where raising hands is sunnah.
3
List the occasions outside prayer
Several occasions outside the prayer are mentioned: seeing the Ka'bah, touching the Black Stone, standing on Safa and Marwah, at 'Arafah, Muzdalifah, after the first two jamarat, during the istisqa' prayer, and after the post-salah tasbih and takbir.
These are all settings of supplication or worship where raising hands is recommended.
4
Identify the proofs cited
The passage cites 'agreement of reports' for the 'Eid takbirs and 'as the noble Sunnah has come' for the hajj-related occasions.
The proofs are from hadith, but the text does not quote them verbatim.
5
Recognize cross-madhhab differences
The Hanafi restriction contrasts with schools like the Shafi'i, which allow raising hands at every change of position in prayer (e.g., bowing, standing).
This highlights the importance of madhhab adherence in ritual practice.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فلا يسن إلا عند افتتاح كل صلاة وعند تكبير القنوت في الوتر وتكبيرات الزوائد في العيدين لاتفاق الأخبار وصفة الرفع فيها حذو الأذنين و یسن رفعهما مبسوطتين نحو السماء حين يرى الكعبة المشرفة أي وقت معاينتها فتكون العين في فقعس للعيدين ومعاينة البيت للدعاء وهو مستجاب و يسن رفعهما حين يستلم الحجر الأسود مستقبلاً بباطنهما الحجر و يسن رفعهما مبسوطتين نحو السماء داعياً حين يقوم على الصفا والمروة و كذلك عند الوقوف بعرفة و وقوف مزدلفة و في الوقوف بعد رمي الجمرة الأولى و الجمرة الوسطى كما ورد بذلك السنة الشريفة وترفع في دعاء الاستسقاء ونحوه لأن رفع اليد في الدعاء سنة و كذلك عند دعائه بعد فراغه من التسبيح والتحميد والتكبير الذي سنذكره عقب الصلوات كما عليه المسلمون في سائر البلدان
It is not sunnah except at the opening of every prayer, and at the takbir of qunut in witr, and the additional takbirs of the two 'Eids, due to the agreement of reports. The description of raising in them is to the lobes of the ears. And it is sunnah to raise them outstretched towards the sky when he sees the noble Ka'bah, meaning at the time of sighting it, so the eyes are at the collarbone for the two 'Eids and for sighting the House for supplication, and it is answered. And it is sunnah to raise them when he touches the Black Stone, facing it with the inner parts of his hands. And it is sunnah to raise them outstretched towards the sky supplicating when he stands on Safa and Marwah, and likewise when standing at 'Arafah, and standing at Muzdalifah, and in standing after throwing the first jamrah and the middle jamrah, as the noble Sunnah has come with that. And they are raised in the supplication for rain and the like because raising hands in supplication is sunnah. And likewise when he supplicates after finishing the tasbih, tahmid, and takbir that we will mention after the prayers, as the Muslims practice in all lands.
Source pages p. 284

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proofs from the Sunnah, expanding on the occasions where raising hands is sunnah according to the Hanafi school. It first affirms the general principle that raising hands is not sunnah except in specific places. Those places are: (1) the opening takbir of every prayer, (2) the takbir for qunut in witr, and (3) the additional takbirs in 'Eid prayers. Then it lists occasions outside the prayer where raising hands is sunnah: when seeing the Ka'bah, when touching the Black Stone, when standing on Safa and Marwah, at 'Arafah, at Muzdalifah, after the first two jamarat, in the istisqa' prayer (rain prayer), and after the post-salah tasbih and takbir. The proof for the 'Eid takbirs is 'agreement of reports' (hadiths). The proof for the other occasions is the practice of the Prophet (صلى الله عليه وسلم) as recorded in the Sunnah. The Hanafi position is that raising hands in supplication is sunnah, and these are specific instances where that sunnah is emphasized.

Key Terms
رفع اليدين (raf' al-yadayn): Raising the hands during prayer or supplication, a sunnah action with specific occasions as listed.
تكبير القنوت (takbir al-qunut): The takbir said at the beginning of the qunut supplication in witr prayer, after the bowing? Actually it is before qunut. Here it means the takbir for qunut.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, raising hands is sunnah in which of the following?
A) Every bowing and standing in prayer
B) Only at the opening takbir and qunut in witr
C) At the opening takbir, qunut in witr, 'Eid takbirs, and various supplications like at the Ka'bah
D) Only in the 'Eid prayer

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school limits raising hands (raf' al-yadayn) to specific moments in prayer and du'a, based on hadith evidence.

Sitting Posture and Tashahhud Recitation in the First Sitting
Rulings on first sitting posture and tashahhud recitation with meaning commentary.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to describe the correct sitting posture for men and women during the first tashahhud, recite the tashahhud of Ibn Mas'ud, and state the Hanafi view on the intention (insha' vs hikayah).

Core Idea
The worshipper initiates the tashahhud as a personal greeting; posture and wording are sunnah.

The first sitting after two rak'ahs is a distinct part of the prayer with its own posture and recitation. In the Hanafi school, the tashahhud of Ibn Mas'ud is the standard, and the worshipper must intend the meanings as if he is directly greeting Allah and His Messenger. This lesson outlines the practical rulings: how to sit, what to say, and the important distinction between initiation and narration.

Guided Path
1
Identify the sitting posture
For men: iftirash (spread left foot, sit on it, erect right foot). For women: tawarruk (sit on left hip, feet to the side).
Posture is sunnah; the act of sitting itself is wajib.
2
Recite the tashahhud of Ibn Mas'ud
The prescribed text begins with 'al-tahiyyatu lillahi wa al-salawatu wa al-tayyibat...' and includes the shahada. Do not add salawat in the first sitting.
The text is from a hadith; its recitation is sunnah muakkadah.
3
Intend the meanings as initiation
The worshipper should intend that he is uttering the words as his own greeting and salutation, not simply narrating what Allah said.
This is the relied-upon Hanafi view, contrary to some who consider it a narration.
4
Point the index finger
Raise the right index finger when saying 'la ilaha' (negation) and lower it when saying 'illa Allah' (affirmation).
Pointing is sunnah on the correct view.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإذا فرغ الرجل من سجدتي الركعة الثانية افترش رجله اليسرى، وجلس عليها ونصب يمناه ووجه أصابعها نحو القبلة، ووضع يديه على فخذيه وبسط أصابعه وجعلها منتهية إلى رأس ركبتيه والمرأة تتورك وقدمنا صفته وقرأ المصلي ولو مقتدياً تشهد ابن مسعود رضي الله عنه ويقصد معانيه مرادة له على أنه ينشئها تحية وسلاماً منه وأشار بالمسيحة من أصابعه اليمنى في الشهادة على الصحيح يرفعها عند النفي ويضعها عند الإثبات ولا يزيد على التشهد في القعود الأول لوجوب القيام للثالثة، وهو كما قال : علمني رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم التشهد أخذ كفي بين كفيه كما يعلمني السورة من القرآن فقال إذا قعد أحدكم في الصلاة فليقل التحيات الله والصلوات والطيبات جمع تحية من حيا فلان فلاناً إذا دعا له عند ملاقاته لقولهم حياك الله أي أبقاك الله والمراد هنا أعز الألفاظ التي تدل على الملك والعظمة، وكل عبادة قولية الله تعالى والمراد بالصلوات هنا العبادات البدنية، ونحوها، والطيبات العبادات المالية الله تعالى وهي الصادرة منه ليلة الإسراء فلما قال ذلك النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم بإلهام من الله تعالى رد الله عليه وحياه بقوله السلام عليك أيها النبي ورحمة الله وبركاته فقابل التحيات بالسلام الذي هو تحية الإسلام وقابل الصلوات بالرحمة التي هي بمعناها ذلك وقابل الطيبات بالبركات المناسبة للمال لكونها النمو والكثرة فلما أفاض سبحانه بإنعامه على النبي بالثلاثة مقابل الثلاثة، والنبي أكرم خلق الله وأجودهم عطف بإحسانه من الفيض لإخوانه الأنبياء والملائكة وصالحي المؤمنين من الإنس والجن فقال السلام علينا وعلى عباد الله الصالحين فعمهم به كما قال الله إنكم إذا قلتموها أصابت كل عبد صالح في السماء والأرض وليس أشرف من العبودية في صفات المخلوقين وهي الرضا بما يفعل الرب، والعبادة ما يرضيه والعبودية أقوى من العبادة لبقائها في العقبي بخلاف العبادة والصالح القائم بحقوق الله تعالى وحقوق العباد فلما أن قال ذلك : إحساناً منه شهد أهل الملكوت الأعلى والسموات وجبريل بوحي وإلهام أن قال كل منهم : أشهد أن لا إله إلا الله وأشهد أن محمداً عبده ورسوله أي أعلم وأبين وجمع بين أشرف أسمائه وبين أشرف وصف للمخلوق وأرقى وصف مستلزم للنبوة لمقام الجمع فيقصد المصلي إنشاء هذه الألفاظ مرادة له قاصداً معناها الموضوعة له عنده كأنه من يحيي الله سبحانه وتعالى ويسلم على النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم وعلى نفسه وأولياء الله تعالى خلافاً لما قاله بعضهم أنه حكاية سلام الله لا ابتداء سلام من المصلي وقرأ الفاتحة فيما بعد الركعتين الأوليين من الفرائض فشمل المغرب ثم جلس مفترشاً رجله اليسرى ناصباً اليمنى وتتورك المرأة وقرأ التشهد المتقدم ثم صلى على النبي ثم دعا ليكون مقبولاً بعد الصلاة على النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم بما يشبه ألفاظ
When a man finishes the two prostrations of the second rak'ah, he spreads his left foot and sits on it, erects his right foot and directs its toes toward the qiblah, places his hands on his thighs and spreads his fingers and makes them reaching to the top of his knees. The woman sits mutawarrikan and we have previously described its description. And the worshipper, even if following an imam, recites the tashahhud of Ibn Mas'ud (may Allah be pleased with him) and intends its meanings as his intention, as if he is uttering them as a greeting and salutation from him. And he points with his right index finger during the shahada, on the correct view: he raises it at the negation and lowers it at the affirmation. And he does not add anything to the tashahhud in the first sitting because standing for the third rak'ah is obligatory. And it is as he said: The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) taught me the tashahhud, taking my palm between his palms as he teaches me a surah from the Quran, and he said: 'When one of you sits in the prayer, let him say: al-tahiyyatu lillahi wa al-salawatu wa al-tayyibat...' (the full tashahhud). ... Then he recited al-Fatihah in what is after the first two rak'ahs of the fard prayers, so it includes Maghrib. Then he sat spreading his left foot and erecting the right, and the woman sits mutawarrikan, and recited the aforementioned tashahhud, then sent salawat upon the Prophet, then supplicated so that it may be accepted after sending salawat upon the Prophet (peace be upon him) with words similar (to something).
Source pages p. 284

Commentary
This passage is an expansion on the rulings of sitting for tashahhud and the recitation of the tashahhud itself. It covers several points: (1) The sitting posture for a man: iftrash (spreading the left foot and sitting on it, with the right foot erect). For a woman: tawarruk (sitting on the left hip with legs together). (2) The recitation of the tashahhud of Ibn Mas'ud, which is the prescribed tashahhud in the Hanafi school. The worshipper should intend the meanings, as if he is initiating greetings and salutations. (3) Pointing the index finger: raised at the negation ('la ilaha') and lowered at the affirmation ('illa Allah'). (4) In the first sitting (after two rak'ahs), only the tashahhud is recited, no salawat or du'a, because standing for the third rak'ah is wajib. (5) Then the text provides a detailed commentary on the meaning of the tashahhud, narrating its origin from the Prophet (peace be upon him) on the night of Isra', and explaining that each phrase (tahiyyat, salawat, tayyibat) corresponds to a response from Allah (salam, rahmah, barakat). The shahada is then witnessed by the inhabitants of the higher heavens and Jibril. The passage ends with a note that the worshipper is initiating these words, not merely narrating them, contrary to some who say it is a narration of Allah's greeting. Finally, for fard prayers, after the first two rak'ahs, the worshipper recites al-Fatihah for the remaining rak'ahs, then sits for the final tashahhud, sends salawat, and makes du'a.

Key Terms
افتراش (iftirash): Sitting posture for men in tashahhud: spreading the left foot and sitting on it, with the right foot erect.
التورك (al-tawarruk): Sitting posture for women and for men in the final tashahhud: sitting on the left hip with both feet to the right or on the side.
تشهد ابن مسعود (tashahhud Ibn Mas'ud): The specific wording of the tashahhud taught by the Prophet to Ibn Mas'ud: 'al-tahiyyatu lillahi wa al-salawatu wa al-tayyibat...'

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school as explained in this passage, what is the ruling on adding salawat upon the Prophet in the first tashahhud?
A) It is sunnah to add salawat
B) It is obligatory
C) It is not permissible
D) It is not recited because standing for the third rak'ah is obligatory

Key Takeaway
The first tashahhud is a sunnah muakkadah act where the worshipper initiates greetings using the Ibn Mas'ud wording, with specific postures for men and women.

Understanding the Meaning and Legal Status of the Tashahhud
Meaning and dispute regarding the tashahhud in the Hanafi school.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the symbolism of each phrase in the tashahhud, identify the Hanafi position on its legal status, and evaluate the dispute over whether it is a narration or an initiation.

Core Idea
The tashahhud reenacts the divine greeting received by the Prophet on the night of Isra'; the worshipper initiates the words as his own act of worship.

The tashahhud is more than a recitation; it is a profound dialogue that originated on the night of Isra'. The commentary in our passage reveals that each phrase corresponds to a divine response: 'tahiyyat' with 'salam', 'salawat' with 'rahmah', and 'tayyibat' with 'barakat'. Understanding this deepens the worshipper's presence. This lesson explores the symbolism and the legal dispute over whether the worshipper is narrating or actively initiating these words.

Guided Path
1
Understand the origin story
The Prophet (peace be upon him) was taught the tashahhud by Allah on the night of Isra'. He uttered the three praises (tahiyyat, salawat, tayyibat), and Allah responded with salam, rahmah, and barakat.
This story is foundational to the meaning.
2
Parse the three components of the greeting
Identify what each term represents: 'tahiyyat' (greetings/sovereignty), 'salawat' (bodily acts of worship), 'tayyibat' (financial worship).
These correspond to the three types of worship: heart, body, and wealth.
3
Identify the difference between insha' and hikayah
Insha': the worshipper initiates the words as his own. Hikayah: he merely narrates what Allah said. The Hanafi position is insha'.
The text explicitly says 'يقصد معانيه مراده له على أنه ينشئها'.
4
Recognize the practical impact
The insha' view makes the tashahhud an active act of worship (thana', salutation) rather than a passive report. It requires more presence of heart.
This difference affects the worshipper's intention and reward.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

على التشهد في القعود الأول لوجوب القيام للثالثة، وهو كما قال : علمني رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم التشهد أخذ كفي بين كفيه كما يعلمني السورة من القرآن فقال إذا قعد أحدكم في الصلاة فليقل التحيات الله إذا قلتموها أصابت كل عبد صالح في السماء والأرض وليس أشرف من العبودية في صفات المخلوقين وهي الرضا بما يفعل الرب، والعبادة ما يرضيه والعبودية أقوى من العبادة لبقائها في العقبي بخلاف العبادة والصالح Commentary

It covers several points: (1) The sitting posture for a man: iftrash (spreading the left foot and sitting on it, with the right foot erect). For a woman: tawarruk (sitting on the left hip with legs together). (2) The recitation of the tashahhud of Ibn Mas'ud, which is the prescribed tashahhud in the Hanafi school. The worshipper should intend the meanings, as if he is initiating greetings and salutations. (3) Pointing the index finger: raised at the negation ('la ilaha') and lowered at the affirmation ('illa Allah'). (4) In the first sitting (after two rak'ahs), only the tashahhud is recited, no salawat or du'a, because standing for the third rak'ah is wajib. (5) Then the text provides a detailed commentary on the meaning of the tashahhud, narrating its origin from the Prophet (peace be upon him) on the night of Isra', and explaining that each phrase (tahiyyat, salawat, tayyibat) corresponds to a response from Allah (salam, rahmah, barakat). The shahada is then witnessed by the inhabitants of the higher heavens and Jibril. The passage ends with a note that the worshipper is initiating these words, not merely narrating them, contrary to some who say it is a narration of Allah's greeting. Finally, for fard prayers, after the first two rak'ahs, the worshipper recites al-Fatihah for the remaining rak'ahs, then sits for the final tashahhud, sends salawat, and makes du'a.

Key Terms
افتراش (iftirash): Sitting posture for men in tashahhud: spreading the left foot and sitting on it, with the right foot erect.
التورك (al-tawarruk): Sitting posture for women and for men in the final tashahhud: sitting on the left hip with both feet to the right or on the side.
تشهد ابن مسعود (tashahhud Ibn Mas'ud): The specific wording of the tashahhud taught by the Prophet to Ibn Mas'ud: 'al-tahiyyatu lillahi wa al-salawatu wa al-tayyibat...'

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what does 'al-tayyibat' refer to in the tashahhud?
A) Good words
B) Attributes of Allah
C) Financial acts of worship
D) Bodily acts of worship

Key Takeaway
The tashahhud reenacts the divine greeting; each phrase symbolizes a type of worship, and the Hanafi school holds that the worshipper initiates these words as an act of direct worship.

The Intention in Tashahhud: Insha' vs. Hikayah in Hanafi Fiqh
Super-commentary on the intention for tashahhud and refutation of the narration view

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the intention in tashahhud, identify the proof from the hadith, and explain the refutation of the contrary opinion.

Core Idea
The tashahhud is the worshiper's own supplication, not a quotation — intention defines the act.

This lesson unpacks a critical distinction in Hanafi prayer: whether the tashahhud is the worshiper's own speech or a mere narration. The super-commentary of al-Tahtawi clarifies that the worshiper must intend the words as his own creation (insha'), refuting those who consider it a quotation of Allah's peace. This distinction affects the validity and reward of the prayer.

Guided Path
1
Identify the contested element
The dispute is about the nature of the tashahhud: is it insha' (creation) or hikayah (narration)?
The text explicitly mentions 'خلافاً لما قاله بعضهم' indicating a scholarly disagreement.
2
State the Hanafi position
The worshiper must intend the tashahhud as his own speech. The text says: 'فيقصد المصلي إنشاء هذه الألفاظ'.
This means the worshiper actively creates the words as his own supplication.
3
Examine the proof
The proof is the hadith of Ibn Mas'ud, where the Prophet taught the tashahhud. The wording 'أشهد أن محمداً عبده ورسوله' indicates the worshiper's testimony.
The hadith is a single-transmission (ahad) but accepted by the Hanafi school.
4
Analyze the contrary view
Some scholars hold that the tashahhud is a narration of Allah's peace. The Hanafi response is that the worshiper initiates the greeting, as shown by the phrase 'السلام علينا' which is a prayer from the worshiper.
The text refutes this by emphasizing the worshiper's active role.
5
Apply the ruling
In practice, the worshiper must consciously intend the meaning of the tashahhud and not merely recite. This ensures the act is valid and rewarded.
The omission of this intention does not invalidate the prayer but may reduce reward; the prayer remains valid if the words are recited correctly.

It is complete by the praise of Allah, glorified and exalted.

Commentary
This passage is a super-commentary (hashiya) on the concluding parts of the prayer, specifically the tashahhud and salam. The author explains that the worshiper should intend the words of tashahhud as his own speech (insha') rather than merely narrating what Allah says. He refutes those who claim it is a quotation of Allah's peace. The text then discusses the virtue of the phrase 'peace be upon us and upon the righteous servants of Allah,' noting that it includes all righteous beings. The best attribute for creation is servitude ('ubudiyya), which remains in the Hereafter as a state, unlike worship ('ibada) which is only for this worldly life. The commentary also clarifies that mentioning 'Gabriel' specifically highlights his superiority. The tashahhud wording is from Ibn Mas'ud, and its specification is recommended. Finally, the salam is performed turning right then left, with the intention of greeting the congregation and the guardian angels.

Key Terms
التشهد (al-tashahhud): The specific supplication recited while sitting in prayer, including the testimony of faith and blessings on the Prophet.
إنشاء (insha'): To originate or create the speech as one's own utterance, as opposed to merely quoting (hikayah).
العبودية (al-'ubudiyyah): A permanent state of servitude to Allah that continues in the Hereafter, characterized by contentment with His decree.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi prayer, the worshiper must intend the tashahhud as his own speech (insha'), not as a narration, and this intention is essential for the proper performance of the salah.

The Legal Ruling on Congregational Prayer in the Hanafi School
Analysis of ruling, definition, and intra-madhhab dispute on congregational prayer.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the five opinions on the ruling of congregational prayer within the Hanafi school and identify the mufta bihi position.

Core Idea
The Hanafi school holds congregational prayer as sunnah muakkadah, though strong wajib opinions exist.

This passage explores the ruling on congregational prayer, presenting a spectrum of five opinions within the Hanafi school and noting the Hanbali view. While the most correct view is sunnah muakkadah, the text highlights that even those who deem it obligatory do not invalidate individual prayer.

Guided Path
1
Identify the five Hanafi opinions
List the five rulings: wajib (obligatory), fard kifayah (collective duty), fard 'ayn (individual duty – Hanbali view attributed), sunnah muakkadah (emphasized sunnah), and mustahabb (recommended). Note which are within Hanafi school and which is external.
The text explicitly mentions Iraqi mashayikh (wajib), Karkhi/Tahawi (fard kifayah), Khurasanis (sunnah muakkadah), and a group who say mustahabb.
2
Distinguish intra-Hanafi from inter-madhhab disputes
Identify which positions are internal to the Hanafi school and which belong to other schools. The first three (wajib, fard kifayah, sunnah muakkadah) are all Hanafi; fard 'ayn is attributed to Imam Ahmad (Hanbali) and mustahabb is a later Hanafi view.
The disagreement among Hanafis is a legitimate ikhtilaf; the Hanbali position is an external challenge.
3
Analyze the thamarah al-khilaf
Determine the practical consequence: those who say wajib do not require repetition of individual prayer; sin is incurred for habitual abandonment. The mufta bihi (sunnah muakkadah) means leaving it is not sinful per se, but habitual neglect is blameworthy.
The text states 'the one who says it is obligatory does not make it a condition for validity, so it is valid even if prayed alone.'
4
Examine the definition of jama'ah
Understand what constitutes a valid congregation in Hanafi fiqh: the imam plus at least one follower, who can be a man, woman, free person, slave, discerning child, angel, or jinn, in a mosque or elsewhere.
The linguistic definition is 'a gathering group'; legal definition includes even non-human followers.
5
Explore the ruling on tadā'ī
Note that gathering for supererogatory prayers (other than Tarawih and witr of Ramadan) is disliked if done with tadā'ī (inciting competition). However, if three or fewer follow the imam, it is not tadā'ī and not disliked.
This is a refinement of the ruling to avoid ostentation.

باب الإمامة قدمنا شيئاً يدل على فضل الأذان وعندنا (هي) أي الإمامة (أفضل من الأذان) لمواظبته والخلفاء الراشدين عليها، والأفضل كون الإمام هو المؤذن وهذا مذهبنا وكان عليه أبو حنيفة رحمه الله (والصلاة بالجماعة (سنة) في الأصح مؤكدة شبيهة بالواجب في أفاده الزيلعي قوله : (القوم والحفظة الأولى حذفه ليعم كل مصل، والله سبحانه وتعالى أعلم، وأستغفر الله العظيم. أعناقاً. هي إتباع الإمام في جزء من صلاته أي أن يتبع فالإتباع مصدر الفعل المبني للمفعول، والإمام هو المتبوع قوله : قدمنا شيئاً يدل على فضل (الأذان منه أن المؤذنين أطول الناس يوم القيامة. قوله : (والصلاة بالجماعة سنة) المراد بها فيما عدا الجمعة، والعيدين فإنها فيهما شرط الجواز. قوله : (سنة في الأصح) وفي البدائع عامة المشايخ على الوجوب، وبه جزم في التحفة، وغيرها، وفي جامع الفقه أعدل الأقوال وأقواها الوجوب، ومنهم من قال : إنها فرض كفاية، وبه قال الكرخي والطحاوي وجماعة من أصحابنا، وقيل: إنها فرض عين وهو قول الإمام أحمد كذا في الشرح والقائل بالفرضية لا يشترطها للصحة، فتصح ولو منفرداً كما في شرح ابن وهبان والجماعة في اللغة الفرقة المجتمعة، وشرعاً، الإمام مع واحد سواء كان رجلاً أو امرأة حراً، أو عبداً، أو صبياً يعقل، أو ملكاً أو جنياً في مسجد، أو غيره، وفي القنية : الأصح أن إقامتها في البيت كإقامتها في المسجد، وإن تفاوتت الفضيلة، وعلى القول بأنها سنة ، أكد هي عين إلا في التراويح فإنها فيها سنة كفاية، ووتر رمضان فإنها فيه مستحبة، وأما وتر غيره، وتطوّعه فمكروهة فيهما على سبيل التداعي . سنة الفجر، وهي . من سنة قال شمس الأئمة الحلواني : : إن اقتدى به ثلاثة لا يكون تداعياً فلا يكره إتفاقاً، وإن اقتدى به أربعة فالأصح الكراهة، وتستحب في الكسوف كما في الدرّ من بابه، وتكره في الخسوف بحر، وفي النهر، والدر اختلف في لحوق الإثم بالترك مرة بدون عذر فمن قال بالوجوب، وهم العراقيون قالوا نعم ومن قال بالسنية وهم الخراسانيون، قالوا : إنما يأثم إذا اعتاد الترك، وحكى المؤلف في شرح الوهبانية عن جوامع الفقه أنها مستحبة، فالأقوال خمسة العلماء إتفقوا على أن فضل الجماعة يحصل بإدراك جزء من صلاة الإمام، ولو آخر وجمهور
Chapter of Imamate. We have already presented something indicating the virtue of the adhan. With us, it (i.e., imamah) is better than the adhan, due to the Prophet's constancy upon it and the Rightly Guided Caliphs. The best is that the imam be the mu'adhdhin, and this is our madhhab, and Abu Hanifa (may Allah have mercy on him) was upon this. His words: 'the people and the guardian angels, the first is omitted to include every praying person, and Allah knows best. I seek forgiveness from Allah the Great.' Necks. It is following the imam in a part of his prayer, i.e., that he follows. Following is a gerund of the passive verb, and the imam is the one followed. His words: 'And congregational prayer is sunnah' means by that other than Jumu'ah and the two Eids, for in them it is a condition of validity. His words: 'sunnah in the most correct view.' In al-Bada'i, the general mashayikh are upon wajib, and he was firm in al-Tuhfah and others. In Jami' al-Fiqh, the most balanced and strongest opinion is wajib. Among them are those who say it is fard kifayah, and this is the view of al-Karkhi, al-Tahawi, and a group of our companions. And it was said it is fard 'ayn, which is the view of Imam Ahmad, as in the commentary. The one who says it is obligatory does not make it a condition for validity, so it is valid even if prayed alone, as in Sharh Ibn Wahban. 'Al-jama'ah' linguistically means a gathering group, and legally, the imam with one person, whether man or woman, free or slave, discerning child, angel, or jinn, in a mosque or elsewhere. In al-Qunyah: the most correct is that its performance at home is like its performance in the mosque, although virtue differs. On the view that it is sunnah, it is emphasized, except in Tarawih, for it is sunnah kifayah, and the witr of Ramadan is recommended. As for other witr and supererogatory prayers, it is disliked in them on the basis of tadā'ī. The sunnah of Fajr and it is from sunnah. Shams al-A'imma al-Halwani said: If three follow him, it is not tadā'ī, so it is not disliked by agreement. If four follow him, the most correct is dislike. It is recommended in solar eclipse as in al-Durr from its chapter, and disliked in lunar eclipse. In al-Bahr, al-Nahr, and al-Durr, they differed about the sin for leaving it once without excuse. Those who say it is obligatory, and they are the Iraqis, say yes; those who say it is sunnah, and they are the Khurasanis, say that he only sins if he habitually leaves. The author narrated in Sharh al-Wahbaniyyah from Jami' al-Fiqh that it is recommended. So the opinions are five. The scholars agreed that the virtue of congregation is attained by catching a part of the imam's prayer, even the last part, and the majority.
Source pages p. 286

Commentary
This passage is a super-commentary opening the chapter on imamate (leading prayer). It first establishes that imamah (leading prayer) is superior to adhan (the call to prayer) because the Prophet and the caliphs consistently performed it. The preferred practice is that the imam also gives the adhan. The main subject is the ruling on congregational prayer. The text presents a spectrum of five opinions within the Hanafi school: 1) it is wajib (obligatory) – the view of many early Mashayikh and considered strongest in Jami' al-Fiqh; 2) it is fard kifayah (collective obligation) – held by al-Karkhi, al-Tahawi, and others; 3) it is fard 'ayn (individual obligation) – attributed to Imam Ahmad (outside Hanafi school); 4) it is sunnah mu'akkadah (emphasized sunnah) – the most correct view according to the text; 5) it is mustahabb (recommended) – mentioned in some later works. The author notes that even those who consider it obligatory do not make it a condition for validity; a prayer performed individually is still valid. The text defines jama'ah legally as the imam with at least one follower, including women, children, jinn, etc. It also discusses the issue of tadā'ī (inciting competition) in supererogatory prayers, where gathering in congregation is disliked for non-emphasized sunan. The virtue of congregation is attained by catching any part of the imam's prayer, even the final sitting.

Key Terms
الإمامة (al-imamah): The act of leading others in prayer; also used for the position of the imam.
صلاة الجماعة (salat al-jama'ah): Prayer performed in congregation, with an imam and at least one follower.
تداعي (tadā'ī): The act of calling others to join in a congregational prayer for supererogatory acts, which is disliked when it leads to showing off or competition.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the most correct view in the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on performing the five daily prayers in congregation?
A) Fard 'ayn
B) Sunnah muakkadah
C) Makruh
D) Mubah

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school's mufta bihi is that congregational prayer for the five daily prayers is sunnah muakkadah, but leaving it habitually without excuse is sinful, and individual prayer remains valid.

The Ruling and Virtue of Congregational Prayer: A Hanafi Internal Dispute
Explaining the virtue of imamate and the legal status of congregational prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the five Hanafi opinions on the ruling of congregational prayer and identify the mufta bihi among them.

Core Idea
Congregational prayer is either sunnah or wajib — the Hanafi school has an internal disagreement that affects sin, not validity.

This passage from Hashiya al-Tahtawi opens the chapter on Imamate, establishing the virtue of imamate and the legal status of congregational prayer. While the base text states it is a confirmed sunnah, the commentator immediately reports that the majority of Hanafi mashayikh consider it wajib. Understanding this internal ikhtilaf is essential because it influences the conditions under which one incurs sin for abandoning it.

Guided Path
1
Identify the base ruling from the matn
Read the base text statement: 'Congregational prayer is sunnah in the most correct view.' Note that it is classified as sunnah muakkadah, resembling wajib in strength.
The matn is the primary authority, but the hashiah immediately qualifies it.
2
Recognize the multiple views reported in the hashiah
The commentator lists several opinions: the majority of mashayikh say wajib; some say fard kifayah (Karkhi, Tahawi); some say fard 'ayn (Ahmad); and even a view of mere recommendation (mustahabb) from Jami' al-Fiqh. Note the geographical division: Iraqis (wajib) vs. Khurasanis (sunnah).
This shows the richness of Hanafi ijtihad and the need for tarjih.
3
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf (practical difference)
The practical consequence: those who say wajib hold that abandoning it once without excuse is sinful; those who say sunnah hold that sin only attaches if one habitually abandons it. However, all agree the individual prayer is valid.
This difference affects fatwa and religious practice.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب الإمامة
قدمنا شيئاً يدل على فضل الأذان وعندنا (هي) أي الإمامة (أفضل من الأذان) لمواظبته والخلفاء الراشدين عليها، والأفضل كون الإمام هو المؤذن وهذا مذهبنا وكان عليه أبو حنيفة رحمه الله (والصلاة بالجماعة (سنة) في الأصح مؤكدة شبيهة بالواجب في القوة (للرجال) للمواظبة ولقوله صلى الله عليه وسلم : صلاة الجماعة أفضل من صلاة أحدكم وحده بخمسة وعشرين جزأه وفي رواية درجة فلا يسع تركها إلا بعذر ولو تركها أهل مصر بلا عذر يؤمرون بها فإن قبلوا وإلا قوتلوا عليها لأنها من شعائر الإسلام ومن خصائص هذا الدين ويحصل فضل الجماعة بواحد ولو صبياً يعقل أو امرأة ولو في البيت مع الإمام، وأما الجمعة فيشترط ثلاثة أو اثنان كما سنذكره (بلا عذر) لأنها تسقط به وشروط صحة الإمامة للرجال الأصحاء ستة أشياء الإسلام) وهو شرط عام فلا تصح إمامة منكر البعث أو خلافة الصديق أو صحبته أو بسبب الشيخين أو بنكر الشفاعة أو ذلك نحو ممن يظهر الإسلام مع ظهور صفته المكفرة له (والبلوغ) لأن صلاة القعدة الأخيرة قبل السلام واختلفوا هل الأفضل مسجد حيه أم جماعة المسجد الجامع وإن استوى المسجدان فأقدمهما أفضل فإن استويا فأقربهما فإن استويا خير العامي، والفقيه يذهب إلى أقلهما جماعة ليكثر واو التلميذ يذهب إلى مجلس أستاذه نهر
قوله : (والصلاة بالجماعة سنة) المراد بها فيما عدا الجمعة، والعيدين فإنها فيهما شرط الجواز. قوله : (سنة في الأصح) وفي البدائع عامة المشايخ على الوجوب، وبه جزم في التحفة، وغيرها، وفي جامع الفقه أعدل الأقوال وأقواها الوجوب، ومنهم من قال : إنها فرض كفاية، وبه قال الكرخي والطحاوي وجماعة من أصحابنا، وقيل: إنها فرض عين وهو قول الإمام أحمد كذا في الشرح والقائل بالفرضية لا يشترطها للصحة، فتصح ولو منفرداً كما في شرح ابن وهبان والجماعة في اللغة الفرقة المجتمعة، وشرعاً، الإمام مع واحد سواء كان رجلاً أو امرأة حراً، أو عبداً، أو صبياً يعقل، أو ملكاً أو جنياً في مسجد، أو غيره، وفي القنية : الأصح أن إقامتها في البيت كإقامتها في المسجد، وإن تفاوتت الفضيلة، وعلى القول بأنها سنة مؤكدة هي عين إلا في التراويح فإنها فيها سنة كفاية، ووتر رمضان فإنها فيه مستحبة، وأما وتر غيره، وتطوّعه فمكروهة فيهما على سبيل التداعي .
قال شمس الأئمة الحلواني : : إن اقتدى به ثلاثة لا يكون تداعياً فلا يكره إتفاقاً، وإن اقتدى به أربعة فالأصح الكراهة، وتستحب في الكسوف كما في الدرّ من بابه، وتكره في الخسوف بحر، وفي النهر، والدر اختلف في لحوق الإثم بالترك مرة بدون عذر فمن قال بالوجوب، وهم العراقيون قالوا نعم ومن قال بالسنية وهم الخراسانيون، قالوا : إنما يأثم إذا اعتاد الترك، وحكى المؤلف في شرح الوهبانية عن جوامع الفقه أنها مستحبة، فالأقوال خمسة العلماء إتفقوا على أن فضل الجماعة يحصل بإدراك جزء من صلاة الإمام، ولو آخر
ومشروعيتها قيام نظام الألفة بين المصلين، والتعلم من العالم أفاده في تركها إلا بعذر المفعول محذوف تقديره المكلف، وسيأتي للمصنف بيان الأعذار في فصل مستقل. قوله : (أهل مصر) بالتنوين لأنّ المراد أهل أي مصر كان. قوله : (ولو صبياً) يفهم منه أن فضيلة الجماعة تحصل بالمتنفل المقتدي. قوله: (أو امرأة) حتى لو صلى في بيته بزوجته أو جاريته، أو ولده فقد أتى بفضيلة الجماعة اهـ كذا في الشرح، ولكن فضيلة المسجد أتم. قوله : (مع الإمام لا حاجة إليه لعلمه من الكلام السابق. قوله: (فيشترط ثلاثة الأولى زيادة لها قوله : (أو إثنان) أي غير الإمام، وأو لحكاية الخلاف، والمعتمد. الأول.
Chapter of Imamate. We have previously presented something indicating the virtue of the adhan. With us, imamate is better than the adhan due to the constant practice of the Prophet and the Rightly Guided Caliphs. It is preferable that the imam be the mu'adhdhin; this is our school and Abu Hanifa (may Allah have mercy on him) was upon it. Congregational prayer is a confirmed sunnah, resembling an obligation in strength (for men), due to constant practice and the Prophet's saying: 'The prayer of a man in congregation is superior to his prayer alone by twenty-five parts (or degrees in another narration).' It is not permissible to abandon it without an excuse. If the people of a city abandon it without excuse, they are commanded to perform it; if they accept, otherwise they are fought for it because it is among the symbols of Islam and the characteristics of this religion. The virtue of congregation is attained with one person even if a discerning child or a woman, even if in the house with the imam. As for Friday, three or two are required as we will mention. Without excuse, because it is dropped by it. The conditions for the validity of imamate for healthy men are six: Islam (which is a general condition — the imamate of one who denies the resurrection, the caliphate of al-Siddiq, his companionship, or curses the two shaykhs, or denies intercession, or similar matters, from one who outwardly shows Islam while his characteristic that makes him an unbeliever is apparent is not valid), and puberty (because...). The last sitting before the salam. And they differed: is the mosque of his neighborhood or the congregational mosque of the city better? If the two mosques are equal, the one with older standing is better. If they are equal, the nearer. If they are equal, the common person chooses, while the jurist goes to the one with fewer congregation to increase the number. The pupil goes to the gathering of his teacher. Al-Nahr said: His saying: 'Congregational prayer is sunnah' means other than Friday and the two Eids, for in those it is a condition of validity. His saying: 'sunnah in the most correct view' — in al-Bada'i, the majority of the mashayikh are upon obligation, and it is affirmed in al-Tuhfa and others. In Jami' al-Fiqh, the most balanced and strongest opinion is obligation. Some said it is a communal obligation, which is the view of al-Karkhi, al-Tahawi, and a group of our companions. It was said it is a personal obligation, which is the view of Imam Ahmad, as in al-Sharh. Those who say it is obligatory do not make it a condition for validity, so it is valid even individually, as in Sharh Ibn Wahban. Linguistically, congregation is a gathered group; legally, it is the imam with one person, whether man, woman, free, slave, discerning child, angel, or jinn, in a mosque or elsewhere. In al-Qunyah: the most correct is that its performance at home is like its performance in the mosque, though the virtue differs. On the view that it is a confirmed sunnah, it is the very sunnah except in tarawih, where it is a communal sunnah, and in witr of Ramadan, where it is recommended. As for witr of other nights and supererogatory prayers, it is disliked in them if done by mutual invitation. Shams al-A'imma al-Halwani said: If three follow him, it is not mutual invitation, so it is not disliked by agreement. If four follow him, the most correct is dislike. It is recommended in solar eclipse as in al-Durr from its chapter, and disliked in lunar eclipse. In al-Bahr and al-Durr, they differed on whether sin follows from abandoning it once without excuse. Those who say it is obligatory, and they are the Iraqis, said yes. Those who say it is sunnah, and they are the Khurasanis, said only if one habitually abandons it. The author in Sharh al-Wahbaniyyah narrated from Jami' al-Fiqh that it is recommended, so there are five opinions. Scholars agree that the virtue of congregation is attained by grasping a part of the imam's prayer, even if the last. Its wisdom is that it establishes a system of affection among the worshippers and learning from the scholar. He said: Abandoning it except with an excuse — the object is omitted, estimated as 'the obligated person.' The author will explain the excuses in a separate chapter. His saying: 'people of a city' with tanwin because it means people of any city. His saying: 'even a child' implies that the virtue of congregation is attained by someone praying supererogatorily following [the imam]. His saying 'or a woman' — even if he prays at home with his wife, slave-girl, or child, he has attained the virtue of congregation, as in al-Sharh, but the virtue of the mosque is more complete. His saying 'with the imam' — there is no need for it as it is understood from the previous speech. His saying: 'three are required' — the first [opinion] adds [the requirement of three]. His saying 'or two' meaning besides the imam, and 'or' indicates narration of disagreement, and the relied-upon is the first.
Source pages p. 286

Commentary
This passage opens the chapter on Imamate from Hashiya al-Tahtawi on Maraqi al-Falah. The author first establishes that imamate (leading prayer) is superior to the adhan (call to prayer) due to the consistent practice of the Prophet and the Rightly Guided Caliphs. It is also preferable that the same person serve as both mu'adhdhin and imam, which was the practice of Abu Hanifa. The central discussion is the legal ruling of congregational prayer. The base text states it is a confirmed sunnah resembling an obligation, supported by the hadith about its superiority and the fact that it cannot be abandoned without excuse. The commentator then reports multiple views within the Hanafi school: the majority of mashayikh consider it obligatory (wajib), some say it is fard kifayah (communal obligation) — a view held by al-Karkhi and al-Tahawi — and a view attributed to Imam Ahmad says it is fard 'ayn (personal obligation). The text notes that even those who make it obligatory do not require it for the validity of the prayer itself (the individual prayer is still valid). The definition of 'congregation' is clarified: it is the imam with one follower, regardless of gender, free/slave, child, angel, or jinn. The virtue is attained even if one joins at the very end. The passage also touches on issues like praying at home vs. mosque, tarawih, witr, eclipse prayers, and the conditions for imamate, of which only the first two (Islam and puberty) are listed before the window ends. The multiple opinions show the range of Hanafi thought on this matter.

Key Terms
الإمامة (al-imāmah): Leadership in prayer, meaning the imam being followed by others in parts of the prayer.
الجماعة (al-jamā‘ah): Legally: the imam with one or more followers, regardless of gender or status.
سنة مؤكدة (sunnah mu’akkadah): A confirmed recommended act, in this context resembling wajib in strength, but not obligatory.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling of congregational prayer according to the majority of the mashayikh (senior scholars) as reported in the text?
A) Sunnah muakkadah
B) Wajib
C) Fard kifayah
D) Mustahabb

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school has a spectrum of rulings on congregational prayer, but all agree the individual prayer is valid; the mufta bihi leans toward wajib.

The Obligation of Congregational Prayer in the Hanafi School
Explaining the virtue of jama'ah and its obligatory nature

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on congregational prayer for men without excuse, identify the primary proof (dalil) and its legal implication (wujub), and contrast it with the Shafi'i position.

Core Idea
Congregational prayer is wajib for men — leaving it without excuse invites fighting.

In this passage from Hashiya al-Tahtawi, we explore the ruling on salat al-jama'ah (congregational prayer). The text cites the well-known hadith that jama'ah is superior to individual prayer by 25 parts, but it goes further: it declares that leaving jama'ah without a valid excuse is not permissible, and if an entire city abandons it, they are to be fought. This strong language establishes wujub (obligation) in the Hanafi school, not mere recommendation. We will dissect the proof and understand why this ruling differs from other madhhabs.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and Its Ruling
What specific act is being discussed? What is the hukm (legal status) according to the Hanafi school? Look for direct statements like 'la yasi'u tarkuha' (it is not permissible to leave it).
The act is salat al-jama'ah for men. The ruling is wajib.
2
Locate the Dalil (Proof)
Find the primary textual evidence cited. The text mentions the hadith of 25 parts and the threat of fighting. Identify the type of dalil: is it Quran, Sunnah, Ijma, or Qiyas?
Sunnah ahad (hadith of 25 parts) and the concept of sha'a'ir al-Islam.
3
Trace the Wajh al-Dalalah (Legal Indication)
How does the dalil prove wujub? The text says 'la yasi'u tarkuha' and 'yuqatalu' (they are fought). In Hanafi usul, fighting is only prescribed for abandoning a wajib, not a sunnah. Connect the threat to the level of obligation.
The threat of fighting elevates the ruling from sunnah to wajib.
4
Note the Ikhtilaf (Scholarly Disagreement)
Identify which school disagrees and their position. The text implies Shafi'is consider it sunnah mu'akkadah. Understand the practical difference: in the Hanafi school, omitting it without excuse is sinful; in the Shafi'i school, it is a loss of reward but not sinful.
This ikhtilaf arises from differing weight given to the same hadith.
5
Determine the Mufta Bihi (Operative Ruling)
Which view is relied upon for fatwa? The text's strong language and al-Tahtawi's affirmation indicate that the relied-upon Hanafi position is wujub. Note any intra-Hanafi differences (some later scholars said sunnah).
The mufta bihi is wajib, as per zahir al-riwayah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
القوة (للرجال) للمواظبة ولقوله صلى الله عليه وسلم : صلاة الجماعة أفضل من صلاة أحدكم وحده بخمسة وعشرين جزأه وفي رواية درجة فلا يسع تركها إلا بعذر ولو تركها أهل مصر بلا عذر يؤمرون بها فإن قبلوا وإلا قوتلوا عليها لأنها من شعائر الإسلام ومن خصائص هذا الدين ويحصل فضل الجماعة بواحد ولو صبياً يعقل أو امرأة ولو في البيت مع الإمام، وأما الجمعة فيشترط ثلاثة أو اثنان كما سنذكره الأحرار) لأن العبد مشغول بخدمة المولى (بلا عذر) لأنها تسقط به واختلفوا هل الأفضل مسجد حيه أم جماعة المسجد الجامع وإن استوى المسجدان فأقدمهما أفضل فإن استويا فأقربهما فإن استويا خير العامي، والفقيه يذهب إلى أقلهما جماعة ليكثر واو التلميذ يذهب إلى مجلس أستاذه نهر قوله : (ولقوله صلى الله عليه وسلم صلاة الجماعة الخ) وورد أنه إذا توضأ فأحسن الوضوء، ثم خرج إلى المسجد لا يخرجه إلا الصلاة لم يخط خطوة إلا رفعت له بها درجة وحطت عنه بها خطيئة فإذا صلى لم تزل الملائكة تصلي عليه ما دام في مصلاه اللهم صل عليه اللهم ارحمه ولا يزال في صلاة ما إنتظر الصلاة، وورد أن من صلى العشاء والصبح في جماعة فكأنما قام الليل كله، وورد صلاة الرجل مع الرجل أزكى من صلاته ،وحده، ومع الرجلين أزكى من رجل واحد، وما زاد فهو أحب إلى الله تعالى وفي المضمرات مكتوب في التوراة صفة أمة محمد وجماعتهم، وأنه بكل رجل في صفوفهم يزاد في صلاتهم صلاة يعني إذا كانوا ألف رجل يكتب لكل رجل ألف ومن مشروعيتها قيام نظام الألفة بين المصلين، والتعلم من العالم أفاده في تركها إلا بعذر المفعول محذوف تقديره المكلف، وسيأتي للمصنف بيان الأعذار في فصل مستقل. قوله : (أهل مصر) بالتنوين لأنّ المراد أهل أي مصر كان. قوله : (ولو صبياً) يفهم منه أن فضيلة الجماعة تحصل بالمتنفل المقتدي. قوله: (أو امرأة) حتى لو صلى في بيته بزوجته أو جاريته، أو ولده فقد أتى بفضيلة الجماعة اهـ كذا في الشرح، ولكن فضيلة المسجد أتم. قوله : (مع الإمام لا حاجة إليه لعلمه من الكلام السابق. قوله: (فيشترط ثلاثة الأولى زيادة لها قوله : (أو إثنان) أي غير الإمام، وأو لحكاية الخلاف، والمعتمد. الأول.
The strength (for men) for perseverance and because the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'Congregational prayer is better than the prayer of one of you alone by twenty-five parts' and in a narration 'degrees'. So it is not permissible to leave it except with an excuse. If the people of a city leave it without an excuse, they are commanded to do it; if they accept, otherwise they are fought over it because it is among the symbols of Islam and from the characteristics of this religion. And the virtue of congregation is obtained with one [follower], even if it is a reasonable child or a woman, even if in the house with the imam. As for Jumu'ah, three or two are required as we will mention. The free [men] because the slave is busy serving the master, (without excuse) because it falls with it. And they differed: which is better, the mosque of his neighborhood or the congregational mosque of the central mosque? If the two mosques are equal, then the older one is better; if equal, then the nearer; if equal, the common person chooses. The jurist goes to the one with fewer congregations to increase... (then continues with hadith).
Source pages p. 287

Commentary
This passage from Hashiya al-Tahtawi explains the ruling and virtue of congregational prayer (salat al-jama'ah). It begins by citing the well-known hadith that congregational prayer is superior by 25 parts (or degrees), establishing its high merit. The text then states that it is not permissible to leave it without a valid excuse, and if an entire city abandons it without excuse, they are commanded to perform it; if they refuse, they are fought. This indicates that jama'ah is considered wajib (obligatory) in the Hanafi school, not merely sunnah, because fighting is prescribed for leaving a wajib act. The reward of congregation is attained even with one follower, be it a child who understands the prayer or a woman, and even if the prayer is performed at home with the imam. Then the passage discusses the conditions for Jumu'ah (Friday prayer), requiring three or two followers, and the preference of mosques. The commentary adds several hadith: the rewards of going to the mosque, angels praying for the one who remains in the mosque, and that praying 'Isha and Fajr in congregation is like standing the whole night. It also notes that the virtue of congregation is obtained even if the follower is performing a nafl (supererogatory) prayer, and that praying at home with family also gives the virtue, though the mosque is more complete. The text clarifies that the word 'people of a city' (ahl misr) is indefinite, meaning any city, and that the reward is for each person in the row, with an example of 1000 men each receiving the reward of 1000 prayers.

Key Terms
صلاة الجماعة (salat al-jama'ah): Prayer performed in congregation with at least one follower behind an imam
شعائر الإسلام (sha'a'ir al-Islam): Distinctive rituals/symbols of Islam that manifest the religion publicly
أهل مصر (ahl misr): People of a city; indefinite meaning any city

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Sunnah mu'akkadah
B) Wajib
C) Fard 'ayn
D) Mubah

Key Takeaway
Congregational prayer (salat al-jama'ah) is wajib for free adult males who are able, based on the hadith of 25 parts and the threat of fighting for its abandonment.

Six Conditions for a Valid Imam in Salah
Enumerating and explaining the six conditions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the six conditions for the validity of imamah in Hanafi fiqh and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute on the minimum recitation required.

Core Idea
An imam must meet six conditions; the most debated is whether one verse suffices for recitation.

In this passage, the author of Maraqi al-Falah enumerates the six conditions that make an imam qualified to lead prayer. While some conditions are universally agreed upon, the Hanafi school has an internal difference on the number of verses the imam must be able to recite. This lesson walks you through each condition and its legal basis.

Guided Path
1
Identify the six conditions
List them in order: Islam, puberty, sanity, masculinity, ability to recite a verse, and freedom from excuses. Note that each is a condition for the imamah to be valid for healthy adult males.
2
Understand the proof for each condition
For each condition, trace the reasoning: e.g., Islam is necessary because the prayer of a non-Muslim is invalid; puberty because a child's prayer is not obligatory; sanity because the insane cannot validly pray; masculinity because a woman cannot lead men; recitation because salah requires Quran; and freedom from excuses because the excused person's prayer is considered deficient.
3
Analyze the intra-Hanafi dispute on recitation
Abu Hanifa holds that one short verse suffices; Abu Yusuf and Muhammad require at least three verses. Understand the argument: Abu Hanifa relies on the general command to recite, while the Sahibayn compare to the minimum required in salah.
4
Note the ruling on following a child or an excused person
An adult cannot follow a child in any prayer, fard or nafl, because the child's prayer is not binding. Similarly, an excused person (e.g., with incontinence) may only lead others with the same excuse.
5
Recognize the special case of the khuntha
A hermaphrodite is treated as female for imamah: cannot be followed by a male or another khuntha, but can be followed by a woman. This is due to the default assumption of femaleness.

نفلاً غير مضمون، وثمرته الإنتقاض بالقهقهة كذا في التنوير
His saying: (for men) As for women, not all conditions are required, rather masculinity is excluded from them, for a woman's imamah for her like is valid. His saying: (the healthy) excludes those with excuses, for their imamah is valid for their likes. His saying: (and it is a general condition) so there is no need to mention it. His saying: (or one who insults the two shaykhs) it is better to say: or one who insults or abuses. His saying: (or the like of that) like one who denies the Isra', or vision, or punishment of the grave... (then fragmented). The child's prayer is nafl and his nafl is not binding. (And sanity) because his prayer is valid without it? (al-sakran) (and masculinity) excludes the woman due to the command to delay them, and the khuntha is a woman, so only her like may follow her. (And recitation) by memorizing a verse by which prayer is valid, with a difference. (And) the sixth, freedom from (excuses) for the excused person's prayer is necessary... (then continues with details).
Source pages p. 287

Commentary
This passage details the six conditions required for the validity of the imamah for healthy men in congregational prayer. The first condition is Islam: the imam must be a Muslim. One who denies essential beliefs such as resurrection, the caliphate of Abu Bakr, or the Prophet's intercession is not valid. However, if someone denies the vision of Allah but says 'He is not seen due to His majesty', his imamah may be valid according to some. The second condition is puberty (bulugh): an adult cannot follow a child in prayer, even in nafl, because a child's prayer is nafl and not binding, whereas the follower's nafl is binding, leading to a building of the strong (adult) upon the weak (child). Some scholars from Balkh allowed it in tarawih, but the relied-upon position is that it is invalid. The third condition is sanity ('aql): a drunk or chronically insane person cannot lead. A person with intermittent insanity may lead when sane. The fourth condition is masculinity (dhukurah): women cannot lead men; a khuntha (hermaphrodite) is considered female in this ruling, so neither men nor another khuntha may follow him/her, but women may follow. The fifth condition is ability to recite at least one verse: Abu Hanifa said one short verse suffices; Abu Yusuf and Muhammad require three short verses. The sixth condition is freedom from excuses that prevent perfect prayer (e.g., chronic illness, incontinence); such excused persons may only lead others with the same excuse. The text also discusses consequences if the iqtida' (following) becomes invalid: if the invalidity is due to a missing condition, the prayer does not start; if due to a difference in the type of prayer (e.g., follower's prayer different from imam's), it becomes a nafl prayer that is not guaranteed (ghayr madmun).

Key Terms
البلوغ (al-bulugh): The condition of puberty; a child's prayer is considered nafl and not valid for following in fard
الخنثى (al-khuntha): A hermaphrodite; in this context, treated as female for the purpose of leading prayer, so cannot be followed by a male or another khuntha

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, can an adult follow a child in fard prayer?
A) Yes, if the child is discerning
B) No, not in fard
C) Yes, in all prayers
D) No, not even in nafl

Key Takeaway
The six conditions ensure the imam's prayer is regular and binding; the most nuanced is the ability to recite, with a legitimate intra-Hanafi difference on the minimum quantity.

Inherent Conditions for the Imam: Adulthood, Sanity, Masculinity, and Recitation
Listing the first four conditions for valid imamate

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the four inherent conditions for the imam (bulugh, aql, dhukura, qira'a) and explain the Hanafi reasoning behind each, including the intra-madhhab difference on the number of verses required.

Core Idea
An imam must be adult, sane, male, and able to recite at least one verse — these are indispensable for valid imamate.

This passage from al-Tahtawi's Hashiya refines the conditions that an imam must satisfy. The first four conditions relate to the imam's own capacity: he must have reached puberty, be of sound mind, be male, and be able to recite a minimum amount of the Qur'an. Each condition is derived from the broader principles of prayer validity and the social order of congregational prayer.

Guided Path
1
Identify the condition of adulthood
The author states that a child's prayer is nafl and not binding. Why can't a child lead an adult? Because the stronger cannot build on the weaker.
2
Identify the condition of sanity
Prayer without sanity is invalid, so a drunkard or madman cannot lead.
3
Identify the condition of masculinity
Women are commanded to pray behind men; a hermaphrodite is classed as a woman for imamate, so only women may follow.
4
Identify the condition of recitation ability
The imam must memorize at least one verse that makes prayer valid. There is an ikhtilaf: Abu Hanifa says one verse suffices, while Abu Yusuf and Muhammad require three short verses.
The mufta bihi is that one verse suffices.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الصبي نقل ونفله لا يلزمه (والعقل) لعدم صحة صلاته بعدمه كالسكران (والذكورة) خرج به المرأة للأمر بتأخيرهن والخنثى امرأة فلا يقتدي به غيرها والقراءة) بحفظ آية تصح بها الصلاة على الخلاف (و) السادس السلامة) من (الأعذار فإن المعذور صلاته ضرورية فلا يصح إقتداء غيره به كالرعاف) الدائم وانفلات الريح) ولا يصح إقتداء من به بمن به سلس بول لأنه ذو عذرين (والفأفأة) بتكرار الفاء (والتمتمة) بتكرار التاء فلا يتكلم إلا به واللثغ) بالتاء المثلثة والتحريك وهو واللثغة بضم اللام وسكون الثاء تحرك اللسان من السين إلى الثاء ومن الراء إلى الغين ونحوه لا يكون إماماً لغيره وإذا لم يجد في القرآن شيئاً خالياً. الشغة وعجز عن إصلاح لسانه آناء الليل وأطراف النهار فصلاته جائزة لنفسه وإذا ترك التصحيح والجهد فصلاته فاسدة (و) السلامة من فقد شرط كطهارة) فإن عدمها بحمل خبث لا يعفى لا تصح إمامته الطاهر (و) كذا حكم (ستر) عورة) لأن العاري لا يكون إماماً
The child's prayer is nafl and his supererogatory prayer is not binding upon him. And (mental capacity) because his prayer is not valid without it, like the drunkard. And (masculinity) by it the woman is excluded due to the command to delay them, and the hermaphrodite is a woman in ruling, so none other than her may follow her. And (recitation) by memorizing a verse by which prayer is valid, according to the difference of opinion. And (the sixth) freedom from (excuses), for the excused person's prayer is necessary, so no one else may follow him, like continuous nosebleed and the passing of wind. And the following of one with urinary incontinence by another with the same is not valid, because he has two excuses. And (al-fa'fa'ah) repeating the letter fa, and (al-tamtamah) repeating the letter ta, so he does not speak except with that, and (al-luthgh) with the dotted tha and with vowel movement, and al-luthgha with damm on lam and sukun on tha, a movement of the tongue from sin to tha and from ra to ghayn and the like, he cannot be an imam for others. And if he does not find in the Quran anything free from that defect and is unable to correct his tongue by night and day, his prayer is permissible for himself, but if he abandons correction and effort, his prayer is invalid. And (freedom from) lacking a condition like purity, for if it is absent due to carrying an impure substance that is not excused, his leading the pure person is not valid. And likewise the ruling (covering) of the private parts, because the naked cannot be an imam.
Source pages p. 288

Commentary
This passage from the Hashiya of al-Tahtawi on Maraqi al-Falah refines the conditions for the imam in congregational prayer. The commentator, following the sharh's order, lists the conditions required for the imam's validity: First, adulthood (bulugh): a child's prayer is nafl and not binding, so an adult cannot follow a child because the stronger is built on the weaker. Second, sanity (aql): prayer is invalid without it, like a drunkard or chronic madman. Third, masculinity (dhukura) with certainty: women are excluded due to the command to delay them behind men; a hermaphrodite is treated as a woman, so only women can follow a hermaphrodite. Fourth, ability to recite: one must memorize at least a verse that makes prayer valid; there is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf between Abu Hanifa (one verse suffices) and the Sahibayn (three short verses). Fifth, freedom from excuses: an excused person (like one with chronic nosebleed or incontinence) cannot lead healthy persons because his prayer is deemed necessary (daruri) and incomplete. Also, someone with speech defects (fa'fa'ah, tamtamah, luthghah – lisping) cannot lead others unless he is unable to correct it after effort, in which case his own prayer is valid but not as imam except for someone with the same defect. Sixth, freedom from missing a condition like purity (from hadath or najas) or covering the private parts: an impure or naked person cannot lead. The commentator notes refinements: the imamate of a child is generally invalid, though some scholars from Balkh said it is valid for tarawih; the relied position is no validity without exception. For the hermaphrodite, the author's absolute statement is refined because a woman can follow a hermaphrodite. For the excused, one with the same excuse can follow, but not one with a different excuse. The passage concludes with the ruling that if the imamate is invalid due to lack of a condition, the prayer does not become the follower's own solitary prayer because he intended congregation, per the relied view, unless the defect is due to difference in type of prayer, in which case it becomes a non-binding supererogatory prayer.

Key Terms
الخنثى (al-khuntha): A hermaphrodite with both male and female reproductive organs; in ruling, considered a woman for imamate.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the minimum recitation required for an imam according to the relied position?
A) Al-Fatihah
B) One verse
C) Three verses
D) A complete surah

Key Takeaway
The imam must be adult, sane, male, and able to recite at least one verse for the congregation's prayer to be valid.

Conditions for the Imam: Freedom from Excuses, Speech Defects, Purity, and Covering
Listing the final conditions for valid imamate: freedom from excuses, speech defects, impurity, and nudity

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the conditions of freedom from chronic excuses, speech defects, impurity, and uncovering, and apply the rules for who may follow such an imam.

Core Idea
An imam with a chronic excuse or speech defect can only lead those with the same defect; an impure or uncovered imam cannot lead at all.

This part of the passage covers the remaining conditions for the imam: he must be free from chronic excuses that affect the validity of his prayer, from speech defects that distort recitation, and from missing the conditions of purity and covering. These rulings ensure that the imam's prayer is as complete as possible, so that the follower's prayer is not built on deficiency.

Guided Path
1
Identify the condition of freedom from chronic excuses
The excused person's prayer is considered 'necessary' (daruri) and lacks full validity, so he cannot lead the healthy.
Examples: constant nosebleed, incontinence of wind or urine.
2
Understand the rule for excused persons leading each other
One with urinary incontinence cannot lead another with the same, because that would involve two excuses (the imam's and the follower's).
The text says 'because he has two excuses' implying it is worse.
3
Identify speech defects (fa'fa'ah, tamtamah, luthgh)
These defects make recitation incorrect; such a person cannot lead others unless they have the same defect and he cannot correct it after effort.
If he abandons effort, his own prayer becomes invalid.
4
Apply the ruling on purity
If the imam lacks purity due to carrying an inexcusable impurity, his imamate is invalid for the pure.
5
Apply the ruling on covering the private parts
A naked person cannot be imam.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

Commentary
This passage from the Hashiya of al-Tahtawi on Maraqi al-Falah refines the conditions for the imam in congregational prayer. The commentator, following the sharh's order, lists the conditions required for the imam's validity: First, adulthood (bulugh): a child's prayer is nafl and not binding, so an adult cannot follow a child because the stronger is built on the weaker. Key Terms
اللثغ (al-luthgh): A speech defect that changes letters, like sin to tha or ra to ghayn; such a person cannot be imam unless defective like himself.
المعذور (al-ma'dhur): One with a chronic excuse like constant nosebleed or incontinence; his prayer is valid but cannot lead healthy persons.
الفأفأة (al-fa'fa'ah): Repeating the letter fa when speaking.
التمتمة (al-tamtamah): Repeating the letter ta when speaking.

D) No one

Key Takeaway
An imam must be free from chronic excuses, speech defects, impurity, and nudity; otherwise, his imamate is invalid, and even others with the same defect cannot follow him.

Conditions for Valid Iqtida (Following an Imam)
Conditions for valid iqtida in congregational prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the four key conditions for valid iqtida and identify which condition is violated in a given scenario.

Core Idea
Four conditions make iqtida valid: intention, imam's intent for women, heel precedence, and no disparity in obligation level.

This lesson explains the essential conditions for following an imam in prayer as outlined by al-Tahtawi. The Hanafi school stipulates these conditions to ensure the unity and validity of congregational prayer. Understanding them prevents common errors that could invalidate the follower's prayer.

Guided Path
1
List the conditions mentioned
Read the passage and identify each condition. There are four conditions explicitly given: intention of the follower, intention of the imam for women, precedence of the imam's heel, and the imam not being in a lower state.
The passage mentions 'fourteen things approximately' but only four are detailed.
2
Understand the intention requirement
The follower's intention must be concurrent with the takbir, either real (simultaneous) or virtual (no foreign act between). The passage states that the follower intends both the prayer and the following.
Virtual concurrency means no distracting act occurred.
3
Analyze the women-following condition
If women follow a male imam, the imam must intend to lead them. Without this intention, the prayer is invalid due to the risk of improper alignment (muhadhat).
This condition applies even in Jumu'ah and 'Eid prayers according to the majority.
4
Examine positioning and obligation level
The imam must be ahead by the heel; mere finger precedence due to long foot does not harm. Also, the imam's prayer should not be of a lower obligation than the follower's (e.g., nafl behind fard).
Some require the imam to be ahead, but the relied-upon view is that equality suffices.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وشروط صحة الاقتداء أربعة عشر شيئاً تقريباً (نية المقتدي المتابعة مقارنة لتحريمته أما مقارنة حقيقية، أو حكمية كما تقدم فينوي الصلاة، والمتابعة أيضاً (ونية الرجل الإمامة شرط لصحة اقتداء النساء به) لما يلزم من الفساد بالمحاذاة، ومسئلتها مشهورة ولو في الجمعة والعيدين على ما قاله الأكثر (وتقدم الإمام بعقبه عن) عقب (المأموم) حتى لو تقدم أصابعه لطول قدمه لا يضر (وأن لا يكون الإمام (أدنى حالاً من المأموم كافتراضه
And the conditions for the validity of following are approximately fourteen things: the follower's intention of following concurrent with his takbir – either real or virtual – so he intends the prayer and also the following; and the man's intention of imamah is a condition for the validity of women's following him due to what necessitates corruption by alignment, and its case is well-known even in Jumu'ah and the two 'Ids according to what the majority said; and the imam's precedence with his heel over the heel of the follower so that even if his fingers precede due to the length of his foot it does not harm; and that the imam not be in a lower state than the follower, like his being a supererogatory prayer while the follower is obligatory.
Source pages p. 290

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement enumerating the conditions for valid iqtida (following an imam). It lists: (1) the follower's intention to follow the imam, concurrent with his own takbir; this can be real (simultaneous) or virtual (no foreign act between). (2) The imam must intend to lead if women follow him, to avoid corruption due to positioning. (3) The imam must be ahead in the position of the heel; finger position due to long foot doesn't matter. (4) The imam's state should not be lower than the follower's, e.g., if the imam is praying a nafl and the follower is praying a fard. The commentary expands on these: for intention, it discusses that just the intention of following suffices; for women, the imam must intend imamah to make the women's prayer valid; for positioning, the correct view is equality (not ahead). The passage also notes that the conditions are about fourteen in number.

Key Terms
الاقتداء (al-iqtida'): The follower's attachment of his prayer to the imam's prayer.
نية المتابعة (niyyat al-mutaba'ah): Intention of following the imam, concurrent with one's own takbir.
المحاذاة (al-muhadhat): Alignment of the woman with the imam, which would corrupt the prayer if not intended.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling if a woman follows a man in prayer without the man intending to lead her?
A) Her prayer is valid but disliked.
B) Her prayer is invalid due to the possibility of corruption by alignment.
C) His prayer is invalid.
D) Both prayers are valid if they stand correctly.

Key Takeaway
Four conditions – intention, imam's intent for women, heel equality, and obligation equivalence – ensure valid iqtida.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
12 min
Conditions for Valid Iqtida' in Prayer
Lists conditions for valid iqtida'

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list and explain the key conditions for valid iqtida' (following the imam) in Hanafi prayer law and distinguish between mufta bihi positions and intra-madhhab differences.

Core Idea
The Hanafi conditions for iqtida' ensure the follower's prayer is legally bound to the imam's — intention, spatial alignment, and unity of prayer are essential.

This passage from Hashiya al-Tahtawi enumerates approximately fourteen conditions for the validity of following an imam in prayer. Al-Tahtawi not only lists these conditions but also refines certain positions, noting where the author's strict view departs from the relied-upon Hanafi madhhab. The conditions cover the follower's and imam's intention, spatial relations, and the identity of the prayer being offered.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is iqtida' (following the imam). Its conditions are necessary for validity; omission of any condition renders the follower's prayer invalid.
Iqtida' is not a separate prayer but a mode of performing prayer in congregation.
2
Enumerate the key conditions from the passage
List the conditions: intention of the follower (mutaba'a) concurrent with takbir, imam's intention to lead women, spatial advancement/alignment, imam not in a lower state (impurity), unity of prayer type and day, unity of time (resident leading traveler after time), imam not a masbuq, and no foreign separator.
The passage lists 'approximately fourteen' but only some are explicitly detailed.
3
Distinguish mufta bihi from disputed points
On advancement, the mufta bihi is alignment (equality) not strict ahead. On intention of imamah for women in Friday/Eid, there is disagreement; the relied-upon view requires it.
Al-Tahtawi explicitly says the author's view on advancement is contrary to the madhhab.
4
Analyze the rationale behind the conditions
Each condition ensures that the follower's prayer is genuinely linked to the imam's: intention creates the link, spatial alignment prevents corruption, unity of prayer ensures the imam's act is the same as the follower's obligation.
The condition of imam not being in a lower state preserves the dignity of the congregation.
5
Apply to a hypothetical case
Consider a man who follows an imam praying Asr while the follower intends Zuhr. The condition of unity of prayer is violated; the follower's prayer is invalid.
This shows the practical impact of the conditions.
