For a covered person. (And conditions for validity of iqtida' are approximately fourteen things: intention of the follower for followership concurrent with his takbir, either real or virtual as previously, so he intends the prayer and also the followership. And intention of the man for imamah is a condition for validity of women following him, due to the corruption that would result from alignment, and its issue is well-known, even in Friday and the two Eids according to what most said. And that the imam be ahead by his heel from the heel of the follower, so that if his fingers are ahead due to the length of his foot, it does not harm. And that the imam not be in a lower state than the follower, such as his fard not being pardoned if it exceeds a dirham's amount or reaches a quarter of the garment. He said: 'His imamah for a pure person is not valid.' Its apparent meaning is even if the impure person does not find an eliminator, or finds it but a hindrance occurs like uncovering of the private parts. And the apparent restriction is that iqtida' of a carrier of a preventing impurity to him is valid. He said: 'For a covered person.' And his imamah for one like him is valid. He said: 'And conditions of validity of iqtida' (which is in language absolute adherence as in al-Qamus, and in sharia is binding a person's prayer to the prayer of the imam). He said: 'Intention of the follower for followership' such as intending with him the commencement in his prayer, or iqtida' with him in it. Even if he only intends iqtida' with him, the correct view is that it suffices, and it refers to the imam's prayer even if the follower has no knowledge of it because he made himself a follower of the imam, contrary to those who say the follower needs three intentions: intention of the original prayer, intention of specification, and intention of iqtida', as informed by al-Sayyid. And intention of followership is a condition in other than Friday and Eid according to the chosen view, because they are specific to congregation, so they do not need intention of iqtida'. Likewise in al-Qahistani and Saka al-Anhar. As for intention of imamah, it is not a condition except in the case of women. And the follower is not required to specify the imam; rather it is better not to, because if he specifies him and it turns out otherwise, his prayer becomes invalid. He said: 'Or virtual' by there being no foreign separator between them, as in the commentary. He said: 'So he intends the prayer and also the followership' this branching is not good on its predecessor, and you have known that the intention of iqtida' only is valid, even if he has no knowledge of the specific prayer of the imam. He said: 'Due to the corruption that would result from alignment' i.e., for him or for a similar follower, and corruption does not occur without his commitment, which is by his intention. And the woman does not enter into the imam's prayer unless he intends her imamah, and the hermaphrodite is like the female, and there is no difference between one and multiple. He said: 'According to what most said.' And in al-Nahr from al-Khulasah, a preference for non-requirement in them. He said: 'And they agreed on non-requirement for them in the funeral prayer,' as informed by al-Sayyid. And in the speech there is indication that the imam is male; as for a female imam, what was mentioned does not apply. He said: 'Even if his fingers are ahead' i.e., of the follower with his heel behind the imam's heel due to the length of his foot, i.e., of the follower, it does not harm. Know that what the author stated of requiring advancement is contrary to the madhhab, because if he aligns, iqtida' is valid. And the consideration in the one who gestures is the head, so if his head is behind the imam's head and his feet ahead of his feet, it is valid, and vice versa is not valid, as in al-Zahidi. And in al-Durr: 'A single person stands aligned i.e., equal to the right of his imam according to the madhhab. As for a single woman, she must be behind, and there is no consideration of the head, but of the foot, even if a child, in the correct view, as long as he is not ahead by more than a foot.' And that the imam not pray a fard other than his fard, i.e., the follower's fard, like Zuhr and Asr and two Zuhrs from two days, for participation, and it requires unity, so iqtida' of a person who made a vow to another who made a vow not vowing the specific vow of the imam is invalid due to his lack of authority over others in what he has undertaken, nor of the person who made a vow to the person who swore, because the vowed prayer is stronger. And that the imam not be a resident for a traveller after the time in a four-rakat prayer, due to what we have previously, so it would be iqtida' of one obligated by one performing supererogatory with respect to the sitting or recitation. And that he not be a masbuq (latecomer) due to the problematic nature of his iqtida'. And that there be no separation between the imam and the follower that would invalidate. He said: 'And that the imam not be in a lower state than the follower' is not from that which applies if someone who considers witr obligatory follows someone who considers it sunnah, for that is valid due to unity and does not differ by difference of belief. Likewise, someone praying a sunnah behind someone praying another sunnah, like sunnah of Isha behind someone praying Tarawih, or sunnah of Zuhr after behind someone praying the before, is permissible, as in al-Bahr and others. And in al-Zahiriyyah: 'He prayed two raka'ah of Asr and the sun set, so a person followed him in the remaining two—it is permissible, even though it is qada for the follower, because the prayer is one,' as in al-Shalabi from al-Zaylai, and al-Qahistani also transmitted it. He said: 'For participation' i.e., because the follower is a participant with the imam, so unity is necessary so that the imam's prayer encompasses the follower's prayer, from the commentary summarized. He said: 'So iqtida' of a vow-maker is invalid' as a branch on the previous, so there is no unity in their two vows. He said: 'If he did not vow the specific vow of the imam'; but if he vowed it by saying 'I vow to pray the two raka'ah that so-and-so vowed,' then it is valid due to unity, as informed by al-Sayyid. He said: 'Due to his lack of authority etc.' is the reason for 'so it is invalid', and the pronoun is for the vow-maker, meaning that obligation only appears with respect to the vow-maker, not to others, so if he follows another in other than his vow, it is iqtida' of a person obligated by a person performing supererogatory, as informed in the commentary. And if he gave the reason that difference of vows is like difference of obligatory prayers, it would be more apparent. He said: 'Nor the vow-maker with the person who swore' the person who swore says, for example, 'By Allah, I will pray such-and-such,' and the opposite is like the person who swore with the person who swore, as in the commentary. He said: 'Because the vowed prayer is stronger' due to being obligatory in itself; as for the one sworn upon, it is a nafilah that is permissible to do or leave, one of its two aspects is strengthened by the oath, so its obligation is for fulfillment of the oath. And do not be troubled by the invalidity of iqtida' of an obligated person to a supererogatory performer by the replacement imam who came after the bowing and followed him in the two prostrations, for the two prostrations are nafilah for the successor and fard for the one who caught the bowing with the imam, because what is prohibited is iqtida' of an obligated person to a supererogatory performer in all actions, not in some, as informed by al-Sayyid. But there is a consideration in it because of what will come in the issue of iqtida' of a traveller after the time to a resident, for the corruption there only comes from considering some of the prayer as supererogatory, i.e., the sitting or recitation. He said: 'After the time' i.e., the iqtida' occurred after the time; as for if the iqtida' occurred during the time, then the time passed while they are in prayer, the iqtida' is valid and he is obligated to complete. And if the resident imam made takbir during the time and the traveller followed after it expired, it is not valid. He said: 'In a four-rakat prayer' as for two-rakat and three-rakat, they do not change in travel or residence. He said: 'Due to what we have previously' that it is required that he not be in a lower state than the follower. He said: 'With respect to the sitting' if he follows him in the first pair, because it is fard on the follower since his fard is two raka'ah, not on the imam. And what the author means by 'supererogatory performer' is general.
Source pages p. 290

Commentary
This passage from Hashiya Al-Tahtawi discusses the conditions for the validity of following an imam (iqtida') in prayer. The author begins by listing approximately fourteen conditions, though not all are fully enumerated here. The first condition is the intention of the follower (muqtadi) to follow the imam simultaneously with his own takbirat al-ihram. This intention can be real (simultaneous in time) or virtual (without a foreign separator). The follower must intend both the prayer itself and the act of following. The second condition is that a male imam must explicitly intend to lead women; otherwise, the women's following is invalid due to the issue of alignment (muhadha). This is required even in Friday and Eid prayers according to most scholars, though there is a view preferring non-requirement. The third condition is that the imam must be ahead by his heel relative to the follower's heel. If the follower's foot is long and his toes are ahead but his heel is behind, it is acceptable. However, the text notes that the relied-upon position is that alignment (equality) is permissible; the consideration is the head for a standing person and the foot for a seated one. The fourth condition is that the imam should not be in a lower state than the follower, meaning, for example, if the imam's clothing has an impurity that exceeds what is excusable, his imamah for a pure person is invalid. The fifth condition is that the imam and follower must be performing the same type of obligatory prayer (e.g., both Zuhr) and from the same day; if they are on different days or different prayers, it is invalid. This is required for participation (musharaka). The sixth condition is that a resident imam cannot lead a traveller follower in a four-rakat prayer when the prayer is performed after its time, because the traveller's prayer becomes shortened, so the follower would be following a supererogatory imam in some actions. For two-rakat and three-rakat prayers, this does not apply. The seventh condition is that the imam should not be a masbuq (one who joined late) because of the problematic nature of his iqtida'. Finally, there must be no foreign separator between imam and follower that would invalidate the prayer. The passage also discusses related issues, such as the validity of following an imam whose belief differs regarding the obligation of witr, or following one sunnah prayer behind another sunnah, and the case of a person who made a vow following another vow-maker or a person who swore an oath.

Key Terms
الإقتداء (al-iqtida'): Following the imam in prayer: legally binding one's prayer to the prayer of the imam.
المتابعة (al-mutaba'a): The act of following the imam, intended by the follower at the beginning of prayer.
نية الإمامة (niyyat al-imamah): The imam's intention to lead specifically women.
المحاذاة (al-muhadha): Alignment of the follower's heel with the imam's heel (or standing position).
المشاركة (al-musharaka): Participation: the follower is a participant with the imam in the same prayer, requiring unity of prayer type.
المسبوق (al-masbuq): One who joins the prayer late, having missed part of it with the imam.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is a condition for the validity of a woman following a male imam?
A) The woman must stand to the right of the imam
B) The imam must intend to lead women
C) The woman must be behind the imam by at least one foot
D) The woman must be in the same row as the men

Key Takeaway
The conditions for valid iqtida' in Hanafi prayer include intention, spatial alignment, and unity of prayer, with the mufta bihi allowing alignment over strict advancement.

Conditions for the Imam Not Being Inferior to the Follower: Unity of Prayer in Congregational Prayer
Explaining the requirement that the imam and follower share the same prayer type

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the condition that the imam's prayer must be of the same type and obligation as the follower's, and apply it to identify valid and invalid imam-follower pairings in the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
The follower's prayer is invalid unless the imam's prayer is identical in type and obligation.

In the Hanafi school, the validity of following an imam in congregational prayer hinges on a fundamental condition: the imam's prayer must be exactly the same as the follower's in terms of being obligatory or supererogatory, and in the specific prayer (e.g., Zuhr behind Zuhr). This lesson unpacks this condition through various cases discussed by the commentator, including vowed prayers, oaths, traveler vs. resident, and the masbuq. Understanding this condition is crucial for ensuring the correctness of your congregational prayer.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core condition
The passage begins by stating that the imam should not be performing an obligatory prayer different from the follower's. This is the basis for all subsequent rulings.
The condition is called 'ittihad' (unity).
2
Distinguish valid and invalid vow-based prayers
Analyze the case of two nadhirs (vowers): if they vow different prayers, following is invalid. If the follower vows exactly the imam's vow, it is valid.
The reason given is that the nadhir has no authority over others in his vow.
3
Compare nadhir and halif
A nadhir cannot follow a halif because the vowed prayer is stronger (obligatory by intent) while the sworn prayer is only obligatory to fulfill the oath.
Illustrates the principle that the imam's prayer must be at least as strong as the follower's.
4
Handle traveler and resident after time
A traveler following a resident after the designated time in a four-rakat prayer is invalid because the resident's prayer becomes partly supererogatory for the traveler.
The invalidity arises from the imam being in a 'lower state' regarding part of the prayer.
5
Clarify the masbuq and lahiq
A masbuq (latecomer) is not considered in a lower state, but a lahiq (one who missed due to a barrier) is not allowed to be an imam.
The passage also mentions that differences in belief (e.g., regarding witr) do not affect unity.

And he transmits: The imam should not be performing an obligatory prayer other than the follower's obligatory prayer, like Zuhr and Asr or two Zuhr prayers from two different days, because of partnership, and partnership requires unity. So it is not valid for a nadhir (vower) to follow another nadhir if he did not vow the same vow as the imam, because he has no authority over others in what he undertook. Nor may a nadhir follow one who swore an oath, because the vowed prayer is stronger. And the imam should not be a resident for a traveler after the time in a four-rakat prayer, as we mentioned earlier, so it would be a follower of an obligatory prayer following one performing a supererogatory prayer regarding the sitting or the recitation. And the imam should not be a masbuq (latecomer) due to the ambiguity of his following. He said: ('And that the imam should not be in a lower state than the follower) is not applicable if someone who considers witr obligatory follows someone who considers it sunnah, for that is valid because of unity and does not differ with differing belief. Likewise, one praying a sunnah prayer follows one praying another sunnah, like sunnah of Isha behind one praying tarawih, or sunnah of Zuhr after behind one praying before, it is permissible, as in al-Bahr and others. And in al-Zahiriyya: He prayed two rakats of Asr and the sun set, then a person followed him in the last two, it is permissible, even though this is a make-up for the follower, because the prayer is one, as in al-Shalabi from al-Zayla'i, and al-Qahistani also transmitted it. He said: (for partnership) meaning that the follower is a partner of the imam, so unity is necessary so that the imam's prayer includes the follower's prayer, summarized from the sharh. He said: (so it is not valid for a nadhir to follow a nadhir) is a branch of what preceded, so there is no unity in their two vows. He said: if he did not vow the specific vow of the imam. But if he vowed it, by saying 'I vow to pray the two rakats that so-and-so vowed,' then it is valid because of unity, as stated by al-Sayyid. He said: (because he has no authority over others) is the cause for his statement 'so it is not valid', and the pronoun refers to the nadhir, meaning that obligation appears only in the right of the nadhir, not in others. So if he follows another in something other than his vow, it is a follower of an obligatory prayer following a supererogatory one, as stated in the sharh. And if he had explained it by saying that the difference of two vows is like the difference of two obligatory prayers, it would be more apparent. He said: (nor the nadhir by the halif) the halif is someone who says, for example, 'By Allah, I will pray such and such,' and the opposite is like a halif following a halif, as in the sharh. He said: (because the vowed is stronger) because its obligation is intentional, while the one sworn upon is an action that is permissible to do or leave, but one of its two aspects is strengthened by the oath, so its obligation is to fulfill the oath. And do not be confused by the validity of a follower of an obligatory prayer following a supererogatory prayer in the case of the imam appointing someone who came after the ruku' and following him in the two prostrations, for the two prostrations are supererogatory for the caliph but obligatory for the one who caught the ruku' with the imam, because the prohibition is of a follower of an obligatory prayer following a supererogatory one in all actions, not in some, as stated by al-Sayyid. And there is a consideration in this due to what will come in the issue of a traveler following a resident after the time, for the invalidity there arises from considering supererogatory in part of the prayer, namely the sitting or the recitation. He said: (after the time) meaning the following occurred after the time. But if the following occurred within the time, then they exited while in prayer, then the following is valid and completion is obligatory. And if the resident imam said the takbir within the time and the traveler followed after exiting the time, it is not valid. He said: (in a four-rakat prayer) as for two-rakat and three-rakat, they do not change in travel or residence. He said: (as we mentioned) that it is a condition that he not be in a lower state than the follower. He said: (regarding the sitting) if he followed him in the first pair, for it (sitting) is obligatory on the follower because his obligation is two rakats, not on the imam. And what the author intended by 'by a supererogatory one' is general, not the non-obligatory. He said: (or the recitation) meaning if he followed him in the second pair, then the recitation there is supererogatory for the imam if he recited in the first pair, but obligatory for the follower. And if the imam did not recite in the first, there are two narrations regarding the validity of following, and its verification will come in the prayer of the traveler, God willing. He said: (due to the ambiguity of his following) meaning the state of his ihram. And he became obligated to recite due to the ambiguity of being alone. Yes, when the two masbuqs complete, one observing the other to know the number of what he missed, there is no harm. And it is a condition that the imam is not a lahiq (one who missed some rakats without a barrier) because he is de facto behind the imam and does not recite.
Source pages p. 291

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the conditions required for the validity of following the imam in congregational prayer. The key condition discussed is that the imam should not be in a state inferior to the follower in terms of the prayer itself. This means the imam's prayer must match the follower's prayer in type (obligatory or supererogatory) and in specific prayer (e.g., Zuhr behind Zuhr). The author explains various cases: following a nadhir (one who vowed) by another nadhir is invalid unless they vowed the same thing; a nadhir cannot follow a halif (one who swore an oath) because the vowed prayer is stronger. Additionally, a traveler following a resident after the time for a four-rakat prayer is invalid because the imam's prayer becomes supererogatory in part. The commentary also discusses the masbuq (latecomer) and clarifies that differences in belief regarding witr do not invalidate following because the type remains the same. The text also touches on the issue of following in supererogatory prayers where differences are permissible. Overall, the passage emphasizes the necessity of unity (ittihad) between the imam and follower in the category and specific prayer for the following to be valid.

Key Terms
ناذر (nādhir): A person who has vowed to perform a specific prayer, making it obligatory on him by his own vow.
حالف (ḥālif): A person who has sworn an oath to perform a prayer, making it necessary for him to fulfill the oath, but the prayer itself remains a permissible act that he has sworn to do.
مسبوق (masbūq): A person who joins the congregational prayer after the imam has already started, missing one or more rakats.
اتحاد (ittiḥād): Unity of the prayer in type, time, and obligation between the imam and the follower.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Yes, because both are praying two rakats from a vow.
B) No, because the vows are different and there is no unity.
C) Yes, if they vowed the same intention.
D) No, unless the imam is also a nadhir.

Key Takeaway
For the follower's prayer to be valid, the imam's prayer must be exactly the same in type and obligation – unity (ittihad) is essential.

Barriers Between Imam and Follower: River, Road, and Women's Rows
Explaining the conditions regarding physical barriers and women's rows in congregational prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three barriers that invalidate following the imam and apply the Hanafi ruling on women's rows to determine whose prayer is invalid.

Core Idea
Three women in a row behind the imam invalidate the prayer of the three men directly behind them.

Congregational prayer requires a direct connection between the imam and follower. Certain barriers break this connection, rendering the follower's prayer invalid. This lesson examines the three barriers identified in the hadith: a river, a road, and a row of women. We'll explore the precise conditions for each barrier and how the Hanafi school resolves internal differences based on the primary texts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
The act is following the imam in congregational prayer. The ruling is that if a specified barrier exists, the follower's prayer becomes batil (invalid). Determine the three types of barriers from the hadith.
The ruling applies to male followers; similar barriers between followers also invalidate.
2
Locate the dalil
The primary proof is the hadith: 'Whoever has between him and the imam a river, a road, or a row of women, there is no prayer for him.' Identify this as a hadith ahad and note its implications.
The hadith is referenced but not fully quoted in the passage.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The explicit phrase 'there is no prayer for him' indicates the entire prayer is invalid. Analyze how each type of barrier is defined (e.g., small river vs. large river, road with carts).
The definition of 'small river' is based on whether a boat can pass.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Scholars differ on the number of women that affect the prayer (two vs. three) and the definition of a small river. Also, Abu Yusuf holds that two people on the road can form a row, while the relied-upon view requires three.
The text mentions 'قيل' (it was said) for alternative views.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The text states 'وعليه الفتوى' for the ruling on three women. For the river, the correct view distinguishes small from large based on boat passage. For the road, three people on the road form a row that removes the barrier.
Tarjih is based on the primary texts and consistency with other rulings.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (وأن لا يفصل بين الإمام والمأموم) أي الذكر، ومثله الفصل بين المأمومين كما في الحلبي . قوله: (فسدت صلاة ثلاثة خلفهن) أي وواحد عن يمينهن، وآخر عن يسارهن. قوله : (وقيل الثلاث صف) كما إذا كان الصف تاماً، وأطلق الكلام فشمل ما إذا كان بين النساء والمقتدي حائل، أولا كما يأتي في مسئلة المحاذاة إن شاء الله تعالى قوله اثنين خلفهما فقط أي ولا يتجاوز الفساد إلى ما بعد فلا ينافي فساد صلاة المحاذي عن يمينهما ويسارهما قوله : فسدت صلاة . من حاذته الخ) ولا يفسد أكثر من ذلك لأن الذي فسدت صلاته من كل جهة يكون حائلاً بينها، وبين الرجال. قوله : (في الصحيح) أي هذا القول في الفرق بين النهر الصغير والكبير هو الصحيح، وقيل الصغير ما تحصى شركاؤه وقيل ما يشبه القوي ويمنع النهر، ولو كان في المسجد كالطريق قوله: (تمر فيه العجلة والمراد أن تكون صالحة لذلك لا مرورها بالفعل في الدرر . والعجلة بالتحريك آلة يجرها الثور، والمراد بالطريق هو . النافذ ذكره السيد قوله: (وليس فيه صفوف متصلة اعلم أنه إذا إتصل المصلون، وقاموا في الطريق فإن قام واحد في عرض الطريق، وإقتدى بالإمام جاز وكره أما الجواز، فلأنه لم يبق بينه وبين الإمام طريق تمر فيه العجلة، وأما الكراهة فللصلاة في ممر الناس، فإن قام رجل خلف هذا المقتدي وراء الطريق، وإقتدى بالإمام لا يصح لأن صلاة من قام على الطريق مكروهة مع كونه غير صف فصار في حق من خلفه كالعدم، ولا يعد هذا إتصالاً، ولو كان على الطريق ثلاث جازت صلاة من خلفهم لأن الثلاث صف في بعض الروايات، وعند إتصال الصفوف لا يكون الطريق حائلاً ولو كان على الطريق إثنان فعلى قياس قول أبي يوسف تجوز صلاة من خلفهما لأنه جعل المثنى كما
He said: (And that there should not be a separation between the imam and the follower) meaning the male follower, and similar is separation between the followers, as in al-Halabi. He said: (The prayer of three [women] behind them becomes invalid) meaning one on their right, and another on their left. He said: (And it was said: three rows) as if the row is complete, and the expression is general, so it includes whether there is a screen between the women and the follower or not, as will come in the issue of alignment, God willing. He said: Two behind them only, meaning the invalidity does not extend beyond, so it does not contradict the invalidity of the prayer of the one aligned on their right and left. He said: The prayer of the one who is aligned [with them] becomes invalid, etc. And no more than that becomes invalid, because the one whose prayer is invalid from each side becomes a barrier between them and the men. He said: (in the correct) meaning this statement regarding the difference between a small and big river is the correct one, and it was said: the small one is one whose partners can be counted, and it was said: it is like the strong and prevents the river, even if in the mosque like the road. He said: (in which the cart passes) and the intent is that it is suitable for that, not that it actually passes, as in al-Durar. And 'ajala (with tashdid) is an instrument pulled by an ox, and the intent of 'road' is the thoroughfare, mentioned by al-Sayyid. He said: (And there are no continuous rows) Know that when the worshippers connect and stand in the road, then if one stands across the road and follows the imam, it is permissible but disliked. As for permissibility, because there remains no road between him and the imam in which a cart passes; as for dislike, because of praying in the path of people. Then if a man stands behind this follower across the road and follows the imam, it is invalid because the prayer of the one who stood on the road is disliked and he is not a row, so he becomes in the right of those behind him like a non-entity, and this is not considered connection. And if there are three on the road, then the prayer of those behind them is permissible because three are a row according to some narrations. And when rows are connected, the road does not act as a barrier. And if there are two on the road, then by analogy with the statement of Abu Yusuf, the prayer of those behind them is permissible, because he considered the two as [a row].
Source pages p. 291

Commentary
This passage addresses the physical barriers that invalidate following the imam in congregational prayer. The primary proof is the hadith: 'Whoever has between him and the imam a river, a road, or a row of women, there is no prayer for him.' The commentary explains the details: a river small enough for a boat to pass, a road suitable for a cart, and women's rows. For women, if there are three women in a row behind the imam, the prayer of the men directly behind them (one on each side and one behind) is invalid, but if only two women, only the two men directly behind them are affected. The commentary also discusses the definition of small river vs. big river, and the road condition. It further explains that if worshippers stand on the road and form a connection, the barrier is removed. There is a difference among Hanafi scholars: according to Abu Yusuf, two people on the road can serve as a barrier for those behind them, but the relied-upon position is that three are needed to form a row. The passage also mentions that if the rows are continuous with no gap, the road does not interrupt.

Key Terms
صف النساء (ṣaff al-nisā’): A row of women praying behind the imam, which can act as a barrier for the men behind them if there are three women in a single row.
نهر (nahr): A river or stream that divides the space between the imam and follower. The small river (one where a boat can pass) prevents validity; the large river does not.
طريق (ṭarīq): A public road suitable for carts (عجلة) to pass. If the road has continuous rows of worshippers, it does not act as a barrier.
عجلة (‘ajala): A cart or wagon pulled by an animal, used as a measure for the road: a road that can accommodate such a cart is a barrier.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If three women are standing in a row behind the imam, whose prayer becomes invalid?
A) The prayer of all men in the congregation.
B) The prayer of the three men directly behind them: one on the right, one on the left, and one behind.
C) The prayer of only the woman in the middle.
D) No one's prayer is invalid because women do not affect men's prayers.

Key Takeaway
The presence of a small river, a road without continuous worshipper rows, or a row of three women directly behind the men invalidates the follower's prayer in the Hanafi school.

Women's Rows as a Barrier in Salah
Ruling with proof from hadith

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on women's rows as a barrier in congregational prayer and apply the specific numbers to determine whose prayer is invalidated.

Core Idea
A row of women between the imam and male followers invalidates the prayer of specific men, not all, based on a prophetic hadith.

This passage from Hashiya al-Tahtawi elucidates a ruling from a prophetic hadith that lists three barriers invalidating the connection between imam and follower: a river, a road, and a row of women. The Hanafi school specifies the exact number of men whose prayer is spoiled, refining a general statement into a precise legal rule.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is performing prayer behind a row of women that lies between the imam and male followers. The ruling is that the prayer of specific men becomes fasid (invalid).
The hadith says 'la salata lahu' which the Hanafis interpret as invalidity of perfection, but here it leads to fasid.
2
Locate the dalil
The dalil is the prophetic hadith: 'Whoever has between him and the imam a river, a road, or a row of women has no prayer.'
The hadith is ahad, thus zanni al-thubut.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The explicit mention of 'saff al-nisa' (row of women) as a barrier indicates that it is an obstacle to valid prayer. The negation 'la salata lahu' implies the prayer is not valid (fasid).
The Hanafis restrict the general negation to specific men based on practice and additional reasoning.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Some Hanafis (the 'qil' opinion) hold that three rows of women spoil the prayer of all men behind them, not just three. The author rejects this and states the fatwa is on the first view.
The ikhtilaf is intra-Hanafi; the opposing opinion is considered weak.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
The author declares 'wa 'alayhi al-fatwa' (upon it is the fatwa), establishing the relied-upon position that three women spoil three men, not all.
The tarjih is based on the principle that those whose prayer is spoiled become a barrier themselves, limiting the effect.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والمأموم صف من النساء لقول النبي من كان بينه وبين الإمام نهر أو طريق أو صف النساء فلا صلاة له فإن كن ثلاثاً فسدت صلاة ثلاثة خلفهن من كل صف إلى آخر من الصفوف وعليه الفتوى وجاز اقتداء الباقي، وقيل : الثلاث صف مانع من صحة الاقتداء لمن خلف صفهن جميعاً وإن كانتا ثنتين فسدت صلاة اثنين خلفهما فقط وإن كانت واحدة في الصف محاذية فسدت صلاة من حاذته عن يمينها ويسارها وآخر خلفها. قوله : (فسدت صلاة ثلاثة خلفهن) أي وواحد عن يمينهن، وآخر عن يسارهن. قوله : (وقيل الثلاث صف) كما إذا كان الصف تاماً، وأطلق الكلام فشمل ما إذا كان بين النساء والمقتدي حائل، أولا كما يأتي في مسئلة المحاذاة إن شاء الله تعالى قوله اثنين خلفهما فقط أي ولا يتجاوز الفساد إلى ما بعد فلا ينافي فساد صلاة المحاذي عن يمينهما ويسارها قوله : فسدت صلاة . من حاذته الخ) ولا يفسد أكثر من ذلك لأن الذي فسدت صلاته من كل جهة يكون حائلاً بينها، وبين الرجال.
And the follower [is invalidated by] a row of women due to the Prophet's saying: 'Whoever has between him and the imam a river, a road, or a row of women has no prayer.' If they are three, the prayer of three behind them is spoilt from every row to the end of the rows, and upon it is the fatwa. The remainder may follow. It is said: the three rows prevent the validity of following for whoever is behind all of their rows. If they are two, the prayer of two behind them only is spoilt. If there is one woman in the row aligned, the prayer of those aligned to her right and left and the one behind her is spoilt. His statement: '(the prayer of three behind them is spoilt)' meaning one to their right and one to their left. His statement: '(it is said the three rows)' as if the row is complete, and the speech is general including whether there is a barrier between the women and the follower or not, as will come in the issue of alignment, God willing. His statement: 'two behind them only' meaning the corruption does not extend beyond that, so it does not contradict the corruption of the prayer of those aligned to their right and left. His statement: 'the prayer of those aligned to her is spoilt' and no more is spoilt because those whose prayer is spoilt from each side become a barrier between her and the men.
Source pages p. 292

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from hadith regarding women's rows as a barrier in congregation. The base text states that if a row of women exists between the imam and male followers, it invalidates the prayer of certain men. The hadith cited lists three barriers: a river, a road, and a women's row. The author then details the numbers: three women spoil the prayer of three men behind them (one directly behind and one on each side). Two women spoil only two men behind them. One woman spoils those aligned to her right and left and the one directly behind. The commentary clarifies that the corruption is limited and that those whose prayer is spoilt themselves become a barrier for men further behind. The relied-upon position (al-fatwa) is that three women spoil three men, and the alternative opinion that three rows spoil all behind is not taken. This ruling is specific to the Hanafi school and emphasizes that women are not a barrier simply by presence but by forming distinct rows that interrupt the connection.

Key Terms
صف النساء (saff al-nisa): A row of women praying individually (not necessarily in congregation) that lies between the imam and male followers.
محاذاة (muhadhat): Alignment: a woman standing directly beside a man (left or right) in the same row.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon position in this passage, how many men's prayers are spoiled if three women form a row behind the imam?
A) All men behind them from that row to the end
B) Three men: one behind the row and one on each side
C) Only the man directly behind
D) No men are spoiled if the women are visible

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school limits the effect of a women's row as a barrier to specific numbers: three women spoil three men per row, two spoil two, one spoils those aligned and the one behind.

Barriers Between Imam and Follower in Salah
Ruling on river and road as barriers with measurement and exceptions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on physical barriers (river, road, gap) that invalidate following the imam, explain the two-row measurement, and identify the exception for the same mosque.

Core Idea
A river navigable by boat or a road for carts is a barrier; a gap that fits two rows also breaks continuity.

In congregational prayer, the follower must be connected to the imam without physical gaps. But not every separation is a barrier. The Hanafi school specifies that a river passable by a small boat or a road wide enough for a cart acts as a barrier if rows are not continuous. Even an empty gap that can accommodate two rows (about a cubit or two) invalidates following. However, wide open spaces within the same mosque, its courtyard, or Eid prayer ground are considered one location and do not break connection. This lesson unpacks the textual evidence and the relied-upon measurement.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its condition
The act is following the imam in prayer. The condition is that no barrier should separate them. List the prohibited barriers: navigable river, cart-road, and any gap of two rows (mufta bihi).
The barrier is defined as a physical separation that breaks the continuity of rows.
2
Locate the dalil and its implication
The hadith specifying river and road as barriers. The Hanafi school derived the measurement (two rows) from scholarly consensus and the need to define a minimal gap that disrupts connection.
The hadith is ahad (zanni al-thubut) but accepted for practical rulings.
3
Understand the measurement of the gap
The text says a gap accommodating two rows is a barrier. The commentary explains that the gap is measured from the prostration place of one row to the standing place of the next row, about a cubit or two.
There is an alternative opinion that one row suffices, but the fatwa is on two rows.
4
Apply the exception for the same mosque
The entire mosque, its courtyard, and Eid prayer grounds are considered one location. Therefore, even large empty spaces inside do not count as barriers. This is a critical refinement.
Exception due to the ruling that the whole mosque is like one place.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأن لا يفصل بين الإمام والمأموم (نهر يمر فيه الزورق) في الصحيح والزورق نوع من السفن الصغار (ولا طريق تمر فيه العجلة) وليس فيه صفوف متصلة والمانع في الصلاة فاصل يسع فيه صفين حتى على المفتي به. قوله : يسع فيه (صفين) والفرجة بين الصفين مقدار ذراع أو ذراعين، كذا في الخانية والظاهر أنّ هذا يعتبر من محل السجود، ومحل قيام الآخرين من كل صف لأنّ الذراع لا يكفي في التحديد من محل قيام الصف إلى محل قيام الآخر. قوله : على المفتي (به وقيل : ما يسع صفاً واحداً والفضاء الواسع في المسجد لا يمنع وإن وسع صفوفاً لأن له حكم بقعة واحدة كذا في الأشباه من الفن الثاني، فلو اقتدى بالإمام في أقصى المسجد، والإمام في المحراب جاز كما في الهندية. قال البزازي : المسجد وإن كبر لا يمنع الفاصل فيه إلا في الجامع القديم بخوارزم فإن ربعه كان على أربعة آلاف اسطوانة، وجامع القدس الشريف أعنى ما يشتمل على المساجد الثلاثة الأقصى والصحراء، والبيضاء كما في الحلبي والشرح، والظاهر أنّ ذلك لإشتباه حال الإمام على المأموم لا لاختلاف المكان ومصلى العيد كالمسجد وجعل في النوازل والخلاصة والخانية مصلى الجنازة مثل المسجد أيضاً، وفناء المسجد له حكم المسجد يجوز لإقتداء فيه وإن لم تكن الصفوف متصلة.
And that there should not separate between the imam and the follower (a river through which a boat passes) in the correct view, and the boat is a type of small ship, (nor a road through which a cart passes) and there are not continuous rows in it. The barrier in prayer is a gap that accommodates two rows, until upon what is the fatwa. His statement: 'accommodates two rows' and the gap between the two rows is about a cubit or two cubits, thus in al-Khaniyya, and apparent is that this is considered from the place of prostration and the place of standing of others from each row because the cubit is not sufficient for determination from the place of standing of the row to the place of standing of the other. His statement: 'upon what is the fatwa' and it is said: what accommodates one row. The wide space in the mosque does not prevent even if it accommodates rows because it has the ruling of one location, thus in al-Ashbah from the second art. So if one follows the imam at the far end of the mosque while the imam is at the mihrab, it is permissible, as in al-Hindiya. Al-Bazzazi said: The mosque, even if large, does not prevent the separation except in the old mosque of Khwarazm, of which a quarter had four thousand pillars, and the Noble Mosque of Jerusalem, meaning that which comprises the three mosques: al-Aqsa, al-Sahra, and al-Bayda, as in al-Halabi and the Sharh. The apparent is that this is due to confusion of the state of the imam to the follower, not due to difference of place. The 'id prayer ground is like the mosque. It is made in al-Nawazil, al-Khulasa, and al-Khaniyya that the funeral prayer ground is also like the mosque. The courtyard of the mosque has the ruling of the mosque; following in it is permissible even if the rows are not continuous.
Source pages p. 292

Commentary
This is a ruling regarding physical barriers between imam and follower. The base text specifies that a river navigable by a small boat (zawraq) or a road used by carts are barriers that invalidate following unless the gap is filled by connected rows. The key measure is a gap that can accommodate two rows (about one to two cubits) is considered a barrier. The commentary clarifies that this measurement is from the place of prostration of one row to the standing place of the next. There is an alternative opinion that a gap of one row is enough. Importantly, wide open spaces within the same mosque do not count as barriers because the entire mosque is considered one place. Similarly, courtyards of mosques and 'id prayer grounds retain the same ruling. This emphasis on the mosque being one location is a distinctive Hanafi position.

Key Terms
زورق (zawraq): A small boat or skiff that can traverse a river.
العجلة (al-'ajala): A cart or carriage drawn by an animal, indicating a road wide enough for wheeled traffic.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the minimum size of a gap that acts as a barrier according to the relied-upon position?
A) A gap accommodating one row
B) A gap accommodating two rows
C) Any gap, regardless of size
D) A gap of three cubits

Key Takeaway
The barrier in congregational prayer is defined as a gap that can accommodate two rows (about a cubit), but the entire mosque, its courtyard, and Eid grounds are considered one location, so internal gaps are not barriers.

Wall as a Barrier: The Exception for Known Transitions
Ruling on wall barrier with exception for known transitions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on following an imam across a large wall and apply the exception when the imam's transitions are known by hearing or sight.

Core Idea
A large wall is not a barrier if you can see or hear the imam's movements—knowing is key.

We have learned that a large wall separating the follower from the imam normally invalidates following. However, the Hanafi school recognizes an important exception. In this lesson, we will examine this exception and the evidence behind it, so that you can apply it correctly in practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the general ruling and condition
State the default rule: a large wall that obscures knowledge of the imam's transitions is a barrier, making following invalid. Recognize that the condition is the wall's size causing uncertainty.
The size is relative; not a fixed measurement.
2
Locate the exception
Find that if knowledge of the imam's transitions is possible through hearing or sight, the wall is not a barrier and following is valid.
The exception applies even if the follower cannot reach the imam.
3
Examine the dalil
Review the hadith of the Prophet praying in 'Aisha's chamber while the people in the mosque followed him. Understand that this proves a wall does not necessarily prevent valid following.
The hadith is ahad but deemed reliable for this ruling.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi tarjih
Identify that the relied-upon view is the choice of Shams al-A'imma al-Halwani, who upheld the exception. Recognize that earlier stricter views are not operative for fatwa.
The text states 'fi al-sahih' and 'huwa ikhtiyar Shams al-A'imma'.
5
Apply to modern scenarios
Consider cases like following from an adjacent room with a loudspeaker or from a roof connected to the mosque. The principle applies as long as the follower can perceive the imam's actions.
Hearing the takbir from a muballigh also suffices.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(و) يشترط أن (لا) يفصل بينهما (حائط كبير) يشتبه معه العلم بانتقالات الإمام فإن لم يشتبه العلم بانتقالات الإمام لسماع أو رؤية) ولم يمكن الوصول إليه (صح الاقتداء) به (في الصحيح) وهو اختيار شمس الأئمة الحلواني لما روى أن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم كان يصلي في حجرة عائشة رضي الله عنها والناس في المسجد يصلون بصلاته، وعلى هذا الاقتداء في المساكن المتصلة بالمسجد الحرام وأبوابها من خارجه صحيح إذا لم يشتبه حال الإمام عليهم لسماع أو رؤية ولم يتخلل إلا الجدار كما ذكره شمس الأئمة فيمن صلى على سطح بيته المتصل بالمسجد أو في منزله بجنب المسجد وبينه وبين المسجد حائط مقتدياً بإمام في المسجد وهو يسمع التكبير من الإمام أو من المكبر تجوز صلاته كذا في التجنيس، والمزيد ويصح اقتداء الواقف على السطح بمن هو في البيت ولا يخفى عليه حاله.
And it is a condition that there should not separate between them a large wall that makes knowledge of the imam's transitions uncertain. If the knowledge of the imam's transitions is not uncertain due to hearing or sight, and it is not possible to reach him, then following him is valid in the correct view. This is the choice of Shams al-A'imma al-Halwani, because it is narrated that the Prophet (peace be upon him) used to pray in the chamber of 'Aisha (may Allah be pleased with her) while the people in the mosque prayed following his prayer. Upon this, following in houses connected to the Sacred Mosque and its doors from outside is valid if the condition of the imam is not uncertain to them due to hearing or sight, and only the wall intervenes. As Shams al-A'imma mentioned regarding one who prays on the roof of his house connected to the mosque or in his house beside the mosque, and between him and the mosque there is a wall, following an imam in the mosque while he hears the takbir from the imam or from the one who repeats (mukabbir), his prayer is permissible. Similarly in al-Tajnis and al-Mazid. And the following of one standing on the roof with one who is in the house is valid if his state is not hidden from him.
Source pages p. 293

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling on walls as barriers, with an exception. The general rule is that a large wall that obscures knowledge of the imam's movements is a barrier. However, if the follower can see or hear the imam's transitions (e.g., takbir), following is valid. This is based on the practice of the Prophet praying in 'Aisha's chamber while people in the mosque followed him. The commentary extends this to houses connected to the Sacred Mosque and even to cases where a wall exists but the follower hears the takbir from a repeater. This exception is accepted by Shams al-A'imma al-Halwani and is the relied-upon position. It indicates that the key factor is not the physical barrier per se but the ability to follow the imam's actions. The Hanafi school thus allows following across walls if communication is possible.

Key Terms
حائط كبير (ha'it kabir): A large wall that prevents knowledge of imam's movements.
انتقالات الإمام (intiqalat al-imam): The movements or transitions of the imam between postures (e.g., ruku', sujud).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Any wall is allowed if the follower is in the mosque
B) If the follower can hear the imam's takbir, it is valid
C) Only if there is a hole in the wall
D) It is never valid to pray across a wall

Key Takeaway
Following an imam across a wall is valid if you can hear or see his movements, based on the Prophet's example.

Unity of Place Between Imam and Follower
Ruling on imam riding and follower walking or riding different animal

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi condition of unity of place (ittihad al-makan) for valid following in prayer and distinguish the positions of Abu Hanifa and Imam Muhammad regarding riding on different animals.

Core Idea
Following in prayer requires unity of place; different animals break it, but close proximity may suffice by istihsan.

This lesson examines a specific condition for the validity of following an imam in congregational prayer: the unity of place. The text addresses the scenario where the imam is riding and the follower is walking or riding a different animal. According to the Hanafi school, such a difference in mounts typically indicates a difference in place, rendering the following invalid. However, Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani introduced a concession based on istihsan (juristic preference), allowing validity if the animals are brought close together. Understanding this intra-Hanafi difference sharpens your grasp of how conditions operate and how concessions can soften strict rules.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act in question is the follower's prayer behind an imam while the imam is riding a mount and the follower is walking or riding a different mount. The ruling: such following is invalid due to difference of place.
The condition is that imam and follower must share the same place; if not, following is batil.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof (dalil) is the talil (reasoning): 'li-ikhtilāf al-makān' (due to difference of place). This is not a revealed text but a rational inference from the requirement of unity in congregational prayer.
The underlying principle is that following requires physical unity; otherwise, the follower is effectively praying alone.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The wajh al-dalalah is that riding different animals causes spatial separation, which obstructs the intended unity. The condition of unity is derived from the general command to follow the imam (e.g., 'The imam is appointed to be followed').
Spatial separation is presumed unless the animals are close enough to negate it.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Imam Muhammad (al-Shaybani) differed: he used istihsan to permit the prayer if the two mounts are brought close together, even if not the same animal. His view is a leniency within the school.
Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf apparently held the stricter view requiring actual same mount or same place.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The text presents Muhammad's view as 'istahsana' but does not elevate it to mufta bihi. The predominant position (zahir al-riwayah) is the stricter one: unity of place requires same mount or at least same location. However, the istihsan concession is noted for fatwa when needed.
In practice, many later Hanafi fatwas adopt Muhammad's concession for ease, but the theoretical ruling remains conservative.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(و) يشترط أن لا يكون الإمام راكباً والمقتدي راجلاً أو بالقلب (أو راكباً) دابة غير دابة إمامه لاختلاف المكان وإذا كان على دابة إمامه صح الاقتداء لاتحاد المكان. قوله : (أو راكباً دابة غير دابة إمامه) واستحسن محمد جواز الصلاة إذا قربت دابته من دابة الإمام.
And it is a condition that the imam should not be riding while the follower is walking, or the follower riding a mount other than the imam's mount, due to difference of place. If he is on the same mount as the imam, following is valid due to unity of place. His statement: 'or riding a mount other than the imam's mount', and Muhammad deemed it good (istahsana) to permit the prayer if his mount is brought close to the imam's mount.
Source pages p. 293

Commentary
This passage states the condition that the imam and follower should share the same place (makan). If the imam is riding and the follower is walking or riding a different animal, their places are considered different, so following is invalid. However, if the follower rides the same animal as the imam, place is unified and following is valid. The commentary notes that Imam Muhammad (al-Shaybani) used istihsan (juristic preference) to permit prayer if the animals are brought close together, even if different. This reflects a leniency within the Hanafi school. The underlying rationale is unity of place, but proximity can achieve that.

Key Terms
اتحاد المكان (ittihad al-makan): Unity of place between imam and follower, essential for valid following in Hanafi school.
استحسان (istihsan): Juristic preference used by Imam Muhammad to allow following when animals are close.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In addition to the main ruling, what did Imam Muhammad (al-Shaybani) consider permissible regarding riding?
A) Following if the follower is on any animal
B) Following if the follower is walking
C) Following if the animals are close together
D) Following if the imam is on foot

Key Takeaway
The condition of unity of place is essential for valid following, but Imam Muhammad's istihsan allows leniency with close proximity between mounts.

Following the Imam from a Different Ship
Ruling on following imam from a separate unconnected ship.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the condition for valid following (iqtida') when the imam and follower are in separate ships and identify whether the ships must be connected.

Core Idea
A follower cannot validly follow an imam in a separate, unconnected ship — each ship forms its own congregation.

The Hanafi school places great emphasis on physical unity of place (ittihad al-makan) for the validity of following the imam. This lesson examines a specific application: when the imam leads salah from one ship and the follower prays in another ship. The passage establishes that if the two ships are not connected (muqtarina), the follower's prayer is invalid because each ship is considered a separate congregation. This ruling highlights the importance of spatial continuity in congregational prayer.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
The act is following an imam in salah from a different ship. The passage states that if the ships are not connected, the following is invalid (la tujuz).
The ruling is a condition of validity: the follower's salah is batil if the ships are separate.
2
Understand the analogy
The text says the two ships are 'ka al-jam'' — like two separate congregations. Each ship is an independent space, just as two mosques are separate places for prayer.
This analogy explains why physical connection is necessary.
3
Note the key term: muqtarina
Muqtarina means connected or adjacent. The ships must be physically linked (e.g., moored together, gangplank) to maintain unity of place.
If ships are only close but not connected, the condition is not met.
4
Apply the ruling to similar scenarios
If the ships are connected (e.g., tied together), following is valid. If not, the follower must either join the imam's ship or pray individually.
This condition applies to all salah, including obligatory prayers.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(و) يشترط أن لا يكون) المقتدي في سفينة والإمام في سفينة (أخرى غير مقترنة بها) لأنهما كالجمع، وعلى قياس قول محمد لا تجوز. قوله : (غير مقترنة بها) إن كالجمع.
(And it is a condition that) the follower should not be in a ship while the imam is in another ship not connected to it, because they are like two separate congregations. And on the analogy of Muhammad's statement, it is not permissible. His statement: 'not connected to it' meaning they are like separate congregations.
Source pages p. 293

Commentary
This passage adds a condition that the follower and imam should not be in separate ships that are not connected (muqtarina). If the ships are separate and not adjacent, following is invalid because each ship constitutes its own separate congregation (like two different mosques). The commentary references that on the analogy (qiyas) of Imam Muhammad's view, it is not permissible. The implication is that if the ships are close together (connected or moored side-by-side), following might be valid, similar to the ruling about riding animals being brought close. This ruling emphasizes that spatial separation across water is a barrier unless the ships are physically linked.

Key Terms
مقترنة (muqtarina): Connected or adjacent ships, allowing unity of place.
كالجمع (ka al-jam'): Like two separate congregations (jama'at), each with its own imam.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is following invalid if the follower is in a different ship not connected to the imam's ship?
A) Because water is a barrier like a river
B) Because each ship is considered a separate congregation
C) Because the ships move too much
D) Because the follower cannot hear the imam's takbir

Key Takeaway
For valid following in salah, the imam and follower must be in the same physical space; separate unconnected ships are like separate congregations.

Condition of No Large Wall Between Imam and Follower
States the condition of no large wall, with proof from hadith

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi condition regarding a wall between imam and follower and apply it to cases where knowledge of the imam's movements is possible through hearing or seeing.

Core Idea
A large wall invalidates following only if it causes confusion; if the follower can see or hear, following is valid.

This lesson examines a specific condition in congregational prayer: the presence of a large wall between imam and follower. Al-Tahtawi clarifies that the wall is a preventer only if it obscures knowledge of the imam's movements. We will explore the ruling, its proof from the sunnah, and its application to real scenarios like mosques and rooftops.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine the act being ruled upon (following the imam in prayer) and the ruling regarding the wall condition. The text states a conditional ruling: following is valid if no large wall causing confusion exists.
The condition is that the absence of a large wall is wajib for validity.
2
Locate the dalil
Find the proof cited: the hadith of the Prophet praying in Aisha's room while people in the mosque followed him. Note that this is a sunnah ahad hadith.
The hadith is used as evidence that a wall does not inherently prevent following.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
Analyze how the hadith proves the ruling. The Prophet's action shows that a physical barrier (wall) does not invalidate following if the followers can still know the imam's movements (here, presumably by seeing or hearing).
The key is that knowledge of the imam's actions is possible despite the wall.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Identify that this is a matter of ikhtilaf. Some scholars (e.g., Shafi'is) require no barrier at all, while Hanafis allow a wall if knowledge is possible. The text adopts the Hanafi position as mufta bihi.
The practical difference: Hanafis permit prayer with a wall if conditions are met; Shafi'is generally do not.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
على المفتي به (و) يشترط أن (لا) يفصل بينهما (حائط) كبير (يشتبه معه العلم بانتقالات الإمام فإن لم يشتبه العلم بانتقالات الإمام لسماع أو رؤية) ولم يمكن الوصول إليه (صح الاقتداء) به (في الصحيح) وهو اختيار شمس الأئمة الحلواني لما روى أن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم كان يصلي في حجرة عائشة رضي الله عنها والناس في المسجد يصلون بصلاته، وعلى هذا الاقتداء في المساكن المتصلة بالمسجد الحرام وأبوابها من خارجه صحيح إذا لم يشتبه حال الإمام عليهم لسماع أو رؤية ولم يتخلل إلا الجدار كما ذكره شمس الأئمة فيمن صلى على سطح بيته المتصل بالمسجد أو في منزله بجنب المسجد وبينه وبين المسجد حائط مقتدياً بإمام في المسجد وهو يسمع التكبير من الإمام أو من المكبر تجوز صلاته كذا في التجنيس، والمزيد ويصح اقتداء الواقف على السطح بمن هو في البيت ولا يخفى عليه حاله
According to the mufta bihi (position), it is conditional (that) no large wall separates them that would cause confusion about knowing the imam's movements. If knowledge of the imam's movements is not confused due to hearing or seeing, and it is not possible to reach him, then following him is valid according to the sound position. This is the choice of Shams al-A'imma al-Halwani, based on the narration that the Prophet (peace be upon him) used to pray in the room of Aisha (may Allah be pleased with her) while the people in the mosque prayed following his prayer. According to this, following in dwellings connected to the Sacred Mosque with their doors from outside is valid if the condition of the imam is not confused for them due to hearing or seeing, and nothing separates them except the wall, as mentioned by Shams al-A'imma regarding one who prays on the roof of his house connected to the mosque, or in his house adjacent to the mosque with a wall between him and the mosque, following an imam in the mosque while he hears the takbir from the imam or from the muballigh: his prayer is permissible. Similarly in al-Tajnis, and more: following of one standing on the roof of one who is in the house is valid if his condition is not hidden from him.
Source pages p. 293

Commentary
This passage from Hashiya al-Tahtawi is a statement of the ruling (hukm) regarding the condition that no large wall separate the imam from the follower. The matn (base text) stipulates that a large wall that causes confusion about knowing the imam's movements is a preventer. However, if the follower can ascertain the imam's movements through hearing or seeing, even if a wall exists, the following is valid. Shams al-A'imma al-Halwani supports this with the hadith of the Prophet praying in Aisha's room while people in the mosque followed him, indicating that a wall does not necessarily invalidate following if knowledge is possible. The author then applies this to dwellings connected to the Sacred Mosque and to rooftops, affirming validity when the imam's state is known.

Key Terms
حائط كبير (ha'it kabir): A large wall that causes confusion about knowing the imam's movements.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, what is the condition regarding a wall between imam and follower?
A) No wall is allowed whatsoever.
B) A wall is allowed if the follower can see the imam.
C) A wall is allowed only if the follower can hear the imam.
D) A wall is allowed if the follower can see or hear the imam and his movements are not confused.

Key Takeaway
Following an imam across a wall is valid in the Hanafi school as long as the follower can ascertain the imam's movements through hearing or seeing.

Unity of Place for Mounts and Boats
States conditions about mounts and boats

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the condition of unity of place (ittihad al-makan) for followers on mounts or boats and apply it to determine validity of iqtida.

Core Idea
Following is invalid if the mount or boat differs; unity of place is essential.

When the imam is mounted and the follower is on foot or on a different animal, the congregation (jama'ah) is not valid because the places are considered separate. This lesson clarifies the ruling for mounts and boats, establishing the principle that the follower must share the same physical carrier as the imam.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Prohibited Scenario
Find the scenario where the imam is riding and the follower is either on foot or riding a different animal. The text states this is invalid due to 'ikhtilaf al-makan' (difference of place).
2
Identify the Permissible Scenario
Now locate the exception: if the follower rides the same animal as the imam, the following is valid due to 'ittihad al-makan' (unity of place).
3
Apply the Analogy to Boats
The text extends the same rule to boats: if the imam and follower are in separate boats not adjoining, it is like two separate mounts and invalid. Muhammad al-Shaybani's qiyas confirms this.
The phrase 'قياس قول محمد' refers to Imam Muhammad's reasoning.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(و) يشترط أن لا يكون الإمام راكباً والمقتدي راجلاً أو بالقلب (أو راكباً) دابة (غير دابة إمامه لاختلاف المكان وإذا كان على دابة إمامه صح الاقتداء لاتحاد المكان (و) يشترط أن لا يكون) المقتدي في سفينة والإمام في سفينة (أخرى غير مقترنة بها) لأنهما كالجمع، وعلى قياس قول محمد لا تجوز قوله : يسع فيه (صفين) والفرجة بين الصفين مقدار ذراع أو ذراعين، كذا في الخانية والظاهر أنّ هذا يعتبر من محل السجود، ومحل قيام الآخرين من كل صف لأنّ الذراع لا يكفي في التحديد من محل قيام الصف إلى محل قيام الآخر. قوله : على المفتي (به وقيل : ما يسع صفاً واحداً والفضاء الواسع في المسجد لا يمنع وإن وسع صفوفاً لأن له حكم بقعة واحدة كذا في الأشباه من الفن الثاني، فلو اقتدى بالإمام في أقصى المسجد، والإمام في المحراب جاز كما في الهندية. قال البزازي : المسجد وإن كبر لا يمنع الفاصل فيه إلا في الجامع القديم بخوارزم فإن ربعه كان على أربعة آلاف اسطوانة، وجامع القدس الشريف أعنى ما يشتمل على المساجد الثلاثة الأقصى والصحراء، والبيضاء كما في الحلبي والشرح، والظاهر أنّ ذلك لإشتباه حال الإمام على المأموم لا لاختلاف المكان ومصلى العيد كالمسجد وجعل في النوازل والخلاصة والخانية مصلى الجنازة مثل المسجد أيضاً، وفناء المسجد له حكم المسجد يجوز لإقتداء فيه وإن لم تكن الصفوف متصلة. قوله : لسماع) من الإمام أو المقتدي ومثله الرؤية وفي حاشية الدرر للمؤلف الصحيح إعتبار الإشتباه فقط، وقواه في الدر بالنقل عن المعتبرات خلافاً لما في الدرر، والبحر وغيرهما من إشتراط عدم إختلاف المكان اهـ فلو إقتدى من بمنزله بمن في المسجد وإن إنفصل عنه صح لم يوجد مانع من نحو طريق ولم يشتبه حال الإمام، وأفاد السيد جواز الإقتداء في بيت بإمام فيه ولو مع وجود فاصل يسع صفين فإن البيت في هذا كالمسجد
(And) it is conditional that the imam not be riding and the follower on foot or [unclear], (or riding) an animal other than the imam's animal due to difference of place. If he is on the imam's animal, following is valid due to unity of place. (And) it is conditional that the follower not be in a boat and the imam in another boat not adjoining it, because they are like two animals. According to the analogy of Muhammad's statement, it is not permissible. His statement: 'it accommodates two rows' and the gap between the rows is the measure of a cubit or two cubits, as in al-Khaniyya. Apparently this is considered from the place of prostration and the standing place of others from each row, because a cubit is not sufficient for definition from the standing place of a row to the standing place of another. His statement: 'according to the mufta bihi' and it is said: it accommodates one row. A large open space in the mosque does not prevent even if it accommodates rows because it has the ruling of a single place, as in al-Ashbah from the second art. So if one follows the imam at the far end of the mosque while the imam is in the mihrab, it is permissible, as in al-Hindiyya. Al-Bazzazi said: The mosque, even if large, does not prevent the divider except in the ancient congregational mosque of Khwarazm, where a quarter of it had four thousand columns. And the Noble Mosque of Jerusalem, meaning what includes the three mosques: al-Aqsa, al-Sahra', and al-Bayda', as in al-Halabi and al-Sharh. Apparently that is due to confusion of the imam's state for the follower, not due to difference of place. The Eid prayer ground is like the mosque, and in al-Nawazil, al-Khulasa, and al-Khaniyya, the funeral prayer ground is also like the mosque. The courtyard of the mosque has the ruling of the mosque; following is permissible in it even if the rows are not connected. His statement: 'for hearing' from the imam or the follower, and similarly seeing. In Hashiyat al-Durar, the author [says] the correct view is to consider only confusion, and he strengthened it in al-Durr by quoting from the reliable sources, contrary to what is in al-Durar, al-Bahr, and others of stipulating no difference of place. So if one follows from his house to someone in the mosque, even though separated, it is valid if there is no preventer like a road and the imam's state is not confused. And al-Sayyid stated the permissibility of following in a house with an imam in it, even with a divider that accommodates two rows, because the house in this is like the mosque.
Source pages p. 293

Commentary
This passage from Hashiya al-Tahtawi is a commentary on multiple conditions for valid following. First, the imam and follower must not be on different mounts; if on the same mount, it is valid. Similarly, they must not be in separate boats unless the boats are connected. The commentary also discusses the condition that the space between follower and imam should accommodate at least two rows (about a cubit or two). However, a large mosque is considered one space, so distance does not prevent following if the imam's state is known. The author then addresses the condition of hearing/seeing, clarifying that the correct criterion is whether there is confusion about the imam's movements, not mere difference of place. Examples include following from a house to the mosque if no obstacle exists.

Key Terms
اتحاد المكان (ittihad al-makan): Unity of place; being on the same mount or in connected boats.
اختلاف المكان (ikhtilaf al-makan): Difference of place; the condition being on different mounts or separate boats.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When is following valid according to the Hanafi school regarding mounts?
A) When the follower is on any mount and the imam is on any mount.
B) When the follower rides the same animal as the imam.
C) When the follower is on foot and the imam is on a mount.
D) When the imam and follower are on different mounts but in the same stable.

Key Takeaway
Unity of place (ittihad al-makan) is a necessary condition for valid following; if the imam and follower are on different mounts or in separate unconnected boats, the congregation is invalid.

Space Between Rows and Ruling of Large Mosques
Explains gap between rows and ruling of large mosques

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi ruling that a large mosque is considered one place for following, even if the gap between rows is large, and distinguish exceptions like the Khwarazm mosque.

Core Idea
A large mosque is one place; large gaps between rows do not prevent following.

The text discusses the permissible gap between rows, which can be up to a cubit or two, and then expands to large mosques: even if the mosque is vast, it is considered one place (hukm baq'ah wahidah). This means a follower in the far end can validly follow the imam in the mihrab, provided there is no confusion about the imam's movements.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Permissible Gap Between Rows
The text states that the gap between rows can be the measure of a cubit (dhira') or two cubits. This is from al-Khaniyya. Note that this measurement is taken from the place of prostration to the standing place of the next row.
The cubit measurement is approximate; the key is that a gap larger than two cubits might break the connection.
2
Examine the Ruling for Large Mosques
The text then says that a large open space in the mosque (al-fida' al-wasi' fi al-masjid) does not prevent following, even if it accommodates multiple rows, because the mosque has the ruling of a single place (lahu hukm baq'ah wahidah).
This is from al-Ashbah. The example given: following from the far end of the mosque while the imam is in the mihrab is valid.
3
Note the Exception: Khwarazm Mosque
Al-Bazzazi mentions that the ancient mosque of Khwarazm had many columns, which might create a barrier. But the text clarifies that this is due to confusion about the imam's state, not difference of place.
4
Apply the Ruling to Eid and Funeral Prayers
The text extends the same ruling to the Eid prayer ground (musalla al-'id) and the funeral prayer ground (musalla al-janazah). The courtyard (fina') of the mosque also has the same ruling.
Thus, even if rows are not connected in the courtyard, following is valid.

إشتباه حال الإمام (ishtibah hal al-imam): Confusion about the imam's state; e.g., not knowing if he is praying or in which position.

10 min
The True Criterion: Confusion of State vs Difference of Place
Resolves the criterion: confusion rather than difference of place

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify that the correct Hanafi criterion for valid following across a distance is the absence of confusion about the imam's state, not merely unity of place, and apply this to cases like following from a house.

Core Idea
The decisive condition is avoiding confusion about the imam's movements, not just being in the same place.

While earlier texts emphasized unity of place, the later Hanafi scholarship (as reflected in Hashiyat al-Durar and al-Durr al-Mukhtar) establishes that the real condition is that the follower must not be confused about the imam's state (ishtibah). This lesson clarifies that even from a separate house, following can be valid if there is no obstacle and the follower can ascertain the imam's actions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Two Criteria Presented
The text mentions two criteria: (1) Some scholars (in al-Durar, al-Bahr) condition no difference of place (adam ikhtilaf al-makan). (2) The correct view (al-sahih) according to the author of Hashiyat al-Durar is to consider only confusion (i'tibar al-ishtibah faqat).
The text sides with the second view, strengthened by quotes from reliable sources.
2
Apply the Confusion Criterion to House-to-Mosque Scenario
If someone follows from his house to an imam in the mosque, even though the house is separate, it is valid if there is no road or other obstacle (mani') and the imam's state is not confused (lam yashtabih hal al-imam).
This is a relaxation of the strict unity-of-place condition.
3
Apply the Confusion Criterion to Following within a House
Al-Sayyid states that following within a house (imam in one room, follower in another) is valid even if there is a divider that accommodates two rows, because the house is like a mosque in this respect.
Again, confusion is the key, not the physical barrier.
