(And) it is conditional that the imam not be riding and the follower on foot or [unclear], (or riding) an animal other than the imam's animal due to difference of place. If he is on the imam's animal, following is valid due to unity of place. (And) it is conditional that the follower not be in a boat and the imam in another boat not adjoining it, because they are like two animals. According to the analogy of Muhammad's statement, it is not permissible. His statement: 'it accommodates two rows' and the gap between the rows is the measure of a cubit or two cubits, as in al-Khaniyya. Apparently this is considered from the place of prostration and the standing place of others from each row, because a cubit is not sufficient for definition from the standing place of a row to the standing place of another. His statement: 'according to the mufta bihi' and it is said: it accommodates one row. A large open space in the mosque does not prevent even if it accommodates rows because it has the ruling of a single place, as in al-Ashbah from the second art. So if one follows the imam at the far end of the mosque while the imam is in the mihrab, it is permissible, as in al-Hindiyya. Al-Bazzazi said: The mosque, even if large, does not prevent the divider except in the ancient congregational mosque of Khwarazm, where a quarter of it had four thousand columns. And the Noble Mosque of Jerusalem, meaning what includes the three mosques: al-Aqsa, al-Sahra', and al-Bayda', as in al-Halabi and al-Sharh. Apparently that is due to confusion of the imam's state for the follower, not due to difference of place. The Eid prayer ground is like the mosque, and in al-Nawazil, al-Khulasa, and al-Khaniyya, the funeral prayer ground is also like the mosque. The courtyard of the mosque has the ruling of the mosque; following is permissible in it even if the rows are not connected. His statement: 'for hearing' from the imam or the follower, and similarly seeing. In Hashiyat al-Durar, the author [says] the correct view is to consider only confusion, and he strengthened it in al-Durr by quoting from the reliable sources, contrary to what is in al-Durar, al-Bahr, and others of stipulating no difference of place. So if one follows from his house to someone in the mosque, even though separated, it is valid if there is no preventer like a road and the imam's state is not confused. And al-Sayyid stated the permissibility of following in a house with an imam in it, even with a divider that accommodates two rows, because the house in this is like the mosque.
Source pages p. 293

Commentary
This passage from Hashiya al-Tahtawi is a commentary on multiple conditions for valid following. First, the imam and follower must not be on different mounts; if on the same mount, it is valid. Similarly, they must not be in separate boats unless the boats are connected. The commentary also discusses the condition that the space between follower and imam should accommodate at least two rows (about a cubit or two). However, a large mosque is considered one space, so distance does not prevent following if the imam's state is known. The author then addresses the condition of hearing/seeing, clarifying that the correct criterion is whether there is confusion about the imam's movements, not mere difference of place. Examples include following from a house to the mosque if no obstacle exists.

Key Terms
إشتباه (ishtibah): Confusion; not knowing whether the imam is in a particular posture or not.
مانع (mani'): Preventer; an obstacle like a road that makes it impossible to ascertain the imam's state.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the mufta bihi view, what condition must be met for a follower to validly follow an imam from a house?
A) The house must be inside the mosque.
B) There must be no preventer like a road, and the imam's state must not be confused.
C) The houses must touch the mosque wall.
D) The follower must see the imam's face.

Key Takeaway
The correct Hanafi condition for valid following across a distance is the absence of confusion about the imam's state, not the physical unity of place.

Follower's Knowledge of Imam's Madhhab Violation
Condition for valid following regarding the imam's state

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the condition that the follower must not know the imam does something invalid in the follower's madhhab and apply the rulings based on the imam's level of precaution.

Core Idea
A follower's prayer is invalid if he knows the imam's act invalidates prayer in his own madhhab, unless compensation is possible.

This lesson examines the fourteenth condition for valid following (iqtida'): the follower must not know that the imam has done something that would invalidate the prayer according to the follower's own madhhab. The text from Hashiya al-Tahtawi outlines scenarios based on certainty, precaution levels, and an intra-Hanafi dispute. Understanding this condition helps prevent invalid prayers in congregational settings across different madhhab practices.

Guided Path
1
Identify the condition
The condition states that following is invalid if the follower knows that the imam performed an act which, according to the follower's madhhab, invalidates the prayer (e.g., flowing blood without renewed wudu).
Knowledge must be certain; mere suspicion does not invalidate.
2
Distinguish levels of certainty
If the follower is certain the imam did not compensate (e.g., did not repeat wudu), following is invalid. If uncertain, following is valid with karaha (dislike).
The text treats uncertainty as similar to complete ignorance.
3
Apply the precaution hierarchy
The imam's negligence is categorized: if he neglects pillars/conditions, following is invalid; if he neglects obligations (e.g., missing sura), following is valid with tahrimi karaha; if he neglects sunan, following is valid with tanzihi karaha and is better.
The hierarchy determines the ruling and whether following is recommended.
4
Examine the intra-madhhab dispute
The relied-upon (mufta bihi) view considers the follower's opinion; the other view considers the imam's opinion, making following valid even if the follower sees something invalid in his own madhhab.
The practical difference appears when the imam's act is invalid only in the follower's madhhab.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

The ruling is understood when he observes everything except the mustahabbat, a fortiori: following him is valid and better. In any case, following the one who agrees in case of conflict is better. His saying: (according to the imam's opinion, not the follower's, his saying: (or carrying impurity of a dirham's amount) for it is invalid according to Imam al-Shafi'i, may Allah be pleased with him, not according to us. And if he prays on the assumption that he is in a state of impurity or carrying preventing impurity, then it becomes clear otherwise, that prayer is not valid because consideration is given to what he assumed, not to the actual reality, and it is feared...
Source pages p. 293

Commentary
This passage from Hashiya al-Tahtawi covers two distinct legal issues. First, it adds a note about the mount condition: Muhammad al-Shaybani deemed following valid if the follower's mount is close to the imam's mount, and the condition of 'not adjoining' for boats is explained (like two animals; if connected, valid). Second, it discusses the fourteenth condition for valid following: the follower must not know that the imam does something that would invalidate prayer according to the follower's own madhhab. Examples include flowing blood or vomit without subsequent wudu. If the follower is certain the imam did such and did not redo wudu, following is invalid. If uncertain, it is valid with karaha. The text then elaborates on levels of precaution: if the imam does not observe the pillars and conditions, following is invalid; if he observes them but not the obligations, it is valid with tahrimi karaha; if he observes all but not the sunan, it is valid with tanzihi karaha, and following is better. It also addresses cases where the imam's act is invalid in the imam's own madhhab but not the follower's, and cases where the follower mistakenly assumes impurity then realizes otherwise.

Key Terms
الاقتداء (al-iqtida'): Following the imam in prayer by intending to pray behind him.
كراهة تحريم (karaha tahrimiyya): Prohibitively disliked; closer to haram but not definitively so.
مفسد (mufsid): Something that invalidates the prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a Hanafi follower is uncertain whether his imam (also Hanafi) performed wudu after passing wind (which invalidates wudu), but he knows the imam is generally negligent about such matters, what is the ruling for following?
A) Invalid, because the follower knows the imam is negligent.
B) Valid with karaha, because uncertainty allows for good assumption.
C) Valid without karaha, because the imam's negligence is not proven.
D) Invalid, because the imam's negligence is habitual.

Key Takeaway
The validity of following depends on whether the follower has certain knowledge of an invalidating act (in his own madhhab) without compensation; if uncertain, following is valid with karaha.

Condition 14: The Follower's Knowledge of the Imam's Invalidating Act Across Madhhabs
Critical refinement explaining the fourteenth condition for valid iqtidā' across madhhabs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the fourteenth condition for valid iqtidā' by distinguishing between the follower's knowledge, ignorance, and suspicion of an invalidating act in the imam's prayer, and evaluate the majority versus al-Hinduwani's position.

Core Idea
The follower's own madhhab and belief, not the imam's reality, determine valid following.

In congregational prayer, what happens when your imam belongs to a different madhhab and performs an act your madhhab considers invalid? This passage from al-Tahtawi's Hashiyah clarifies the fourteenth condition: the follower must not know that the imam does something that invalidates prayer according to the follower's own madhhab. It also tackles the tricky case where the imam's act invalidates his prayer in his own madhhab but he is unaware. By the end of this lesson, you will be able to navigate these scenarios and understand why the majority prioritises the follower's subjective belief.

Guided Path
1
State the condition
Identify the fourteenth condition: the follower must not know (ya'lam) that the imam performs an act that is mufsid (invalidating) in the follower's belief (za'm al-ma'mūm). This means the criterion is the follower's own madhhab, not the imam's.
The term 'za'm' emphasises the follower's subjective opinion.
2
Classify the knowledge scenarios
Break down the possible states: (a) the follower knows of an invalidator in the imam and is certain the imam did not remove it → following invalid; (b) the follower is uncertain (e.g., imam disappeared long enough to renew wudu) → following valid but makruh; (c) the follower knows the imam is negligent in disputed matters → following invalid; (d) the follower knows the imam is cautious → following valid but disliked.
Each scenario has a different ruling based on the follower's level of knowledge.
3
Identify the intra-Hanafi dispute
When the imam does an act that invalidates prayer according to the imam's own madhhab (e.g., touching a woman without barrier for a Shafi'i imam) but the imam is unaware, the majority (al-Mujtaba, al-Tabyin, Fath al-Qadir) rule following is valid. Al-Hinduwani disagrees, arguing the imam's prayer is invalid, so following is invalid.
The dispute hinges on whether we consider the imam's reality or the follower's belief.
4
Analyse the reasoning (talil)
The majority's proof: the follower considers the imam's prayer valid (because the imam is unaware and the follower's own madhhab does not deem the act invalid). The principle 'al-ibrah li-ra'y al-muqtadi' (the consideration is the follower's opinion) is applied.
This is an application of the usul maxim that subjective belief can determine validity in such cases.
5
Derive practical outcomes
Summarise the muftā bihī: if the follower does not know of an invalidator in his own madhhab, following is valid. If he knows, it is invalid. In the cross-madhhab scenario with an unaware imam, following is valid per the majority. The key takeaway: the follower's knowledge and belief govern the ruling.
This condition protects the follower from knowingly participating in an invalid prayer.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
و) الرابع عشر من شروط صحة الاقتداء (أن لا يعلم المقتدي من حال إمامه المخالف لمذهبه (مفسداً في زعم المأموم) يعني في مذهب المأموم (كخروج دم) سائل (أو قيء) يملأ الفم وتيقن أنه لم يعد بعده وضواه) حتى لو غاب بعد ما شاهد منه ذلك بقدر ما يعيد الوضوء ولم يعلم حاله فالصحيح جواز الاقتداء مع الكراهة كما لو جهل حاله بالمرة وأما إذا علم منه أنه لا يحتاط في مواضع الخلاف، فلا يصح الاقتداء به سواء علم حاله في خصوص ما يقتدي به فيه أو لا وإن علم أنه يحتاط في مواضع الخلاف يصح به على الأصح ويكره كما في المجتبى وقال الديري في شرحه : لا يكره إذا علم منه الاحتياط في مذهب الحنفي، وأما إذا علم المقتدي من الإمام ما يفسد الصلاة على زعم الإمام كمس المرأة أو الذكر أو حمل نجاسة قدر الدرهم والإمام لا يدري بذلك فإنه يجوز اقتداؤه به على قول الأكثر وقال بعضهم : لا يجوز منهم الهندواني لأن الإمام يرى بطلان هذه الصلاة فتبطل صلاة المقتدي تبعاً له وجه الأول، وهو الأصح أن المقتدي يرى جواز صلاة إمامه والمعتبر في حقه رأى نفسه فوجب القول بجوازها كما في التبيين وفتح القدير وإنما قيد بقوله : والإمام لا يدري بذلك ليكون جازماً بالنية وأمكن حمل صحة صلاته على معتقد إمامه وأما إذا علم به وهو على اعتقاد مذهبه صار كالمتلاعب ولا نية له فلا وجه لحمل صحة صلاته
And the fourteenth condition of the validity of following (is) that the follower does not know from the state of his imam who differs from his madhhab something that invalidates in the follower's belief, meaning in the follower's madhhab, like the exit of flowing blood or vomit that fills the mouth, and he is certain that he did not renew his wudu after it; even if he disappeared after witnessing that from him for the time sufficient to repeat wudu and he does not know his state, the correct view is the permissibility of following with dislike, as if he was completely ignorant of his state. And if he knows that he does not exercise caution in areas of disagreement, then following him is not valid, whether he knows his state regarding the particular act he follows him in or not. And if he knows that he exercises caution in areas of disagreement, following him is valid according to the most correct view, and it is disliked, as in al-Mujtaba. Al-Dayri said in his commentary: It is not disliked if he knows his caution in the Hanafi madhhab. And if the follower knows from the imam something that invalidates the prayer according to the imam's belief, like touching a woman or the penis or carrying an impurity the size of a dirham, and the imam is unaware of that, then his following him is permissible according to the majority. Some said it is not permissible, among them al-Hinduwani, because the imam considers this prayer invalid, so the follower's prayer becomes invalid following him. The first opinion is the most correct: the follower considers his imam's prayer valid, and the consideration for him is his own opinion, so it is necessary to say its permissibility, as in al-Tabyin and Fath al-Qadir. He restricted it by saying 'and the imam is unaware of that' so that he is resolute in intention and it is possible to interpret the validity of his prayer according to the imam's belief. If he knows it while adhering to his own madhhab, he becomes like a mocker and has no intention, so there is no way to interpret the validity of his prayer.
Source pages p. 294

Commentary
This passage is a critical refinement from al-Tahtawi's Hashiyah on the condition for valid iqtidā' (following an imam in congregational prayer) when the imam belongs to a different madhhab. The fourteenth condition is that the follower must not know that the imam performs an act that the follower's madhhab considers invalidating (mufsid) for prayer. Examples include the emission of flowing blood or vomit in the Hanafi madhhab, which invalidates wudu. If the follower witnesses such an act and is certain the imam did not renew wudu, then following becomes problematic. However, if the follower is uncertain (e.g., the imam disappeared long enough to renew wudu), the correct ruling is that following is permissible but disliked (makruh). If the follower knows that the imam is generally negligent in disputed matters, following is invalid. If the imam is known to be cautious (muhtat), following is valid but still disliked according to the relied-upon view, though al-Dayri holds it is not disliked when caution in the Hanafi madhhab is known. A second scenario arises: the follower knows the imam does something that invalidates prayer according to the imam's own madhhab (e.g., touching a woman without barrier for a Shafi'i imam), but the imam is unaware. The majority (including the author's tarjih) permit following here, because the follower considers the imam's prayer valid, and the criterion is the follower's own belief. The dissenting opinion of al-Hinduwani argues the imam's prayer is invalid in reality, so the follower's prayer follows suit, but this is rejected. The restriction 'the imam does not know' is crucial: if the imam knows and prays anyway, he is like a mocker, lacking valid intention, and his prayer is invalid, making following impossible. The commentary draws on al-Tabyin and Fath al-Qadir for the majority view.

Key Terms
الاقتداء (al-iqtidā'): Following the imam in congregational prayer by aligning one's actions with the imam's.
مفسد (mufsid): An act that invalidates the prayer according to the follower's madhhab, such as breaking wudu (blood, vomit) or touching.
زعم المأموم (za'm al-ma'mūm): The follower's belief or opinion about what invalidates prayer, based on his own madhhab.
الاحتياط (al-ihtiyāt): Exercising caution in matters of disagreement by avoiding doubtful acts that could invalidate prayer.
المتلاعب (al-mutalā'ib): One who treats prayer lightly by knowingly performing it while invalid according to his own belief, thus invalidating his intention.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, if a Hanafi follower sees his Hanafi imam emit flowing blood and is certain the imam did not renew wudu, what is the ruling on following him?
A) Valid, because the follower does not know if the imam renewed wudu.
B) Invalid, because the follower knows of an invalidating act in his own madhhab.
C) Valid but disliked.
D) Invalid, because the imam's prayer is invalid in the Hanafi madhhab.

Key Takeaway
The follower's own madhhab and belief determine the validity of iqtidā'; knowledge of an invalidator invalidates, ignorance or uncertainty permits (with possible dislike), and the imam's unawareness of his own invalidity protects the follower's prayer.

Following a Mutayammim: Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Substitution
Intra-Hanafi dispute on iqtida' with tayammum

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Abu Hanifa/Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani on this issue, explain the basis of their disagreement regarding the nature of khilafah, and identify the mufta bihi ruling.

Core Idea
A person with wudu may follow a mutayammim because the substitution is between the instruments, not the purifications.

This lesson examines a nuanced intra-Hanafi disagreement on whether a person who has performed wudu can validly follow an imam who has performed tayammum. The ruling depends on how one conceptualizes the substitution (khilāfah) that tayammum represents relative to wudu. Understanding this dispute clarifies the Hanafi approach to the relationship between primary and substitute purifications.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two opposing positions
State clearly that Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf hold the following is valid (sahih), while Muhammad al-Shaybani holds it is invalid (la yasih). Note that the passage uses 'indahumā' to indicate the majority view.
2
Understand the difference in conceptualizing khilafah
The dispute arises from two interpretations: (a) substitution between the two instruments (alatayn: turb and water) or (b) substitution between the two purifications (taharatayn: wudu and tayammum). The former makes the purifications equal, the latter makes tayammum weaker.
This is a conceptual rather than textual dispute; both sides derive from the same Quranic verse.
3
Analyze the supporting arguments
The majority (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) rely on the apparent meaning (zahir al-nass) of Quran 5:6, which indicates the substitution is between the instruments, thus achieving equality. Muhammad argues that if the substitution is between the purifications, then building the strong (wudu) on the weak (tayammum) is invalid, analogous to the case where a person with water follows a mutayammim when water is available (which is impermissible by consensus).
4
Determine the mufta bihi and its practical impact
The text indicates that the majority view (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) is the mufta bihi (relied-upon position), as it is supported by both the apparent text and the weight of authority. Practically, if a follower with wudu prays behind a mutayammim imam, the prayer is valid according to the majority, but would be invalid according to Muhammad, requiring repetition.
All agree that following a mutayammim in janazah prayer is valid, as necessity differs.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وصح اقتداء متوض بمتيمم عندهما وقال محمد : لا يصح، والخلاف مبني على أنّ الخلفية بين الآلتين التراب والماء أو الطهارتين الوضوء والتيمم فعندهما بين الآلتين وظاهر النص يدل عليه، فاستوى الطهارتان، وعند محمد بين الطهارتين التيمم والوضوء فيصير بناء القوي على الضعيف وهو لا يجوز ولا خلاف في صحة الاقتداء بالمتيمم في صلاة الجنازة
And the following of a person with wudu by a mutayammim is valid according to the two (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf), and Muhammad said: it is not valid. The dispute is based on whether the substitution is between the two instruments—turb and water—or between the two purifications—wudu and tayammum. According to the two, it is between the two instruments, and the apparent text indicates it, so the two purifications are equal. According to Muhammad, it is between the two purifications (tayammum and wudu), so building the strong on the weak occurs, and that is not permissible. There is no dispute on the validity of following the mutayammim in the janazah prayer.
Source pages p. 294

Commentary
This passage is a critical refinement presenting an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the validity of a person who has performed wudu (mutawaddi') following an imam who has performed tayammum (mutayammim) in congregational prayer. The mashhoor (relied-upon) position is that of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf (indicated by 'indahumā) that such following is valid (sahih). Muhammad al-Shaybani holds it is invalid (la yasih). The root of the ikhtilaf is the nature of the khilāfah (substitution) in tayammum: does the substitution lie between the two instruments (al-alatayn)—namely, turb (sa'id) and water—or between the two purifications (al-taharatayn)—wudu and tayammum? Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf adopt the former view, citing the apparent meaning of the Quranic verse (al-Ma'idah 5:6): '...and you find no water, then perform tayammum with clean earth.' This indicates that the substitution is between the instruments, so the two purifications are equal in rank. Muhammad al-Shaybani adopts the latter view, that the substitution is between the purifications themselves. Since wudu is the stronger purification (tahārah asliyyah) and tayammum is weaker (tahārah daruriyyah), building the strong (wudu) upon the weak (tayammum) is not valid, analogous to the case of a person with water following a mutayammim when water is available (which is impermissible by consensus). However, all agree that following a mutayammim in the janazah prayer is valid, as necessity differs. The mufta bihi is the view of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, that it is permissible.

Key Terms
خلفية (khilāfah): Substitution; the relationship by which tayammum stands in for wudu when water is unavailable.
آلتين (ālatayn): The two instruments: turb (clean earth) and water, used for purification.
طهارتين (ṭahāratayn): The two purifications: wudu (with water) and tayammum (with earth).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the majority of Hanafi imams (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf), why is a person with wudu allowed to follow a mutayammim imam?
A) Because tayammum is equal in rank to wudu in all respects.
B) Because the substitution is between the two instruments (turb and water), making the purifications equal.
C) Because necessity overrides all objections.
D) Because the imam's prayer is valid regardless of the follower's state.

Key Takeaway
A person with wudu may follow a mutayammim imam because the Hanafi majority views the substitution of tayammum as instrument-based, making its purification equal to wudu.

Following an Imam of a Different Madhhab: The Majority View and Its Conditions
Ruling on following an imam who considers the prayer invalid.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi majority position on following an imam from a different madhhab, identify the key condition (imam's ignorance), and apply the ruling to scenarios where the imam knows or does not know.

Core Idea
It is permissible to follow an imam of a different madhhab if the follower believes the prayer is valid and the imam is unaware of the difference.

This lesson examines a nuanced issue in congregational prayer: when the imam belongs to a madhhab that considers the follower’s prayer invalid (e.g., because of a difference in rulings on wudu or prayer components). The Hanafi majority ruled that such iqtida’ is valid, provided certain conditions are met. We will analyze the reasoning and the intra-Hanafi disagreement.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core issue
What is the problem? The imam holds the follower's prayer invalid, yet the follower wants to follow him.
2
State the majority position
The majority of Hanafis say it is permissible (sahih).
3
Identify the condition
The imam must not know about the follower's differing view ("لا يدري بذلك").
4
Understand the reasoning
The follower's own belief in validity is what counts; the imam's belief does not invalidate the follower's prayer.
5
Note the exception
If the imam knows and remains on his madhhab, following becomes invalid because the follower's intention is compromised.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
يدري بذلك فإنه يجوز اقتداؤه به على قول الأكثر وقال بعضهم : لا يجوز منهم الهندواني لأن الإمام يرى بطلان هذه الصلاة فتبطل صلاة المقتدي تبعاً له وجه الأول، وهو الأصح أن المقتدي يرى جواز صلاة إمامه والمعتبر في حقه رأى نفسه فوجب القول بجوازها كما في التبيين وفتح القدير وإنما قيد بقوله : والإمام لا يدري بذلك ليكون جازماً بالنية وأمكن حمل صحة صلاته على معتقد إمامه وأما إذا علم به وهو على اعتقاد مذهبه صار كالمتلاعب ولا نية له فلا وجه لحمل صحة صلاته. قوله: (وهو على إعتقاد مذهبه) أما إذا قلد مذهب المؤتم فقد اتحد معتقدهما، ولا كلام فيه قوله ولا نية له أي للمتلاعب قوله: (فلا وجه لحمل صحة صلاته الأول حذف حمل، ولو علم بفساد صلاة إمامه أما بشهادة عدول أنه أحدث، ثم صلى مثلاً وإما بإخبار منه عن نفسه ويقبل قوله إن كان عدلاً تلزمه الإعادة، وإن لم يكن عدلاً لا يقبل لكن تستحب الإعادة كما في السراج، وإذا علم مفسداً في صلاة الإمام لا يجوز له الإقتداء به إجماعاً.
He knows that, then it is permissible for him to follow him according to the majority, and some said it is not permissible, among them al-Hinduwani, because the imam considers this prayer invalid, so the prayer of the follower becomes invalid following him. The first view is the more correct, that the follower considers the prayer of his imam permissible, and what is considered in his case is his own opinion, so it is necessary to say it is permissible, as in al-Tabyin and Fath al-Qadir. And he restricted it by his saying: 'And the imam does not know that' so that he is resolute in his intention and it is possible to attribute the validity of his prayer to the belief of his imam. But if he knows it and he is upon the belief of his madhhab, he becomes like a trifler and has no intention, so there is no way to attribute the validity of his prayer. His saying: (and he is upon the belief of his madhhab) - as for if he follows the madhhab of the follower, then their beliefs are united and there is no discussion. His saying: 'and he has no intention' - i.e. for the trifler. His saying: 'so there is no way to attribute the validity of his prayer' - the first [word] 'attribution' is omitted. And if he knows the corruption of his imam's prayer, either by the testimony of upright persons that he had an event, then prayed, or by his own information from himself - if he is upright, his statement is accepted and he must repeat; if he is not upright, it is not accepted, but repetition is recommended as in al-Siraj. And if he knows a nullifier in the prayer of the imam, it is not permissible for him to follow him by consensus.
Source pages p. 295

Commentary
This passage from the hashya addresses the ruling on a follower whose imam belongs to a different madhhab that considers the follower's prayer invalid. The author first states the majority opinion (of the Hanafis) that it is permissible to follow such an imam, provided the imam is unaware of the follower's differing view. The hashya explains the reasoning: the follower bases his action on his own belief that the prayer is valid, not the imam's opinion. The key condition is the imam's ignorance, ensuring the follower's intention remains sound. If the imam knows the follower's view but sticks to his own, the act becomes mere play and invalid. The commentary then clarifies that if the follower adopts the imam's madhhab, the issue resolves. A secondary ruling: if the follower later learns the imam's prayer was invalid (e.g., due to ḥadath), he must repeat if the imam was trustworthy; otherwise, repetition is recommended. The passage concludes that if a nullifier is known during the prayer, following is impermissible by consensus.

Key Terms
اقتداء (iqtidā’): The act of following an imam in congregational prayer.
مذهب (madhhab): A school of Islamic law; here referring to the doctrinal position of the imam or follower.
تابعية (tābi‘iyyah): Subordination; the principle that the follower's prayer is linked to the imam's.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Following an imam of a different madhhab is valid if the follower believes the prayer is valid and the imam is unaware of the difference; the follower's own intention determines validity.

Can a Mutayammim Lead a Person with Wudu?
Intra-Hanafi dispute on imam's tayammum validity

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the intra-Hanafi dispute on whether a person with wudu can follow a mutayammim imam, and state the mufta bihi position.

Core Idea
Does tayammum equal wudu? The answer hinges on whether you see it as a tool substitution or a purification substitution.

In Hanafi fiqh, a person with wudu normally follows an imam who also has wudu. But what if the imam has performed tayammum? This lesson unpacks a fascinating intra-madhhab disagreement between Imam Muhammad and the two (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) on this very question. The passage from Hashiya al-Tahtawi shows how the same Quranic verse can be read differently, leading to opposite rulings.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two positions
State that Muhammad holds it invalid, while Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf hold it valid. Understand the core legal outcome.
Both positions are recorded in Zahir al-Riwayah.
2
Analyse the reasoning (ta'lil)
Muhammad focuses on the necessity (darura) of tayammum, making it a weak purification, so a strong purification (wudu) cannot lean on it. The two focus on the absoluteness (itlaq) of tayammum, making it like wudu in essence.
This is an example of qiyas khafi (hidden analogy) vs istihsan.
3
Examine the dalil from the Quran
The verse 'fa lam tajidu ma'an fa tayammamu…' mentions water and earth as two tools. The two see this as substitution between tools, so they are equivalent. Muhammad sees it as substitution between the two purifications themselves.
The Quranic text is the same, but the understanding differs.
4
Apply to a hypothetical far'
If a person with wudu also has water and follows a mutayammim, both sides agree it is invalid. This shows where the analogy breaks: the two's hypothetical case confirms their reasoning.
This contrasts with the original case where the follower has no water.
5
Determine the mufta bhi
The position of the two (validity) is the relied-upon fatwa. Al-Tahtawi notes 'wa la huma' and the apparent text supports this view.
The tarjih is based on the broader applicability and textual support.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (والخلاف الخ) اعلم أن طهارة التيمم فيها جهة الإطلاق باعتبار عدم توقتها بخلاف طهارة المستحاضة مثلاً وجهة الضرورة باعتبار أن المصير إليها الضرورة العجز عن الماء، وهذا لا خلاف فيه وإنما الخلاف في التعليل فعلل محمد ههنا بجهة الضرورة لنفي جواز إقتداء المتوضيء بالمتيمم إحتياطاً، وهما عللا الصحة بجانب الإطلاق لأن طهارته كالطهارة بالماء من حيث ذلك، وهذا الاختلاف مبني على الخلاف الذي ذكره . قوله : (وظاهر النص يدل عليه) فإن الله تعالى قال : فلم تجدوا ماء فتيمموا صعيداً طيباً فإنه ذكر الآلتين، وجعل الخلفية بينهما قوله وعند محمد بين (الطهارتين أي واحداهما وضرورية والأخرى أصلية ولا شك أن من اشتمل على الطهارة الأصلية أقوى حالاً . من حال من اشتمل على الطهارة الضرورية فصار كما لو كان مع المتوضيء ماء فاقتدى بالمتيمم فإنه لا يجوز ولهما أن التيمم طهارة مطلقة أي غير مؤقتة بوقت الصلاة، ولهذا لا تتقدر بقدر الحاجة.
His saying: (and the dispute etc.) Know that the purification of tayammum has an aspect of absoluteness because it is not tied to a time, unlike the purification of a mustahadah for example, and an aspect of necessity because resorting to it is necessitated by inability to find water. There is no dispute about this; the dispute is only in the reasoning. Muhammad here reasoned with the aspect of necessity to negate the permissibility of a person with wudu following a mutayammim, as a precaution. The two (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) reasoned for validity based on the aspect of absoluteness, because his purification is like purification with water in that respect. This difference is based on the difference he mentioned. His saying: (and the apparent text indicates it) because Allah Most High said: 'and you do not find water, then perform tayammum with clean earth' – He mentioned the two tools and made substitution between them. And according to Muhammad, it is between the two purifications, one being necessary and the other original. There is no doubt that one who has original purification is stronger than one who has necessary purification. Thus it becomes like the case where a person with wudu has water and follows a mutayammim – which is not permissible. Their (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf's) view is that tayammum is an absolute purification, i.e., not tied to the time of prayer, and therefore it is not limited to the extent of need.
Source pages p. 295

Commentary
This passage explains the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the validity of a person with wudu (متوضئ) following a mutayammim (متيمم) as imam. The hashya first clarifies that tayammum has two aspects: absoluteness (إطلاق) because it is not time-bound, and necessity (ضرورة) because it is allowed only when water is absent. The disagreement is not about these aspects but about which to emphasize. Imam Muhammad emphasizes necessity, leading him to rule that such following is invalid, as a strong purification (wudu) should not be built upon a weak one (tayammum). Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf emphasize absoluteness, considering tayammum to be like wudu in essence, so it is valid. The proof from the Quran (5:6) is cited: the āyah mentions 'water' and 'earth' as alternative tools, indicating substitution between tools (not between purifications), supporting the view of the two. Muhammad, however, sees substitution between the purifications themselves, hence the ruling. This is a classic example of qiyāṣ khafī (hidden analogy) versus istiḥsān.

Key Terms
متيمم (mutayammim): A person who performs tayammum (dry ablution) due to unavailability of water.
إطلاق (iṭlāq): Absoluteness; here referring to tayammum not being tied to a specific prayer time.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the effective cause (illa) of the dispute between Imam Muhammad and the two (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf)?
A) Whether tayammum can be performed in the mosque.
B) Whether the substitution in the Quran is between tools or between purifications.
C) Whether the follower has water or not.
D) Whether tayammum requires intention.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, a person with wudu may validly follow a mutayammim imam (mufta bihi) because tayammum is an absolute purification, equivalent to wudu for the purpose of imamate.

Rulings on Equivalence in Imamate
Series of rulings on equivalence in imamate

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rulings on who may follow whom in prayer based on equivalence and identify the intra-madhhab disagreements.

Core Idea
Equivalence in purification and physical ability determines the validity of following in prayer.

This passage from Hashiya al-Tahtawi clarifies several cases where the validity of following depends on the similarity in state between imam and follower. It addresses purification cases (washing vs. wiping), physical positions (standing/sitting/gesturing), and the difference between supererogatory and obligatory prayer. Understanding these rulings helps ensure the validity of congregational prayer in various circumstances.

Guided Path
1
Identify the cases
List all the distinct scenarios mentioned: ghasil following masih, wound covering, standing following sitting, hunchback, gesturer following gesturer, supererogatory behind obligatory, and tarawih exception.
Each case has its own nuance.
2
State the ruling for each case
Determine whether following is valid (sahih) or invalid according to the relied-upon view (mufta bihi). For example, standing following sitting is valid according to the two (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf).
3
Note intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Identify where Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf differ from Muhammad al-Shaybani. For standing following sitting, Muhammad considers it invalid; for hunchback, similar disagreement.
4
Examine the dalil
For the sitting imam case, the proof is the hadith of the Prophet (peace be upon him) leading prayer sitting while the companions stood behind him during his final illness.
This is a zanni dalil but sufficient for istihsan.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The positions of the two (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) are mufta bihi in most cases, as adopted by later Hanafi authorities.
The minority view of Muhammad is considered less preponderant.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله: (وصح اقتداء غاسل بماسح) لاستواء حالهما ثم الماسح على الجبيرة أولى من الماسح على الخف لأن مسحها كالغسل لما تحتها بخلاف الخف قوله: (أو خرقة قرحة) أي جراحة قوله : (لا يسيل منها شيء) فإن سال فهو معذور إن استوفي شروطه فلا الاقتداء يصح به إلا لمماثل له، أو لمن حالاً منه قوله: (وصح اقتداء قائم بقاعد أي يركع، ويسجد وهذا عندهما خلافاً لمحمد، وقوله أحوط كما في البرهان وغيره والدلائل مستوفاة في المطولات. قوله: (صلى خلف أبي بكر الخ) فائدة زائدة وقوله : ثم أتم لنفسه أي لأنه مسبوق. قوله: (إتفاقاً على الأصح) يعني . أن حكاية الاتفاق أصح من حكاية الخلاف ومثله يقال في نظائره. قوله: (وفي الظهيرية هو الأصح) محمول على أنه الأصح من قولي محمد لا الأصح مطلقاً لأن أكثر العلماء أخذ بقولهما، وقد أوضحه السيد قوله : (وصح إقتداء موم بمثله) سواء كانا قائمين، أو قاعدين، أو مستلقين أو مضطجعين، أو مختلفين وكلها جائزة في الأصح كما في النهاية، بل صحح التمرتاشي الإجماع عليه قوله : (أو المأموم مضطجعاً) أي أو كان المأموم مضطجعاً والإمام قاعداً قال في الشرح لا عكسه. قال الزيلعي وهو المختار لكن في النهر عن التمرتاشي الأظهر الجواز على قولهما وكذا على قول محمد في الأصح، وهو المناسب لإطلاق كلام المصنف ولا ينافيه قوله بمثله لأن المراد المثلية بالنظر لمطلق الإيماء، وتمامه في السيد. قوله: (ومتنقل بمفترض إلا في التراويح فإن الأرجح عدم جواز الاقتداء كما في الخانية، وصححه في غاية البيان لأنها شرعت على هيئة مخصوصة فيراعي وصفها الخاص للخروج عن العهدة كما في الدر والمراد أنه لا يحسب من التراويح لا أن الاقتداء يقع باطلاً كما لا يخفى لا يقال أن القراءة في الآخريين فرض في حق المتنقل نقل في حق المفترض لأنا نقول صلاة المقتدي أخذت حكم صلاة الإمام بسبب الاقتداء، ولهذا يلزمه أربع ركعات في الرباعية، ولو لم يدركه إلا في الشفع الثاني، ولهذا أشار المؤلف بقوله، وصار تبعاً لإمامه في القراءة.
His saying: (And it is valid for one who washes to follow one who wipes) because their states are equal. Then the one who wipes over a splint is better than the one who wipes over the khuff because wiping over it is like washing what is under it, unlike the khuff. His saying: (or a cloth over a wound) i.e., a wound. His saying: (from which nothing flows) if something flows, then he is excused if he fulfills the conditions, so following is not valid for him except for one like him or one in his state. His saying: (And it is valid for a standing person to follow a sitting one) i.e., he bows and prostrates, and this is according to the two (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf), contrary to Muhammad, and his saying is more precautionary as in al-Burhan and others, and the proofs are covered in the lengthy texts. His saying: (He prayed behind Abu Bakr etc.) is an additional benefit. His saying: (then he completed for himself) i.e., because he was late. His saying: (by agreement, according to the most correct) means that the narration of agreement is more correct than the narration of dispute, and the like is said in its parallels. His saying: (And in al-Zahiriyyah, it is the most correct) is taken to mean the most correct of Muhammad's two statements, not absolutely most correct, because most scholars adopted the view of the two. His saying: (And it is valid for a gesturer to follow one like him) whether both are standing, sitting, lying on one side, or lying prone, or different, all are permissible in the most correct view as in al-Nihayah; rather al-Tamartashi affirmed consensus upon it. His saying: (or the follower is lying prone) i.e., or the follower is lying prone and the imam is sitting. He said in the sharh: not the reverse. Al-Zayla'i said it is the chosen view, but in al-Nahr from al-Tamartashi, the apparent view is permissibility according to the two, and likewise according to Muhammad in the most correct view, and it matches the general meaning of the author's statement and does not contradict his saying 'like him' because the intended likeness is with respect to absolute gesture. His saying: (And a supererogatory performer behind an obligatory performer) except in tarawih, for the most preponderant view is that following is not permissible, as in al-Khaniyyah, and it is affirmed in Ghayat al-Bayan because it was legislated in a specific way, so its particular description must be considered to discharge the obligation. The intent is that it does not count as tarawih, not that the following is invalid, as is obvious. It cannot be said that the recitation in the last two rak'ahs is obligatory for the supererogatory performer but transferred for the obligatory performer, because we say: the follower's prayer takes the ruling of the imam's prayer due to following, hence he must perform four rak'ahs in the four-rak'ah prayer, even if he joined only in the second pair. And this is what the author indicated by his saying: 'and he becomes a follower to his imam in recitation.'
Source pages p. 296

Commentary
This extended passage from the hashya covers multiple concise rulings from the matn regarding who may validly follow whom in prayer. The overall principle is equivalence (mumāthalah) in the state of purification or physical ability. The hashya systematically explains each ruling: a person who washes his feet (ghāsil) may validly follow one who wipes over khuff or a splint because their states of purification are equal. However, if a wound discharges fluid, the follower must be in a similar state. A standing person may follow a sitting imam according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, while Muhammad considers it invalid, citing precaution. The hashya mentions the historical report that the Prophet (peace be upon him) in his last illness prayed sitting while the people stood behind him. The ruling on following a hunchback (ahdab) is cited: if his hump reaches the bowing level, it is valid according to the two but invalid according to Muhammad. Following a gesturer (mūmī’) by one who also gestures is valid in all cases by agreement, with some details on different positions. A person performing supererogatory prayer may follow one performing obligatory prayer, except in tarawih where it does not count as tarawih, though the following itself is not invalid. The hashya explains that the follower's prayer adopts the imam's ruling, hence he must complete four rak'ahs even if he joined late.

Key Terms
ماسح (māsih): One who wipes over khuff (leather socks) or a splint/wound covering.
موم (mūmī’): One who gestures (especially in prayer due to illness) instead of bowing and prostrating fully.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the mufta bihi Hanafi view, can a person performing supererogatory prayer follow an imam performing obligatory prayer in tarawih?
A) Yes, and it counts as tarawih.
B) Yes, but it does not count as tarawih.
C) No, it is invalid.
D) Only if the follower also intends obligatory.

Key Takeaway
Equivalence in purification and physical ability is the guiding principle for validity of following in prayer; the school's relied-upon view accommodates practical needs.

When the Imam's Prayer is Invalid: Follower's Obligation to Repeat
Ruling on necessity to repeat prayer if imam's prayer is found invalid.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the rule regarding repetition of prayer when the imam's prayer is found invalid, and distinguish between cases of initial invalidity and nullifiers occurring during the prayer.

Core Idea
If the imam's prayer is invalid from the start, the follower must repeat; but if invalidity occurs later, no repetition is required.

This passage from Hashiya al-Tahtawi addresses a key question in congregational prayer: what happens when the imam's prayer is later discovered to be invalid? The ruling depends on whether the invalidity existed from the beginning (due to missing a condition or pillar) or arose during the prayer (such as the imam's apostasy). Understanding this distinction is crucial for determining the follower's obligation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The follower must repeat (i'ādah) as an obligation (fard) when the imam's prayer is found to have been invalid from the beginning due to missing a condition (shart) or pillar (rukn).
The text uses 'a'āda (عاد) meaning repetition as a necessary obligation.
2
Locate the dalil
The principle: 'If the prayer of the imam becomes invalid, the prayer of those behind him becomes invalid.' This is based on the dependency of the follower's prayer on the imam's.
This is a qiyas argument: the follower's prayer is like a building on the imam's foundation.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The legal link is that the follower's prayer is valid only if the imam's prayer is valid. If the imam's foundation is unsound, the follower's building collapses.
Hanafi usul: this is a clear qiyas that cannot be overridden by istihsan in this context.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
However, the rule has exceptions: if a nullifier (mubṭil) occurs during the prayer (e.g., apostasy, imam going to Friday prayer after zuhr, returning to sajdah of recitation), the follower is not required to repeat.
The key distinction is whether the invalidity existed from the start or arose later.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
The commentary (Al-Tahtawi) clarifies that the general principle applies only to initial invalidity, not to later nullifiers. This is the mufta bihi position.
The distinction prevents unnecessary repetition and is based on the practical difference in the nature of the defect.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإن ظهر بطلان صلاة إمامه) بفوات شرط أو ركن (أعاد ) لزوماً يعني افترض عليه الإتيان بالفرض وليس المراد الإعادة الجابرة لنقص في المؤدى لقوله : إذا فسدت صلاة الإمام فسدت صلاة. من خلفه وإذا طرأ المبطل لا إعادة على المأموم، كارتداد الإمام وسعيه للجمعة بعد ظهره دونهم، وعوده لسجود تلاوة أنه باطل . قوله: (بعد ظهره) أي بعد أداء الظهر بجماعة فسعى هو دونهم قوله : (وعوده لسجود تلاوة) ...
(And if the invalidity of his imam's prayer becomes apparent) due to missing a condition or pillar, (he must repeat) necessarily, meaning that it is obligatory upon him to perform the obligation. And it does not mean the compensatory repetition for a deficiency in the performed prayer, because of his saying: 'If the prayer of the imam becomes invalid, the prayer of those behind him becomes invalid.' And if a nullifier occurs, there is no repetition upon the follower, such as the apostasy of the imam and his going to Friday after his zuhr without them, and his return to prostration of recitation that it is invalid. His saying: (after his zuhr) meaning after performing zuhr in congregation, so he went to Friday without them. His saying: (and his return to prostration of recitation)...
Source pages p. 296

Commentary
This passage clarifies the ruling when the imam's prayer is discovered to have been invalid due to a missing condition (shart) or pillar (rukn). The follower must repeat (i'ādah) as a necessary obligation, because the invalidity of the imam's prayer automatically invalidates the follower's prayer according to the principle 'if the imam's prayer is corrupt, the follower's prayer is corrupt.' However, the hashya distinguishes between invalidity arising from a deficiency at the outset and a nullifier that occurs during the prayer ('tāri' al-mubṭil). In the latter case, the follower is not required to repeat. Examples given: the imam's apostasy during prayer, or if the imam leaves to attend Friday prayer after having already prayed zuhr without the knowledge of the followers, or if the imam returns for a prostration of recitation. The exact ruling on the last example is incomplete in the text, but the general principle stands.

Key Terms
بطلان (buṭlān): Invalidity; a prayer that is deficient in a condition or pillar, thus requiring repetition.
إعادة (i'ādah): Repetition of the prayer; here it is required when the imam's prayer is invalid.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In which case is the follower NOT required to repeat the prayer if the imam's prayer becomes invalid?
A) If the imam misses a condition of prayer unknowingly.
B) If a nullifier occurs during the prayer, such as the imam's apostasy.
C) If the imam misses a pillar.
D) Always, because the follower's prayer depends on the imam.

Key Takeaway
The follower's obligation to repeat depends on whether the imam's invalidity existed from the start (requires repetition) or arose during the prayer (no repetition).

Following a Hunchbacked Imam: The Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on validity of following a hunchback imam when hump reaches ruku' level

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the disagreement between Abu Hanifa/Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad regarding following a hunchbacked imam and identify the mufta bihi position.

Core Idea
A hunchbacked imam is valid unless his hump reaches bowing; then the two allow it, Muhammad forbids—the mufta bihi is allowance.

In Hanafi fiqh, the validity of following an imam with a physical condition is tested by analogy to the Prophet's own practice. This passage presents a dispute within the school: when a hunchbacked imam's hump reaches the level of bowing, does the slight bending for ruku' break the analogy with a sitting imam? The answer determines whether the follower's prayer is valid.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is the act being ruled on? Following a hunchbacked imam in prayer. What is the default ruling? Valid if the hump does not reach bowing level – unanimous.
The hump's height relative to bowing is the decisive factor.
2
Locate the dispute
When the hump reaches bowing level and the imam bends slightly for ruku', who disagrees? Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf permit it; Imam Muhammad forbids it.
Note that 'the two' here refers to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, not the usual pair of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad.
3
Understand the proofs
The Hanafi proof (for the two) is qiyas (analogy) to a sitting imam: the lower half of the hunchback is straight/even like a sitting person. Muhammad's proof: the posture is not truly analogous because the bending for ruku' creates a different condition.
The hadith of the Prophet praying while sitting is cited as the basis for the analogy.
4
Evaluate the tarjih
The text states that the view of the two is 'al-asah' (most correct) and that most scholars adopted it. However, al-Zayla'i reports that in al-Zahiriyyah, Muhammad's view is considered most correct within his own position.
The overall mufta bihi is the view of the two; the text clarifies the apparent conflict in 'asah' statements.
5
Determine the practical consequence
The thamarah al-khilaf: if one follows Muhammad's view, the prayer behind such an imam is invalid and must be repeated. Following the view of the two, it is valid.
A mufti should give the fatwa according to the mufta bihi: permissibility.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
النبي صلى الظهر يوم السبت أو الأحد في مرض موته جالساً والناس خلفه قياماً وهي آخر صلاة صلاها إماماً وصلى خلف أبي بكر الركعة الثانية صبح يوم الإثنين مأموماً، ثم أتم لنفسه ذكره البيهقي في المعرفة (و) صح اقتداء (بأحدب) لم يبلغ حدبه حد الركوع اتفاقاً على الأصح وإذا بلغ وهو ينخفض للركوع قليلاً يجوز عندهما وبه أخذ عامة العلماء، وهو الأصح بمنزلة الاقتداء بالقاعد لاستواء نصفه الأسفل ولا يجوز عند محمد قال الزيلعي وفي الظهيرية وهو الأصح انتهى فقد اختلف التصحيح فيه قوله: (صلى خلف أبي بكر الخ) فائدة زائدة وقوله : ثم أتم لنفسه أي لأنه مسبوق. قوله: (إتفاقاً على الأصح) يعني . أن حكاية الاتفاق أصح من حكاية الخلاف ومثله يقال في نظائره. قوله: (وفي الظهيرية هو الأصح) محمول على أنه الأصح من قولي محمد لا الأصح مطلقاً لأن أكثر العلماء أخذ بقولهما، وقد أوضحه السيد
The Prophet prayed Dhuhr on Saturday or Sunday in his illness while sitting, and the people behind him were standing. That was the last prayer he led as imam. He prayed behind Abu Bakr the second rak'ah of Fajr on Monday as a follower, then completed it for himself. This was mentioned by al-Bayhaqi in al-Ma'rifah. And the following of a hunchback is valid if his hump does not reach the level of bowing, by agreement according to the most correct view. If it does reach and he lowers himself slightly for bowing, it is permissible according to the two (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf), and the generality of scholars adopted it, and it is the most correct view, being like following a sitting person because his lower half is even. It is not permissible according to Muhammad. Al-Zayla'i said: And in al-Zahiriyyah, it is the most correct, end. So there is disagreement on what is deemed correct. Commentary: 'He said: (He prayed behind Abu Bakr etc.)' is an additional benefit. 'He said: then he completed for himself' means because he was a latecomer. 'He said: (by agreement according to the most correct)' means that the narration of agreement is more correct than the narration of disagreement. The same is said in its parallels. 'He said: (and in al-Zahiriyyah it is the most correct)' is interpreted to mean the most correct of Muhammad's two sayings, not absolutely the most correct, because most scholars took the position of the two, and al-Sayyid clarified it.
Source pages p. 296

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute within the Hanafi school. It begins by mentioning the Prophet's practice of praying while sitting in his final illness, establishing the general permissibility of following a sitting imam. Then it addresses the specific case of an imam with a hunchback (aḥdab). There are two scenarios: if the hunchback's hump does not reach the level of bowing, there is consensus that following him is valid. If the hump does reach that level and he bends only slightly for bowing, Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf (the Two) rule that it is valid by analogy to a sitting imam, because his lower half remains straight. They are followed by most scholars. Imam Muhammad holds it invalid because the hunchback's posture is not equivalent to sitting. The text notes that al-Zayla'i reports from al-Zahiriyyah that Muhammad's position is considered the most correct within his own criterion, but the overall most correct view is that of the majority. The commentary explains that the phrase 'bi al-mutlaq' (absolutely) qualifies that the asahh is relative. The practical consequence: a follower should follow the view of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf as it is the mufta bihi.

Key Terms
أحدب (aḥdab): A person with a hunchback; a curvature of the spine.
عندهما (ʿindahumā): According to the two: Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf (contrary to usual Sahibayn referring to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad).
الأصح (al-aṣaḥḥ): The most correct opinion among Hanafi scholars.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling of following a hunchbacked imam whose hump reaches the level of bowing and who bends slightly for ruku' according to Imam Muhammad?
A) Permissible
B) Impermissible
C) Permissible only if the follower also sits
D) Impermissible only if the follower stands

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi mufta bihi permits following a hunchbacked imam even if his hump reaches bowing level, by analogy to a sitting imam, despite Imam Muhammad's dissent.

Ruling on a Nodding Follower Following Another Nodding Imam
Ruling on nodding follower following another nodding imam

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions under which a nodding follower (mūm) may validly follow another nodding imam.

Core Idea
A nodding imam can lead a nodding follower if the imam's condition is stronger.

This lesson addresses the validity of praying behind an imam who also prays by gestures. The Hanafi school permits such following under specific conditions, ensuring the follower's prayer is sound.

Guided Path
1
Identify the main ruling
The text states that a nodding follower can validly follow another nodding imam. This is the base ruling.
2
Analyze the conditions
The follower can follow if both are sitting, both are lying down, or the follower is lying and the imam is sitting. The key is that the imam's state is not weaker than the follower's.
Sitting is considered stronger than lying, so an imam sitting can lead a follower lying.
3
Understand the rationale
The ruling is based on the principle that the imam's strength supports the follower's weakness. This ensures the prayer is valid as long as the imam's posture is equal or stronger.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(و) صح اقتداء (موم بمثله) بأن كانا قاعدين، أو مضطجعين أو المأموم مضطجعاً، والإمام قاعداً لقوة حاله ومتتفل بمفترض) لأنه بناء للضعيف على القوي وصار تبعاً لإمامه في القراءة (وإن ظهر بطلان صلاة إمامه) بفوات شرط أو ركن (أعاد ) لزوماً يعني افترض عليه الإتيان بالفرض وليس المراد الإعادة الجابرة لنقص في المؤدى لقوله : إذا فسدت صلاة الإمام فسدت صلاة من خلفه وإذا طرأ المبطل لا إعادة على المأموم، كارتداد الإمام وسعيه للجمعة بعد ظهره دونهم، وعوده لسجود تلاوة بعد تفرقهم ويلزم (الإمام الذي تبين فساد صلاته (إعلام القوم بإعادة صلاتهم بالقدر الممكن ولو بكتاب أو رسول (في المختار) لأنه صلى بهم ثم جاء ورأسه يقطر بهم، وعلي رضي الله عنه صلى بالناس، ثم تبين له أنه كان محدثاً فأعاد، وأمرهم أن يعيدوا وفي الدراية لا يلزم الإمام الإعلام إذا كانوا قوماً غير معينين وفي خزانة الأكمل لأنه خطأ معفو عنه وعن الوبري يخبرهم وإن كان مختلفاً فيه ونظيره إذا رأى غيره يتوضأ من ماء نجس، أو على ثوبه نجاسة.
And valid is the following of a nodding person by another like him, if both are sitting, or both lying down, or the follower lying down and the imam sitting due to the strength of his state. And (valid is) the supererogatory (follower) behind an obligatory (imam) because it is building the weak upon the strong, and he becomes a follower of his imam in recitation. And if the invalidity of his imam's prayer appears (due to missing a condition or pillar), he repeats necessarily, meaning the performance of the obligatory prayer is required; it is not meant the compensatory repetition for a deficiency in the performed prayer. Because he (the Prophet) said: When the imam's prayer becomes corrupt, the prayer of those behind him becomes corrupt. And if an invalidating factor occurs, there is no repetition upon the follower, such as the apostasy of the imam, or his striving for Friday after his Dhuhr without them, or his return for a prostration of recitation after they disperse. And it is obligatory (upon the imam whose prayer is discovered to be invalid) to inform the people to repeat their prayer to the best of his ability, even by a letter or messenger, according to al-Mukhtar. Because he led them in prayer, and then he came with his head dripping water (hadith). And Ali (may Allah be pleased with him) led the people, then it became clear to him that he was in a state of hadath, so he repeated and ordered them to repeat. And in al-Diraya, the imam is not obliged to inform if the people are unspecified. And in Khizanat al-Akmal, because it is a forgiven mistake. And from al-Obari, he should inform them even if it is disputed. Its parallel is if he sees someone performing wudu with impure water, or having impurity on his garment.
Source pages p. 296

Commentary
This passage contains several rulings within the section on following imams. First, it states that a person who prays by gestures (mūm, i.e., nodding due to illness) can validly follow another who also prays by gestures, whether both are sitting or lying down, or the follower is lying and the imam sitting. The key is the imam's state being stronger. Second, a person praying a supererogatory (nafl) prayer can validly follow an imam who is praying an obligatory (farḍ) prayer, based on the principle 'building the weak upon the strong' and because the follower becomes dependent on the imam for recitation. Third, if the imam's prayer becomes invalid due to a missing condition or pillar, the follower must repeat their prayer entirely, not just perform a compensatory prostration. This is based on the general principle that invalidity of the imam's prayer extends to the follower. Exceptions are when an invalidator occurs after the prayer (e.g., apostasy) that does not affect the follower, or when the imam's mistake is unrelated to the follower's prayer, such as the imam's personal journey for Jumu'ah after his own Zuhr. The passage also discusses the obligation of an imam whose prayer becomes invalid to inform the congregation. The preferred view (al-Mukhtar) is that he must inform them even by sending a message, based on the story of Ali (RA). However, other views relieve him if the congregation are unspecified, or consider it a forgiven mistake. The passage ends with an analogy: one must inform others if he sees them using impure water or having impurity on their garment.

Key Terms
موم (mūm): A person who prays by gestures/nodding due to illness or inability to perform full postures.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is a valid scenario for a nodding follower (mūm) to follow another nodding imam?
A) Follower sitting, imam lying
B) Follower lying, imam sitting
C) Follower standing, imam sitting
D) Both standing but unable to bow

Key Takeaway
A nodding follower can validly follow a nodding imam as long as the imam's posture is not weaker than the follower's.

Ruling on a Supererogatory Follower Behind an Obligatory Imam
Ruling on supererogatory follower behind obligatory imam

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi ruling that a supererogatory prayer behind an obligatory imam is valid and provide the rationale.

Core Idea
A nafl follower builds upon the strong foundation of the imam's fard prayer.

This lesson examines the validity of performing a supererogatory (nafl) prayer by following an imam who is leading an obligatory (fard) prayer. The Hanafi school affirms this, based on the principle of building the weak upon the strong.

Guided Path
1
State the ruling
The text explicitly says that a mutanaffil (supererogatory follower) can validly follow a muftarid (imam performing fard).
2
Understand the rationale
The reason given is 'building the weak upon the strong' and that the follower becomes dependent on the imam's recitation, thus the nafl (weaker intention) is supported by the imam's fard (stronger intention).
This is a specific Hanafi principle: the weaker act gains strength through attachment to a stronger act.
3
Note the exception
There is an exception for Tarawih prayer (not in this passage) where the opposite ruling applies: one cannot pray nafl behind an imam performing Tarawih if the imam's intention is also nafl? Actually the exception is that in Tarawih, the imam's prayer is considered supererogatory as well, so the principle still holds? But the text mentions that the ruling is general except in Tarawih (from the original source).
In Tarawih, both imam and follower are considered to be performing nafl, so the ruling remains valid. However, some scholars differentiate.

Ruling on the Imam's Duty to Inform if His Prayer Becomes Invalid
Ruling on imam's invalidity and duty to inform

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi ruling on an imam's obligation to inform his congregation if his prayer is discovered to be invalid, and identify the differences of opinion within the school.

Core Idea
The imam must inform his followers to repeat their prayer, but scholars differ on the scope of this obligation.

This lesson discusses the consequences of an imam's prayer becoming invalid and his duty to inform the congregation. The Hanafi school provides detailed rulings based on hadith and the practice of Ali (RA), with some scholarly disagreement on whether informing is always required.

Guided Path
1
Understand the base ruling
If the imam's prayer becomes invalid due to a missing condition or pillar, the followers must repeat their prayer because the imam's invalidity extends to them, based on the hadith.
Exceptions: if the invalidity occurs after the prayer (e.g., apostasy) or if the imam's mistake is unrelated to the followers (e.g., imam returns for prostration after they leave).
2
Analyze the obligation to inform
According to al-Mukhtar, the imam must inform the congregation even by sending a letter or messenger. This is based on the hadith of the Prophet leading with head dripping and the action of Ali (RA).
3
Examine the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Other views: al-Diraya says the imam is not obliged if the congregation are unspecified; Khizanat al-Akmal considers it a forgiven mistake. Al-Obari suggests he should inform even if disputed.
The parallel is given: if one sees someone using impure water or having impurity on garment, he should inform.

Excuses for Missing Congregational Prayer
Listing of 18 valid excuses exempting one from attending congregational prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the valid excuses for missing congregational prayer according to the Hanafi school and explain the underlying principle of dispensation (rukhsah).

Core Idea
Congregational prayer is wajib, but eighteen valid excuses lift the obligation due to hardship.

In this lesson, we examine the Hanafi ruling on excuses that exempt a Muslim from attending the obligatory congregation (jamāʿa). The passage enumerates a list of conditions—including natural phenomena, physical disabilities, and safety concerns—under which the wujūb of jamāʿa is lifted. Understanding these excuses helps one apply the principle that the Sharīʿah does not impose hardship (ḥaraj).

Guided Path
1
Identify the default obligation
What is the default ruling on attending jamāʿa for men? It is wajib (necessary) according to the Hanafi school, not fard, except for Jumuʿah where it is fard.
2
Recognize the principle of rukhsah
When does the obligation fall away? When there is genuine hardship (mashaqqa). The list provides specific instances where hardship is presumed.
The general rule is that obligations are lifted in cases of necessity or severe hardship.
3
Classify the excuses
Group the listed excuses: (1) Weather-related (rain, severe cold, darkness), (2) Health-related (blindness, paralysis, illness, chronic disease, amputation), (3) Safety-related (fear of a tyrant, imprisonment), (4) Environmental (mud after rain).
4
Note the Hanafi detail
Why are certain conditions included and others excluded? For example, extreme heat is not an excuse, as the text specifies 'severe cold' only. This reflects the principle that the list is exhaustive and analogical extension is limited.
Intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf exists on whether heat can be analogized; the mufta bihi is that it is not an excuse.
5
Apply the list
Given a scenario, determine if the person is excused from jamāʿa. For example, a man with a broken leg that prevents walking is excused under 'sakam' (illness).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
سكت عن فصل يسقط حضور الجماعة بواحد من ثمانية عشر شيئاً منها (مطر) وبرد شديد (وخوف) ظالم (وظلمة) شديدة في الصحيح (وحبس) معسر، ومظلوم (وعمى وفلج وقطع يد ورجل (وسقام وإقعاد ووحل) بعد انقطاع مطر قال :
He remained silent about a chapter: Attendance of congregation is dropped due to one of eighteen things: from them (rain), severe cold, fear of a tyrant, intense darkness in the correct view, imprisonment of a debtor and oppressed, blindness, paralysis, amputation of hand and foot, illness, chronic disease, and quagmire after rain ceases. He said: ...
Source pages p. 297

Commentary
This passage introduces a section listing excuses that allow a Muslim to miss the obligatory congregational prayer. The text enumerates 18 conditions under which the obligation (wujūb) of attending the congregation is lifted. These include natural phenomena (rain, cold, darkness), security concerns (fear of oppression), physical disabilities (blindness, paralysis, amputation), health issues (illness, chronic disease), and environmental obstacles (mud after rain). The commentator notes that the author 'remained silent' about a chapter, implying that the matn omitted the full list, which the hashīya supplies. The ruling is that if any of these excuses exist, it is permissible (and in some cases, recommended) to pray at home rather than in the mosque. The list is exhaustive according to Hanafi sources.

Key Terms
جماعة (jamāʿa): Congregational prayer; here, the obligatory prayer attended in the mosque.
مطر (maṭar): Rain that causes hardship (e.g., leading to muddy roads or discomfort).
وحل (waḥal): Mud or quagmire after rain, making travel to the mosque difficult.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school provides an exhaustive list of 18 valid excuses for missing congregational prayer, grounded in the principle of rukhsah to avoid hardship.

The Imam's Obligation to Inform the Congregation of Invalid Prayer
Ruling with proof on imam's obligation to inform after prayer invalidation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on an imam's duty to inform his congregation if his prayer becomes invalid, identify the proof, and evaluate the competing views within the school.

Core Idea
The imam must inform the congregation if his prayer becomes invalid, even by letter or messenger.

This lesson examines a specific situation in congregational prayer: the imam discovers after completion that his own prayer was invalid due to a missed wajib or impurity. Does he have a duty to inform those who prayed behind him? The Hanafi school has a relied-upon position, supported by actions of the Prophet ﷺ and Ali رضي الله عنه, but also significant internal disagreement. We will explore the ruling, the evidence, and the practical implications.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and Its Ruling
The act under discussion is the imam's obligation to inform the congregation that their prayer is invalid and must be repeated. The passage states that this obligation exists 'in the chosen position' (al-mukhtar).
The ruling is wajib, not fard, because the evidence is zanni.
2
Locate the Dalil (Evidence)
The author cites two pieces of evidence: the Prophet ﷺ leading prayer with his head dripping (implying he had performed ghusl after janabah during the prayer?), and Ali رضي الله عنه discovering he was in a state of hadath after leading prayer, so he repeated and ordered the people to repeat.
These are ahad reports, thus zanni al-thubut.
3
Trace the Wajh al-Dalalah
The Prophet's action of coming with dripping head after leading prayer suggests he informed them indirectly. Ali's explicit ordering of repetition indicates that informing is obligatory (wujub), as an instruction to repeat implies a duty to communicate the reason.
Hanafi usul: the command to repeat indicates obligation.
4
Analyze the Intra-Hanafi Ikhtilaf
According to al-Diraya, the imam is not obligated if the congregation are unspecified (ghayr mu'ayyanin). Khizanat al-Akmal considers it a 'forgiven error' (khata' ma'fu 'anhu), meaning no obligation. Al-Wabiri holds that the imam must inform despite the disagreement.
The disagreement centers on whether the obligation applies when the congregation is not personally known.
5
Determine the Mufta Bihi
The text explicitly says 'في المختار' (in the chosen view), meaning the relied-upon position is that the imam must inform, regardless of whether the congregation is specified or not.
This is the view followed in fatwa.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فأعاد لسجود تلاوة بعد تفرقهم ويلزم (الإمام الذي تبين فساد صلاته (إعلام القوم بإعادة صلاتهم بالقدر الممكن ولو بكتاب أو رسول (في المختار) لأنه صلى بهم ثم جاء ورأسه يقطر بهم، وعلي رضي الله عنه صلى بالناس، ثم تبين له أنه كان محدثاً فأعاد، وأمرهم أن يعيدوا وفي الدراية لا يلزم الإمام الإعلام إذا كانوا قوماً غير معينين وفي خزانة الأكمل لأنه خطأ معفو عنه وعن الوبري يخبرهم وإن كان مختلفاً فيه ونظيره إذا رأى غيره يتوضأ من ماء نجس، أو على ثوبه نجاسة.
He repeated the prostration of recitation after their dispersal, and the imam whose prayer becomes invalid is obligated to inform the people to repeat their prayer to the extent possible, even by letter or messenger (according to the chosen position). Because he (the Prophet) prayed with them, then came with his head dripping, and Ali (may Allah be pleased with him) prayed with the people, then it became clear that he was in a state of hadath, so he repeated and ordered them to repeat. And in al-Diraya: the imam is not obligated to inform if they are unspecified people. And in Khizanat al-Akmal: because it is a forgiven error. And according to al-Wabiri, he informs them even if there is disagreement. And its analogy: if he sees someone performing wudu with impure water, or having impurity on his garment.
Source pages p. 297

Commentary
This passage discusses the ruling on an imam who, after leading prayer, discovers that his prayer was invalid (e.g., he was in a state of impurity, or missed a wajib like sajda tilawa after the congregation dispersed). The relied-upon position (al-mukhtar) is that the imam must inform the congregation to repeat their prayer, even if only by sending a message or a messenger. The proof is the action of the Prophet (ﷺ) who came with water dripping from his head after purification and led the prayer, and the action of Ali (r.a.) who repeated his prayer and ordered the people to repeat when he discovered he was in a state of hadath. However, there is a differing view in al-Diraya that if the congregation were unspecified individuals (not a specific group identified by the imam), he is not obligated to inform them. The Khizanat al-Akmal considers it a forgiven error, meaning the imam's prayer is valid despite his invalidity. But according to al-Wabiri, the imam should inform them even if there is disagreement. The analogy given is similar to seeing someone using impure water for wudu or having impurity on his cloth—one should inform them.

Key Terms
إعلام (i'lam): Informing the congregation that their prayer was invalid and must be repeated.
خطأ معفو عنه (khata' ma'fu 'anhu): An error that is excused, meaning the ruling (obligation to inform) is waived because the imam's mistake was unintentional and forgiven.
المختار (al-mukhtar): The chosen or relied-upon position in the Hanafi school regarding a particular issue.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon position (al-mukhtar) in this passage, what must an imam do if his prayer becomes invalid after leading the congregation?
A) He must inform them to repeat their prayer.
B) He does not need to inform them if they are unspecified.
C) He must inform them only if they are specified.
D) He must repeat his prayer alone and say nothing.

Key Takeaway
An imam whose prayer becomes invalid must inform the congregation to repeat, and this obligation is not lifted by the congregation being unspecified—this is the relied-upon Hanafi view.
