The Eighteen Excuses for Missing Jama'ah
Enumeration and commentary on the eighteen excuses for missing jama'ah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list and explain the eighteen valid excuses for missing congregational prayer in the Hanafi school, including the conditions for each and the intra-Hanafi difference on blindness.

Core Idea
Eighteen excuses save you from the sin of missing jama'ah—but each has specific conditions.

Congregational prayer (jama'ah) is a confirmed sunnah (sunnah mu'akkadah), not an obligatory fard. Yet attending it is highly recommended. The Hanafi school, particularly in later works, enumerates eighteen specific excuses that permit a person to miss the congregation without blame. These excuses range from natural obstacles like rain and severe cold to personal necessities like food cravings or urgent travel. This lesson unpacks each excuse, its conditions, and notable scholarly differences, especially regarding blindness.

Guided Path
1
Understand the status of jama'ah and the concept of excuses
Jama'ah is sunnah mu'akkadah, not fard 'ayn. Missing it without excuse is makruh tanzih. The excuses remove the blame but do not eliminate the virtue.
2
Memorize the list of eighteen excuses
Commit the list to memory: rain, severe cold, fear, darkness, imprisonment (debtor/oppressed), blindness, paralysis, amputation, illness, chair-bound, mud after rain, chronic illness, old age, repetition of fiqh (with a group), food distraction, need to relieve oneself, travel preparedness, nursing a patient, severe night wind.
The text also mentions 'zamanah' and 'shaykhukhah' but counts them separately.
3
Examine conditions for each excuse
Each excuse has specific conditions. For example, rain must wet the ground and make walking difficult; severe cold includes extreme heat by analogy; imprisonment is only an excuse for the insolvent debtor; the blind person is excused even if a guide is found (relying on Abu Hanifa).
The commentary clarifies that for blindness, there is an ikhtilaf: Abu Hanifa excuses unconditionally, while the Sahibayn require lack of a guide.
4
Note the mufta bihi position
The relied-upon view in the text is that all listed excuses are valid, and the blindness difference is resolved by following Abu Hanifa's position.
This reflects the later Hanafi preference for ease.
5
Apply the list to real scenarios
Given a scenario, identify if an excuse from the list applies, check its conditions, and state the ruling.
For instance, a light drizzle that does not wet the shoes is not an excuse.

Chapter: Attending congregational prayer is waived by one of eighteen things: rain, severe cold, fear of an oppressor, severe darkness (according to the correct view), imprisonment of an insolvent and an oppressed person, blindness, paralysis, amputation of hand and foot, illness, being chair-bound, and mud after rain has stopped... (continues with commentary on each).
Source pages p. 297

Commentary
This passage lists the eighteen valid excuses that allow a person to miss the congregational prayer (jama'ah) without sin. The excuses are: 1) rain, 2) severe cold, 3) fear of an oppressor (for one's life or property), 4) severe darkness, 5) imprisonment (for an insolvent debtor or a wrongfully imprisoned person), 6) blindness (though there is a difference if a guide is available), 7) paralysis (or inability to walk), 8) amputation of a hand and foot (from opposite sides), 9) illness, 10) being chair-bound, 11) mud (after rain stops), 12) chronic illness/disability, 13) old age, 14) repetition of fiqh study (with a group), 15) presence of desired food that distracts, 16) need to relieve oneself (urine or stool) or passing wind, 17) intention for a journey that is prepared, 18) staying with a patient who needs him, 19) severe wind at night (not daytime). The commentary elaborates on each, including exceptions and conditions. For example, rain excuses only if it makes walking difficult; severe cold is analogous to extreme heat; blindness excuses even if a guide is available according to Abu Hanifa but Abu Yusuf and Muhammad say it is obligatory if a guide exists, though the relied-upon view is that it is excused. The text also discusses the forgiveness of error regarding the imam's invalidity.

Key Terms
تفرقهم (tafarruqihim): Dispersal of the congregation after the prayer.
مطر (matar): Rain that makes walking difficult, as an excuse to miss jama'ah.
تكرار فقه (tikrar fiqh): Repetition of fiqh study, i.e., reviewing or studying fiqh regularly, which excuses one from jama'ah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Severe cold
C) Having a pet at home
D) Being a woman

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school permits missing jama'ah under eighteen specific excuses, each with conditions; the most disputed is blindness when a guide is available, but the relied-upon view excuses it.

Priority in Leading Prayer: Authority, Knowledge, and Recitation
Hashiya establishing the priority order for imamah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi order of priority for imamah and apply it to determine who should lead in various congregational scenarios.

Core Idea
Owner and ruler lead first regardless of knowledge; thereafter, fiqh expertise trumps recitation skill.

When a congregation gathers for prayer, who gets to lead? The Hanafi school provides a clear hierarchy: first the owner of the place, then a person in authority, then the most knowledgeable in prayer rulings, and only then the best reciter. This lesson unpacks that order and the reasoning behind the preference for fiqh knowledge over mere recitation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the first two categories: owner and ruler
Note that 'sahib manzil' (owner/resident) and 'dhu sultan' (authority figure) are given absolute priority. They lead even if others are more learned or pious.
Abu Hanifa and Muhammad hold that this is a right of authority, not merit.
2
When neither is present, determine the next in line
The text says 'fall-a'lam' – the most knowledgeable in the rulings of prayer (purity, validity, nullifiers). This includes knowing the sunnah of recitation but prioritises fiqh over tajweed.
Memorising the obligatory recitation is a condition of validity; sunnah recitation is a condition of completeness.
3
Spot the intra-Hanafi dispute and the tarjih
Abu Yusuf preferred the best reciter (aqra') based on a hadith. The Sahibayn (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) favoured a'lam. The commentator states the relied-upon view (mu'tamad) is that of the two, because recitation is only one pillar.
This illustrates how later Hanafi scholarship settled internal differences.
4
Apply the order to a practical scenario
Given a group with an owner, a visiting governor, and a faqih, the governor leads. If no ruler, the owner leads. If neither, the faqih leads.
The fasiq (open sinner) is disqualified unless no suitable person exists.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل في بيان الأحق بالإمامة و في بيان (ترتيب الصفوف إذا اجتمع قوم ولم يكن بين الحاضرين صاحب منزل اجتمعوا فيه، ولا فيهم ذو وظيفة وهو إمام المحل (ولا ذو سلطان) كأمير ووال وقاض (فالأعلم) بأحكام الصلاة الحافظ ما به سنة القراءة، ويجتنب قوله: (ولم يكن بين الحاضرين المراد بالبينية معنى المعية. قوله: (صاحب منزل) أي ساكن فيه ولو بالإجارة أو بالعارية على التحقيق أما هو وذو الوظيفة فيقدمان مطلقاً سواء اجتمع فيهما هذه الفضائل المذكورة أو لا فصاحب البيت والمجلس وإمام المسجد أحق بالإمامة من غيره وإن كان الغير أفقه واقرأ وأورع وأفضل منه إن شاء تقدم وإن شاء قدم من يريده، وإن كان الذي يقدمه مفضولاً بالنسبة إلى باقي الحاضرين لأنه سلطانه فيتصرف فيه كيف شاء، ويستحب لصاحب البيت أن يأذن لمن هو أفضل قوله : ( وهو إمام المحل لأن صاحب الوظيفة منصوب الواقف، وبتقديم غيره يفوت غرضه وشرط الواقف كنص الشارع. قوله : (ولا ذو سلطان) فهو أولى من الجميع حتى من ساكن المنزل، وصاحب الوظيفة لأن ولايته عامة. وروى البخاري أن ابن عمر كان يصلي خلف الحجاج، وكفى به فاسقاً قال في البناية: هذا في الزمن الماضي لأن الولاة كانوا علماء وغالبهم كانوا صلحاء، وأما في زماننا فأكثر الولاة ظلمة جهلة اهـ . قوله : (فالأعلم بأحكام الصلاة صحة وفساداً وغيرهما، وهذا مراد من قال: أعلمهم بالفقه وأحكام الشريعة إذ الزائد على ذلك غير محتاج إليه هنا . قوله : (الحافظ ما به سنة القراءة) وأما حفظ مقدار الفرض فمعلوم أنه من شروط الصحة وهذه شروط كمال، وفي الدر بشرط اجتنابه للفواحش الظاهرة، وحفظه قدر فرض ، وقيل : واجب وقيل سنة، وقدم أبو يوسف الأقرأ لحديث ورد في ذلك، والمعول عليه قولهما لأن القراءة إنما يحتاج إليها لإقامة ركن واحد،
Chapter on explaining who is most entitled to imamah. When a group gathers and among those present there is no owner of the house in which they have gathered, nor anyone with a post (i.e., the imam of the locality), nor a person of authority (like an amir, governor, or judge), then the most knowledgeable in the rulings of prayer, who memorizes with it the sunnah of recitation, and avoids... He said: 'And there is no owner of the house present' meaning the concept of being present. He said: 'Owner of the house' means a resident therein, even by rent or by loan in the correct view. As for him and the one with the post, they are given priority absolutely... It is recommended for the owner of the house to give permission to one who is better. And Abu Yusuf gave precedence to the best reciter due to a hadith, but the relied-upon is the position of the two (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) because recitation is only needed for one pillar.
Source pages p. 299

Commentary
This passage from the hashīyah discusses who has the greatest right to lead the congregational prayer (imāmah). The commentator al-Tahtawi explains the base text’s order: first, the owner of the house where the prayer takes place (including a renter or borrower), and the appointed imam of the mosque; second, a person of authority (sultan, governor, judge); third, the most knowledgeable in the rulings of prayer (al-a‘lam), particularly regarding validity and nullification; and fourth, the one who has memorized the sunnah of recitation. The commentary refines that the owner and the appointed imam are always given precedence, even if others are more learned or pious, because it is their right and domain. It is, however, recommended for the owner to delegate to a better person. An intra-Hanafi dispute is noted: Abu Yusuf preferred the best reciter (aqra’) based on a hadith, but the relied-upon opinion (al-mu‘tamad) is that of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad (al-Sahibayn), who give priority to the most knowledgeable in fiqh.

Key Terms
أحق بالإمامة (ahaqqu bi-l-imāmah): The one who has the greatest right or entitlement to lead the prayer.
صاحب منزل (sāhib manzil): The owner or resident of the house where prayer is held, including by rent or loan.
ذو سلطان (dhū sulṭān): A person in authority, such as an amir, governor, or judge.
الأعلم بأحكام الصلاة (al-a'lam bi-ahkām al-ṣalāh): The most knowledgeable in the rulings of prayer, particularly what makes it valid or invalid.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the condition for a person to be considered 'a'lam' (most knowledgeable) for imamah?
A) Memorization of the entire Quran.
B) Knowledge of prayer rulings and memorization of sunnah recitation.
C) Being a scholar of fiqh and hadith.
D) Being a hafiz and a qari.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, the right to lead prayer is determined by authority (owner, ruler) first, then by knowledge of fiqh, not merely by recitation skills.

Reward for Missing Congregational Prayer Due to a Valid Excuse
Ruling with proof on reward via intention

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling and proof for obtaining reward for jama'ah when excused, and explain the role of intention in securing that reward.

Core Idea
Sincere intention to attend jama'ah secures its reward even when a valid excuse prevents actual attendance.

Many Muslims worry that missing congregational prayer due to illness, rain, or other valid reasons means losing the immense reward of praying in congregation. This lesson clarifies that the Prophet ﷺ taught that intentions matter greatly: if you genuinely intended to be there but were prevented, you still receive the full reward. We will examine the primary proof (the hadith of intentions) and understand how the Hanafi school applies this principle.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
Read the opening sentence: 'And if one is cut off from the congregation due to a valid excuse... he obtains its reward.' The ruling is that the reward of congregational prayer is obtained through intention alone when one is excused.
The reward is the same as if he had actually prayed in congregation.
2
Locate the primary evidence
The author cites the hadith: 'Actions are only by intentions, and every person has only what he intended.' This is a universally accepted hadith (muttafaq 'alayh) and is the main proof.
The hadith is recorded in Sahih al-Bukhari and Sahih Muslim.
3
Understand the wajh al-dalalah
The phrase 'and every person has only what he intended' shows that a person receives reward for what he intended, even if he did not actually perform the action. Here, the intention to attend congregation suffices for reward.
The intention must be sincere and present at the time one would normally go.
4
Note the supplementary weak hadith
The commentator adds a weak narration: 'The intention of the believer is more effective than his action.' While weak, it reinforces the importance of niyyah.
The weakness does not undermine the main proof, which is strong.
5
Apply the principle
Recognize that this ruling encourages maintaining the niyyah for good deeds even when obstacles arise. In practice, if a legitimate excuse (e.g., illness, fear, heavy rain) prevents attending jama'ah, one should still intend to attend and will receive the reward.
This is a mercy from Allah, emphasizing that sincere desire brings reward.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإذا انقطع عن الجماعة لعذر من أعذارها المبيحة للتخلف وكانت نيته حضورها لولا العذر الحاصل يحصل له ثوابها لقوله : إنما الأعمال بالنيات وإنما لكل امرىء ما نوى . قوله : ( يستضر ) أي المريض بغيبته وإلا فلا. قوله : (وإنما لكل امرىء ما نوي هو محل الشاهد على أحد ما قيل فيه والمعنى أن له ما نواه وان لم يعمله وروى العسكري في الأمثال والبيهقي في الشعب، وقال إسناده ضعيف عن أنس يرفعه نية المؤمن أبلغ من عمله كما في المقاصد الحسنة والله سبحانه وتعالى أعلم، وأستغفر الله العظيم.
And if one is cut off from the congregation due to an excuse from its permissible excuses for staying behind, and his intention was to attend it were it not for the excuse that occurred, he obtains its reward because of his statement: 'Actions are only by intentions, and every person has only what he intended.' His saying: (he is harmed) meaning the patient by his absence, otherwise not. His saying: 'And every person has only what he intended' is the place of evidence for one of the things said about it, and the meaning is that he has what he intended even if he did not do it. And al-Askari narrated in al-Amthal and al-Bayhaqi in al-Shu'ab, and he said its chain is weak, from Anas marfu'an: 'The intention of the believer is more effective than his action,' as in al-Maqasid al-Hasana. And Allah the Exalted and Sublime knows best, and I seek forgiveness from Allah the Great.
Source pages p. 299

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof. It states that if a person is unable to attend the congregational prayer due to a valid excuse (such as illness, fear, or heavy rain), but his intention was to attend had there been no excuse, he still receives the full reward of congregational prayer. The evidence is the Prophet's hadith: 'Actions are only by intentions, and every person has only what he intended.' The commentator clarifies that the hadith means a person gets the reward for what he intended, even if he did not actually perform the act. He then quotes a weak hadith that the intention of a believer is more effective than his action. This ruling encourages Muslims to maintain the intention to attend congregational prayer, as it brings reward even when prevented by legitimate excuses.

Key Terms
نية (niyyah): Intention; the conscious resolve to perform an act of worship for the sake of Allah. Here, it secures reward for jama'ah despite physical inability to join.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a person intends to attend congregational prayer but is prevented by a valid excuse, what does he receive?
A) No reward because he did not pray in congregation.
B) The full reward of congregational prayer.
C) Half the reward of congregational prayer.
D) Only the reward of praying alone.

Key Takeaway
The intention to attend congregational prayer, when prevented by a valid excuse, secures the reward of the congregation.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
10 min
Priorities for Leading Prayer (Imamah) in Hanafi Fiqh
Order of precedence for imamah with evidence and intra-madhhab refinements

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi order of precedence for imamah and apply it to determine who should lead in a given scenario.

Core Idea
Knowledge of fiqh takes precedence over mere recitation in choosing an imam.

Imagine you are in a congregation with no ruler or mosque imam present. Who should lead the prayer? The Hanafi school provides a detailed hierarchy based on religious qualities and social roles. This lesson unpacks that order, with special attention to why the most knowledgeable in fiqh is preferred over the best reciter, and how the presence of a ruler changes the ruling. Understanding these priorities ensures that the imam is chosen in a way that respects both Islamic law and social harmony.

Guided Path
1
Identify the context
First, determine whether there is a ruler (sultan, amir, judge), a mosque imam, or a house owner present. Their precedence is absolute (wajib for ruler). If none of these, the personal qualities come into play.
The presence of a ruler overrides all other considerations; giving him precedence is wajib to avoid insult.
2
Apply the first personal quality: al-'alim (most knowledgeable)
The most knowledgeable in the fiqh rulings of prayer (conditions, pillars, invalidators) is given precedence, even if he does not know other sciences. The proof: fiqh is needed for all parts of the prayer, unlike recitation which is only one pillar.
This is the mufta bihi position, though Abu Yusuf and al-Shafi'i differ.
3
Sequence the remaining qualities
After al-'alim, consider: (2) al-aqra' (best reciter with knowledge of tajweed rules), (3) al-awra' (most pious, avoiding doubtful matters), (4) al-asan (eldest in Islam, not merely age), (5) ahsan khuluq (best character), (6) ahsan wajh (best face), (7) ashraf nasab (noblest lineage), (8) ahsan sawt (best voice).
Some scholars (e.g., author of al-Khulasah) reversed the order of character and face, but the text places character first.
4
Understand the hadith evidence
The Prophet (ﷺ) said to Malik ibn al-Huwayrith: 'Let the older of you lead you.' The Hanafi school interprets 'akbar' here as precedence in Islam, not necessarily biological age.
The hadith is agreed upon (muttafaq alayh).
5
Apply the ruling to a concrete scenario
Given a group with no ruler or house owner: a scholar who knows the fiqh of prayer but has weak recitation vs. a hafiz who does not know fiqh. The scholar leads according to Hanafi. If both are equal in knowledge, then move to recitation, then piety, etc.
This clear hierarchy avoids confusion and ensures the imam can properly lead.

Source Text

فصل في بيان الأحق بالإمامة و في بيان ترتيب الصفوف إذا اجتمع قوم ولم يكن بين الحاضرين صاحب منزل اجتمعوا فيه، ولا فيهم ذو وظيفة وهو إمام المحل ولا ذو سلطان كأمير ووال وقاض فالأعلم بأحكام الصلاة الحافظ اجتناب المحرمات ثم الأسن لقوله صلى الله عليه وسلم : وليؤمكما أكبر كما ثم الأحسن خلقاً بضم الخاء واللام أي ألفة بين الناس ثم الأحسن وجها أي أصبحهم لأنّ حسن الصورة يدل على حسن السريرة لأنه مما يزيد الناس رغبة في الجماعة ثم الأشرف نسباً لاحترامه وتعظيمه ثم الأحسن صوتاً للرغبة في سماعه قوله : ( عند قوله فالأعلم ) والفقه يحتاج إليه لجميع الأركان والواجبات والسنن والمستحبات. قوله: (بقدم السلطان) الظاهر أن ذلك على سبيل الوجوب لأن في تقدم غيره عليه إهانة له وارتكاب المنهي عنه في الحديث وقد علمت ما في البناية. قوله: (ولا يؤم الرجل في سلطانه) أي في مظهر سلطنته، ومحل ولايته، قوله: (على تكرمته) بفتح التاء المثناة فوق وكسر الراء الفراش ونحوه مما يبسط لصاحب المنزل ويختص به وقيل المائدة قوله : (أي الأعلم بأحكام القراءة) من الوقف، والوصل والابتداء وكيفية أداء الحروف وما يتعلق بها كذا في مسكين والقهستاني والظاهر أن من يحكم الأداء، وإن لم يعلم أحكامه في حكم العالم. قوله : (لا) مجرد كثرة حفظ) يعني جودة حفظ أو الأكثر كما قوله : ((دونه) أي دون العالم الكامل المأخوذ من قوله أي الأعلم. قوله : (ثم الأسن) المراد من الأسن أقدمهم إسلاماً بدليل ما سبق في الحديث من قوله : فإن كانوا في الهجرة سواء فأقدمهم إسلاماً فلا يقدم شيخ أسلم على شاب نشأ في الإسلام نهر، وفيه أنه يفوت التنبيه على مرتبة الأسن، ولذا جعل بعضهم رتبة الأقدم إسلاماً متقدمة على رتبة الأسن، وجعلهما مرتبتين وهو حسن قوله : (وليؤمكما أكبر كما قاله لمالك بن الحويرث ولصاحب له وهو ابن عمه حين أراد السفر ولفظه : إذا حضرت الصلاة فأذنا، ثم أقيما وليؤمكما أكبر كما متفق عليه قوله : أي) ألفة بين الناس هذا تفسير باللازم فإن من حسن . ألفته الناس فكثرت عليه الجماعة والمصنف تبع في تقديم حسن الخلق على حسن الوجه مواهب الرحمن وفتح القدير وعكس ذلك صاحب الخلاصة، والغرر ومسكين لأن الظاهر أول ما يدرك من صفات الكمال أو لأنه كالدليل عليه لأن الظاهر عنوان الباطن. قوله : (يدل على حسن السريرة أي غالباً وفسره في الكافي بالأكثر صلاة بالليل، وحديث: من كثرت صلاته بالليل حسن وجهه بالنهار لم يثبته المحدثون كحديث من صلى خلف عالم تقي فكأنما صلى خلف نبي. قوله: (لأنه الخ) الأولى زيادة الواو لصلاحيته للتعليل استقلالاً. قوله: (ثم الأشرف نسباً) قدم بعضهم عليه الأكثر حسباً والحسب شرف الآباء أو المال أو الدين أو الكرم أو الشرف في العقل، أو الفعال الصالحة والحسب والكرم قد يكونان لمن لا آباء له شرفاء خلقه
Section on explaining who is most entitled to lead the prayer, and on explaining the order of rows. When a group gathers and there is no owner of the house in which they gather, nor is there among them a functionary (i.e., the imam of the locality) nor a ruler (like an amir, governor, or judge), then the most knowledgeable of the rulings of prayer, the one who preserves what is needed for the sunnah recitation, and avoids manifest indecencies, even if he is not versed in other sciences, is most entitled to lead. When they gather, precedence is given to the sultan, then the amir, then the judge, then the owner of the house (even a tenant is given precedence over the owner), and the judge is given precedence over the imam of the mosque due to what has come in the hadith: 'A man should not lead in his own domain, nor sit in his house on his special carpet except with his permission.' Then the best reciter (i.e., the most knowledgeable of the rulings of recitation, not just mere memorization without that). Then the most pious (piety is avoiding ambiguities; it is higher than taqwa because taqwa is avoiding prohibitions). Then the eldest in age (due to his saying: 'Let the older of you lead you'). Then the best in character (i.e., affability among people). Then the best in face (i.e., the most beaming, because good appearance indicates good inner character, as it increases people's desire for congregation). Then the noblest in lineage (out of respect and honor). Then the best in voice (due to the desire to hear him). His saying (regarding 'the most knowledgeable'): Fiqh is needed for all pillars, obligations, sunan, and recommended acts. His saying: 'Precedence is given to the sultan' appears to be obligatory because if someone else precedes him, it is an insult to him and a violation of what is prohibited in the hadith. And you have seen what is in al-Binaya. His saying: 'A man should not lead in his own domain' means in the manifestation of his authority and place of jurisdiction. His saying: 'on his special carpet' (with fatha on the ta and kasra on the ra) is the bedding and the like that is spread for the owner of the house and is specific to him; it is also said it means the dining table. His saying: '(i.e., the most knowledgeable of the rulings of recitation)' regarding stopping, starting, and the manner of pronouncing letters and what pertains to them – as in Miskin and al-Qahistani. And it seems that one who performs recitation well, even if he does not know its rulings, is in the ruling of a knowledgeable person. His saying: 'not just mere memorization' means good memorization or more, as he said. His saying: 'without that' means without the complete knowledgeable person derived from his saying 'the most knowledgeable.' His saying: 'then the eldest' what is meant by al-asan is the one who embraced Islam earliest, as indicated previously in the hadith: 'If they are equal in hijrah, then the one who accepted Islam earliest.' So an old man who accepted Islam later is not given precedence over a youth raised in Islam – as in al-Nahr. And in it is that it misses pointing out the rank of age, so some made the rank of earliest in Islam before the rank of age, making them two ranks – and that is good. His saying: 'Let the older of you lead you' – he said this to Malik ibn al-Huwayrith and his companion (his cousin) when he intended to travel; its wording: 'When the prayer time comes, call the adhan, then establish the iqamah, and let the older of you lead you' – agreed upon. His saying: '(i.e., affability)' this is an interpretation by implication, for whoever has good affability, people gather around him and the congregation multiplies. The author followed in giving precedence to good character over good face in Mawahib al-Rahman and Fath al-Qadir; the opposite of that is held by the author of al-Khulasah, al-Ghurar, and Miskin, because the apparent is the first thing perceived of perfections, or because it is like evidence for it (the inner), as the apparent is the title of the inner. His saying: '(indicates good inner character)' – i.e., generally, and he interpreted it in al-Kafi as 'most prayer at night,' and the hadith: 'Whoever prays much at night will have a good face during the day' has not been confirmed by hadith scholars, like the hadith: 'Whoever prays behind a knowledgeable, pious imam is as if he prayed behind a Prophet.' His saying: 'because...' etc. – it is better to add the waw because it is suitable as an independent cause. His saying: 'then the noblest in lineage' – some give precedence to the one with greater hasab over it. Hasab is honor of forefathers, or wealth, or religion, or generosity, or nobility in intellect, or good deeds. Hasab and karam may be found in one who has no noble forefathers – his character.
Source pages p. 299

Commentary
This passage is a detailed exposition of the order of precedence for leading congregational prayer in the Hanafi school. It begins by stating that if there is no owner of the house, no official imam, and no ruler, then the most knowledgeable of the rulings of prayer, who memorizes enough for the sunnah recitation and avoids manifest sins, is preferred. Then it gives the general order: first the sultan, then the amir, then the judge, then the house owner (even a tenant over the landlord), then the judge over the mosque imam. After these, the list continues: the best reciter (who knows the rules of recitation, not just quantity), then the most pious (avoiding ambiguities), then the eldest (in age, but actually earliest in Islam as per hadith), then the best character (affability), then the best face (indicating good inner state), then the noblest lineage, then the best voice. The commentary clarifies each point, such as that fiqh knowledge is essential for all aspects of prayer, and that giving precedence to the ruler is obligatory to avoid insult. It also notes an internal Hanafi dispute: some (like the author of al-Khulasah) prefer good character over good face, while the main text gives good character first. The passage reinforces the Hanafi principle that the imam should be chosen for religious and moral qualities, not worldly status, but rulers have precedence due to their general authority.

Key Terms
الأعلم (al-a'lam): The most knowledgeable person in fiqh rulings of prayer, including conditions, integrals, and invalidators.
الأقرأ (al-aqra'): The best reciter, meaning most knowledgeable in the rules of tajweed, stops, and starts, not merely one who memorizes the most.
الأورع (al-awra'): The most pious, avoiding doubtful matters (shubuhat), which is considered higher than taqwa (avoiding prohibitions).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, when a ruler (sultan) is present in a congregation, what is the ruling regarding his precedence?
A) It is recommended (sunnah) to give him precedence.
B) It is obligatory (wajib) to give him precedence.
C) The most knowledgeable should lead regardless.
D) The house owner should lead.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi order for imamah begins with rulers (wajib precedence), then the most knowledgeable in fiqh, followed by recitation, piety, precedence in Islam, character, face, lineage, and voice.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
8 min
Qualifications for Leading Prayer (Imamah) in Hanafi Fiqh
Hashiya expanding rulings on precedence in imamah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi hierarchy of imamah qualifications, explain the basis and proof for each, and evaluate the intra-Hanafi dispute between good character and good appearance.

Core Idea
The imam's character takes precedence over appearance; the sultan's right to lead is wajib.

Choosing the right imam for prayer is both a spiritual and social matter. The Hanafi school provides a detailed hierarchy that balances authority, knowledge, piety, and character. This lesson unpacks that hierarchy, its proofs, and a notable internal debate over the priority of character versus appearance.

Guided Path
1
Identify the overall hierarchy
Listen the sequence: sultan → amir → qadi → house owner (even tenant) → most Quranically knowledgeable → most scrupulous → earliest in Islam → best character → best appearance → noblest lineage → best voice → then secondary traits.
The sultan's precedence is wajib; others are sunnah muakkadah.
2
Analyze each key qualification
For each, note the definition and the proof (dalil). For example, 'al-aqra' means knowledge of recitation rules, not mere memorization; 'al-asann' is earliest Islam, not age; 'ahsan khuluq' is affability attracting congregation.
The hadith 'Let the older of you lead' is interpreted as earliest Islam.
3
Examine the intra-Hanafi dispute
Compare the two views on the order of husn al-khuluq and husn al-wajh. The relied-upon view places character first; the opposing view places appearance first. Understand each proof: character for unity, appearance as evidence of inner virtue.
Al-Tahtawi follows Maraqi in preferring character.
4
Note additional and secondary qualifications
Review the traits listed after voice: purest garment, best wife (chastity), largest head (no excess), smallest organ, most wealth (lawful), greatest status. These are less emphasized but part of the complete order.
Some scholars put matrilineal honor before lineage.
5
Apply the rules to resolve a scenario
Take a scenario with several candidates and determine who leads according to the hierarchy. Consider if the sultan is present, if qualities are equal, and the role of lot-drawing or congregation's choice.
If the congregation chooses a less qualified person, they do wrong but the prayer is valid.

الحديث من قوله : فإن كانوا في الهجرة سواء فأقدمهم إسلاماً فلا يقدم شيخ أسلم على شاب نشأ في الإسلام نهر، وفيه أنه يفوت التنبيه على مرتبة الأسن، ولذا جعل بعضهم رتبة الأقدم إسلاماً متقدمة على رتبة الأسن، وجعلهما مرتبتين وهو حسن قوله : (وليؤمكما أكبر كما قاله لمالك بن الحويرث ولصاحب له وهو ابن عمه حين أراد السفر ولفظه : إذا حضرت الصلاة فأذنا، ثم أقيما وليؤمكما أكبركما متفق عليه قوله : أي) ألفة بين الكرم أو الشرف في العقل، أو الفعال الصالحة والحسب والكرم قد يكونان لمن لا آباء له شرفاء خلقه للخضوع (ثم الأنظف ثوباً) لبعده عن الدنس ترغيباً فيه فالأحسن زوجة لشدة عفته فأكبرهم رأساً، وأصغرهم عضواً غير الأولى فقد أساؤا) ولكن لا يأثمون كذا في التجنيس، وفيه لو أم قوماً وهم له كارهون فهو على ثلاثة أوجه إن كانت الكراهة لفساد فيه أو كانوا أحق بالإمامة منه يكره، وإن كان هو أحق بها منهم ولا فساد ومع هذا يكرهونه لا يكره له التقدم لأنّ الجاهل والفاسق يكره العالم، والصالح وقال : إن سركم أن تقبل صلاتكم فليؤمكم علماؤكم فإنهم وفدكم فيما بينكم وبين فيه، والشرف والمجد لا يكونان إلا بهم قوله: (للخضوع) فإن الخضوع يكون عند سماع الصوت الحسن فهو مما يزيد القرآن حسناً . قوله : (ثم الأنظف ثوباً) وبخط الحموي الأفضل ثوباً وهو يرجع إلى كثرة ثمنه قوله: (فالأحسن زوجة أي عنده فيرجع إلى كونه أشد حباً فيها وعبر بالأحسن مريداً به كثرة الحب للتلازم بينهما غالباً فسقط ما في الشرح من قوله، ولو قيل: أشدهم حباً لزوجته لكان أظهر قوله: (فأكبرهم رأساً) أي كبراً غير فاحش وإلا كان منفراً. قوله: (وأصغرهم عضواً فسره بعض المشايخ بالأصغر ذكراً لأن كبره الفاحش يدل غالباً على دناءة الأصل ويحرر ومثل ذلك لا يعلم غالباً إلا بالاطلاع أو الأخبار وهو نادر، ويقال مثله في الأحسن زوجة المتقدم. قوله: (فأكثرهم مالا) لأنه لا ينظر إلى مال غيره وتقل أشغاله في الصلاة، وذلك لأن اعتبار هذا بعدما تقدم من الأوصاف كالورع فتأمل، ومنه يعلم أن المراد المال الحلال قوله : (فأكبرهم جاهاً وقدم بعضهم الأكثر حسباً على الأشرف نسباً، وهو يعم الأكثر مالاً والأكبر جاهاً، ويقدم الحر الأصلي على العتيق. فائدة: لا يقدم أحد في التزاحم إلا بمرجح ومنه السبق إلى الدرس والإفتاء والدعوى فإن استووا في المجيء أقرع بينهم در عن الأشباه . قال : وفي محاسن القراء لابن وهبان، وقيل: إن لم يكن للشيخ معلوم جاز أن يقدم من شاء وأكثر مشايخنا على تقديم الأسبق وأول من سنه ابن كثير اهـ. قوله : فالعبرة بما اختاره الأكثر ) قال في شرح المشكاة لعله محمول على الأكثر من العلماء إذا وجدوا وإلا فلا عبرة لكثرة الجاهلين قال تعالى: (ولكن أكثرهم لا يعلمون) [الزمر: ٣٩] . قوله : (أو كانوا أحق بالإمامة منه يكره) قال الحلبي : وينبغي أن تكون الكراهة تحريمية لخبر أبي داود ثلاثة لا يقبل الله منهم صلاة وعد منهم من تقدم قوماً وهم له کارهون قوله: (يكره العالم والصالح) يصح رجوع كل إلى كل قوله: (فإنهم وفدكم) الوفد مصدر وقد بمعنى قدم وورد والوافد السابق من الإبل قاموس وفي الشرح الوفود القوم يفدون إلى الملك بالحاجة والإرسال .اهـ. فالوفد بمعنى الوافد أي السابق والمعنى أنهم السابقون
And if they gather, the sultan is presented, then the amir, then the qadi, then the owner of the house, even if a tenant, he is presented over the owner, and the qadi is presented over the imam of the mosque due to what is narrated in the hadith. And a man should not lead prayer in his domain, nor sit in his house on his honorific cushion except with his permission. Then the most knowledgeable in recitation, meaning the most knowledgeable of the rulings of recitation, not mere abundance of memorization without that. Then the most scrupulous: scrupulousness is avoidance of doubts, higher than piety because it is avoidance of prohibitions. Then the oldest in Islam, due to his statement ﷺ: 'Let the older of you lead you.' Then the best in character, with dammah of kha and lam, meaning affability among people. Then the best in face, meaning the most handsome, because beauty of appearance indicates goodness of inner self, because it increases people's desire for congregation. Then the noblest in lineage, out of respect and honor for him. Then the best in voice, due to desire to hear him. And the jurist is needed for all pillars, obligations, sunnahs, and recommended acts. His statement: 'the sultan is presented' – apparently that is wajib because for another to precede him is an insult to him and committing the prohibited in the hadith, and you have known what is in al-Binaayah. His statement: 'a man should not lead in his domain' – meaning in the manifestation of his authority and the place of his jurisdiction. His statement: 'on his honorific cushion' – with fatha of the ta and kasr of the ra, the bed or similar spread for the owner of the house and specifically his. It is also said the table. His statement: 'meaning the most knowledgeable of the rulings of recitation' – concerning stop, connection, beginning, and the manner of pronouncing letters and related matters. Thus in Miskin and al-Qahistani. And apparently one who masters performance, even if he does not know its rulings, is in the ruling of the knowledgeable. His statement: 'not mere abundance of memorization' – meaning quality of memorization or the most, as in his statement: 'without that' – meaning without the complete scholar, derived from his statement 'the most knowledgeable'. His statement: 'then the oldest in Islam' – what is meant by the oldest is the earliest in Islam, evidenced by what preceded in the hadith: 'if they are equal in hijra, then the earliest in Islam'. So an old man who converted is not presented over a youth raised in Islam. In it there is that it misses alerting to the rank of old age in Islam, so some scholars made the rank of earliest Islam preceding the rank of old age, making them two ranks, which is good. His statement: 'Let the older of you lead you' – as he said to Malik ibn al-Huwayrith and his companion, his cousin, when he intended to travel. Its wording: 'When prayer is due, give the adhan, then iqamah, and let the older of you lead you' – agreed upon. His statement: 'meaning affability among people' – this is an interpretation by implication, because one of good character makes people friendly, so many congregation join him. The author followed in presenting good character before good face the Mawahib al-Rahman and Fath al-Qadir, while the opposite was followed by the author of al-Khulasa, al-Ghurr, and Miskin, because the apparent is first perceived of the qualities of perfection, or because it is evidence of the inner, as the apparent is the title of the inner. His statement: 'it indicates good inner self' – meaning usually, and he interpreted it in al-Kafi as most night prayer. And the hadith: 'Whoever increases night prayer, his face becomes beautiful by day' – the muhaddithun did not verify it, like the hadith: 'Whoever prays behind a God-fearing scholar, it is as if he prayed behind a prophet.' His statement: 'because' – it is better to add a waw to make it suitable for reasoning independently. His statement: 'then the noblest in lineage' – some scholars presented before it the one with more matrilineal honor, and matrilineal honor is honor of fathers, or wealth, or religion, or generosity, or honor in intellect, or righteous deeds. And matrilineal honor and generosity may exist for one without noble fathers. His character: then the purest in garment – because it is far from filth, encouraging it. Then the one with the best wife due to intense chastity. Then the one with the largest head, then the one with the smallest member, then the one with the most wealth, then the one with the greatest status. And there is disagreement concerning the traveler with the resident: some said they are equal, some said the resident is more entitled. Then if they are equal, they cast lots among them, and whoever's lot comes out is presented. Or the choice is up to the people. If they disagree, then the consideration is what the majority chooses. And if they present someone other than the most entitled, they have done wrong, but they do not sin. Thus in al-Tajnis. And in it: if a man leads a people while they dislike him, it is of three types: if the dislike is for corruption in him, or they are more entitled to the imamah than him, it is disliked. And if he is more entitled than them and there is no corruption, yet they dislike him, it is not disliked for him to come forward, because the ignorant and the corrupt dislike the scholar and the righteous. And he said: 'If you are pleased that your prayer be accepted, let your scholars lead you, for they are your deputies between you and Him.' And honor and glory are only with them. His statement: 'for submission' – submission occurs upon hearing the good voice, thus it increases the beauty of the Quran. His statement: 'then the purer in garment' – and in the handwriting of al-Hamawi: 'the better in garment', which refers to the abundance of its price. His statement: 'the one with the best wife' – i.e., in his view, which refers to his being most loving towards her, and he expressed as 'best' intending abundance of love, due to the necessary correlation between them mostly. So what is in the commentary from his statement 'if it were said: most loving of his wife it would be clearer' falls. His statement: 'the one with the largest head' – i.e., a largeness that is not excessive, otherwise it is repulsive. His statement: 'and the one with the smallest member' – some masters interpreted it as the smallest sexual organ, because its excessive largeness usually indicates baseness of origin, and such is not known usually except by inspection or reports, which is rare. And the like is said concerning the one with the best wife mentioned earlier. His statement: 'the one with the most wealth' because he does not look at others' wealth and his preoccupations in prayer are fewer, and that is because considering this after previous attributes like scrupulousness of questionable things. So contemplate, and from it it is known that what is meant is lawful wealth. His statement: 'then the one with the greatest status' – and some scholars presented the one with more matrilineal honor before the noblest in lineage, and it includes the one with more wealth and the one with greater status. And the free-born is presented over the freed slave. Benefit: No one is given precedence in competition except with a preponderant, and from that is precedence in lesson, fatwa, and lawsuit. If they are equal in coming, lots are cast among them. Quoted from al-Ashbah. He said: And in Mahasin al-Qurra by Ibn Wahban: And it was said: If the teacher has no fixed salary, it is permissible to give precedence to whomever he wishes. And most of our masters are upon giving precedence to the earliest, and the first to legislate it was Ibn Kathir, end. His statement: 'consideration is what the majority chooses' – said in Sharh al-Mishkat: perhaps it is carried upon the majority of scholars if they are present, otherwise there is no consideration for the abundance of the ignorant, as He said: 'But most of them do not know' [Az-Zumar: 39]. His statement: 'or they are more entitled to the imamah from him, it is disliked' – al-Halabi said: It should be that the disapproval is tahrimi (prohibitively disliked) due to the narration of Abu Dawud: 'Three people whose prayer Allah does not accept: one who leads a people while they dislike him.' His statement: 'the scholar and the righteous are disliked' – it is correct that each refers to each. His statement: 'for they are your deputies' – al-wafd is a verbal noun meaning arrival, and the wafid is the one preceding from camels. In the commentary: al-wufud are the people who come to the ruler with a need and message. end. So al-wafd means the wafid, i.e., the preceding one, and the meaning is that they are the preceding ones.
Source pages p. 300

Commentary
This passage from Hashiya al-Tahtawi is a detailed commentary on the rules of precedence in leading prayer (imamah) within the Hanafi school. It expands on the base text of Maraqi al-Falah, clarifying each qualification and resolving scholarly differences.

The passage begins by establishing the hierarchy of authority: when several qualified persons are present, the sultan (ruler) takes precedence, then the amir (governor), then the qadi (judge), then the owner of the house, even if a tenant—the tenant is preferred over the actual owner because the house is under his control. The qadi is preferred over the regular imam of the mosque because of the hadith forbidding a man to lead in his own domain of authority. The commentator clarifies that the precedence of the sultan is considered wajib (obligatory), as allowing another to lead him would be an insult and a violation of the prohibition in the hadith.

Next, the passage lists the personal qualifications for imamah in order:
1. Al-aqra' (most knowledgeable): The one with the deepest understanding of the rules of Quranic recitation, including correct pronunciation, stops, and starts. This is not mere memorization without understanding.
2. Al-awra' (most scrupulous): The one who avoids doubtful matters; this is higher than taqwa (piety, which only avoids clear prohibitions).
3. Al-asann (oldest in Islam): This is interpreted as the one with the earliest conversion to Islam, not necessarily the oldest in age. The commentator references the hadith from Malik ibn al-Huwayrith: "Let the older of you lead you," and explains that when hijra (migration) is equal, precedence goes to the one with the earliest Islam.
4. Ahsan khuluq (best character): Character that fosters affability and unity among people. The commentator notes a dispute: the author (Maraqi) follows Mawahib al-Rahman and Fath al-Qadir in placing this before good appearance, while others (al-Khulasa, al-Ghurr, Miskin) reverse the order, arguing that the apparent (face) is the first sign of perfection.
5. Ahsan wajh (best face): Beauty of countenance, which generally indicates a good inner self, as it attracts people to the congregation.
6. Ashraf nasab (noblest lineage): To show respect. Some scholars present "akthar hasab" (greater ancestral honor) before this.
7. Ahsan sawt (best voice): Because it enhances the beauty of Quran recitation and induces humility.

Additional qualifications from the commentary include: the purest garment, the one with the best wife (indicating strong marital chastity and love), largest head (not excessively), smallest private part, most wealth (lawful), and greatest status. These are considered after the primary qualities.

The passage then addresses cases of equality: if two candidates are equal, lots are drawn, or the choice is left to the congregation. If they choose someone less qualified, they have done wrong but do not sin. For a traveler versus a resident, there is disagreement: some say equal, others prefer the resident.

Finally, the passage discusses the ruling when the congregation dislikes the imam. If the dislike is due to corruption in the imam or because others are more entitled, it is makruh tahrimi (prohibitively disliked) for him to lead. But if he is more entitled and there is no corruption, yet they dislike him, it is not disliked for him to come forward, as ignorant people may dislike the scholar out of jealousy. The hadith from Abu Dawud is cited: "Three people whose prayer Allah does not accept: one who leads a people while they dislike him." The commentator clarifies that this applies when the dislike is justified.

Key Terms
الأقرأ (al-aqra'): The one with the most knowledge of the rules of Quranic recitation, including stop, start, and proper articulation, not merely the most memorization.
الورع (al-wara'): Abstaining from doubtful matters (shubhat), considered higher than taqwa (piety) because it involves avoiding permissible but ambiguous things.
الأسن (al-asann): The one with the earliest acceptance of Islam, not necessarily the oldest in age, as per the context of the hadith.
حسن الخلق (husn al-khuluq): Good character that fosters affability and harmony among people, leading to a larger congregation.
حسن الوجه (husn al-wajh): Beauty of face, considered an outward sign of inner goodness (حسن السريرة) in most cases.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, when a sultan, a qadi, and an imam of a mosque are all present for prayer, who should lead?
A) The imam of the mosque
B) The qadi
C) The sultan
D) The one with the loudest voice

Key Takeaway
The order of imamah blends authority and piety; the mufta bihi position prioritizes character over appearance.

Order of Preference for Selecting an Imam
Criteria for imam preference and handling equality.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi order of preference for choosing an imam and explain the procedure when candidates are equally qualified.

Core Idea
The most qualified imam is preferred; if equal, lots are drawn or the majority chooses.

In congregational prayer, the choice of imam carries spiritual significance. The Hanafi school outlines a clear hierarchy of preferred qualities. This lesson covers that hierarchy and the rules for resolving ties among candidates.

Guided Path
1
Identify the primary criterion: humility
The first quality mentioned is al-khudūʿ (humility). This is the foundation for valid leadership in prayer.
Humility here implies devotion and mindfulness in the prayer.
2
List the subsequent qualities in order
The order is: cleaner clothes (symbolizing purity), a virtuous wife (indicating chastity), larger head, smaller limbs, wealth, and social status.
Physical features reflect the customs of the time; today, the emphasis is on knowledge and piety.
3
Apply the rule for equality
If two candidates are equal, they draw lots. Alternatively, the choice is left to the congregation; if they differ, the majority view prevails.
Lots are used to avoid conflict and ensure fairness.
4
Understand the consequence of choosing a less deserving imam
The congregation has done wrong (asā'ū) but does not sin (lā ya'thamūn). The act is makruh tanzihi, not sinful.
This encourages following the preferred order without burdening the congregation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
للخضوع (ثم الأنظف ثوباً) لبعده عن الدنس ترغيباً فيه فالأحسن زوجة لشدة عفته فأكبرهم رأساً، وأصغرهم عضواً فأكثرهم مالاً فأكبرهم جاهاً، واختلف في المسافر مع المقيم قيل: هما سواء، وقيل المقيم أولى فإن استووا يقرع بينهم فمن خرجت قرعته قدم أو الخيار إلى القوم فإن اختلفوا فالعبرة بما اختاره الأكثر، وإن قدموا غير الأولى فقد أساؤا ولكن لا يأثمون كذا في التجنيس، وفيه لو أم قوماً وهم له كارهون فهو على ثلاثة أوجه إن كانت الكراهة لفساد فيه أو كانوا أحق بالإمامة منه يكره، وإن كان هو أحق بها منهم ولا فساد ومع هذا يكرهونه لا يكره له التقدم لأنّ الجاهل والفاسق يكره العالم والصالح وقال : إن سركم أن تقبل صلاتكم فليؤمكم علماؤكم فإنهم وفدكم فيما بينكم وبين ربكم وفي رواية فليؤمكم خياركم
For humility (then the one with cleaner clothes) because of distance from filth as an encouragement. Then the one with the best wife due to strong chastity. Then the one with the largest head, then the one with the smallest limb, then the one with the most wealth, then the one with the greatest status. There is a difference regarding the traveler with the resident: some say they are equal, some say the resident is better. If they are equal, they draw lots; whoever's lot comes out is put forward. Or the choice is left to the people; if they differ, consideration is given to what the majority chooses. If they put forward someone who is not the most deserving, they have done wrong but do not sin. Similarly in al-Tajnīs. Regarding one who leads a people while they dislike him, it is of three types: if the dislike is due to corruption in him or they are more deserving of the imamate than him, it is disliked; if he is more deserving than them and there is no corruption, and despite this they dislike him, it is not disliked for him to lead because the ignorant and the sinful dislike the scholar and righteous person. And he said: If you wish that your prayer be accepted, let your scholars lead you, for they are your delegates between you and your Lord. And in a narration: let your best ones lead you.
Source pages p. 301

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement on the order of preference for choosing an imam. It lists criteria: first, the one with the most humility; then cleaner clothes; then one with a good wife (indicating strong chastity); then physical features like largest head and smallest limb; then wealth; then status. It then addresses cases of equality: drawing lots or leaving choice to the congregation. If the majority chooses someone less deserving, they have done wrong but are not sinful. The passage then discusses three scenarios regarding an imam who is disliked by the congregation: if the dislike is due to corruption in him or the congregation is more deserving, it is disliked for him to lead; if he is more deserving and there is no corruption, it is not disliked for him to lead despite their dislike. The hadith encourages following scholars and the best among the community.

Key Terms
إمامة (imāmah): The act of leading congregational prayer.
كراهة (karāhah): Dislike, categorized into tanzihi (avoiding better) and tahrimi (prohibitively disliked).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

C) The wealthier one leads.
D) The congregation votes, and majority decides.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school prescribes a clear order of preference for imam and uses lots to resolve ties; deviating is wrong but not sinful.

Rulings When an Imam Is Disliked by the Congregation
Scenarios of disliked imam and ruling.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the three scenarios regarding an imam whom the congregation dislikes and state whether his leading is disliked or not in each case.

Core Idea
If dislike is due to the imam's corruption or the congregation being more deserving, leading is disliked; if he is more deserving, it is not.

The congregation's perception of the imam matters, but not all dislike renders the imamate invalid. The Hanafi school distinguishes three cases based on the reason for dislike and the imam's qualification. This lesson explains those distinctions.

Guided Path
1
Understand the three types of dislike
The text presents three types: (1) dislike due to corruption (fisād) in the imam, (2) congregation is more deserving of imamate, (3) imam is more deserving but the congregation dislikes him anyway.
The first two cases make leading disliked; the third does not.
2
Determine the ruling for each type
For case 1 and 2: it is makruh (disliked) for him to lead. For case 3: it is not disliked; he should lead despite their dislike.
The reasoning: the ignorant and sinful dislike the scholar and righteous person.
3
Apply the prophetic guidance
The hadith urges letting scholars and the best lead; this supports case 3 where the qualified imam should not step down due to unfounded dislike.
The hadith is cited as a general principle.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

Checkpoint

An imam's leading is disliked only if the congregation's dislike is based on valid religious grounds; otherwise, he should lead despite their feelings.

intermediate

Imamate of a Slave, Blind, Bedouin, Illegitimate Child, and Sinner
States exceptions and conditions for imamate of certain categories

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the imamate of a slave, blind person, bedouin, illegitimate child, and open sinner, and identify the condition that changes the ruling from disliked to permissible.

Core Idea
Imamate is disliked only due to deficiency in knowledge or piety, not inherent attributes.

This passage from Hashiyat al-Tahtawi clarifies the ruling on imamate for certain individuals often questioned for their personal status. The key principle is that dislike (karahah) attaches to deficiencies in knowledge and piety, not to being a slave, blind, bedouin, or illegitimate child. If such a person is more qualified than alternatives, their imamate is not disliked and may even be preferred.

Guided Path
1
Identify the default ruling
For each category (slave, blind, bedouin, illegitimate child, fasiq), note that the text states 'كره' (disliked). Determine the level of karahah — here it is tanzihi (makruh tanzih) unless otherwise specified.
Halawi notes that for the fasiq, some later scholars consider it makruh tahrimi.
2
Examine the reason for dislike
For the blind, the reason is inability to find qibla and protect clothes from filth. For the bedouin and illegitimate child, the reason is ignorance (lack of knowledge) and lack of piety. For the slave, it is lack of knowledge and piety (if not qualified). For the fasiq, it is lack of religious concern despite knowledge.
The reason is always a deficiency in knowledge or piety, not the status itself.
3
Recognize the exception
The passage explicitly states: 'if there is no one better than him, there is no dislike.' Also, if the individual is more knowledgeable and pious than alternatives, the ruling is reversed. For example, if a blind person is more pious than a sighted person, the blind person's imamate is preferred.
This is a key principle: relative merit overrides default dislike.
4
Apply the principle to the fasiq
The fasiq is disliked even if knowledgeable because his lack of religious concern (عدم اهتمامه) is a deficiency in piety. The text does not mention an exception for the fasiq being better, implying the dislike is stronger (possibly tahrimi).
This is consistent with the idea that fasiq's sinfulness harms others' prayer.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وكره إمامة العبد إن لم يكن عالماً تقياً (والأعمى) لعدم اهتدائه إلى القبلة وصون ثيابه عن الدنس، وإن لم يوجد أفضل منه، فلا كراهة (والإعرابي) الجاهل، أو الحضري الجاهل وولد الزنا) الذي لا علم عنده ولا تقوى، فلذا قيده قبله بقوله (الجاهل) إذ لو كان عالماً تقياً لا تكره إمامته لأنّ الكراهة للنقائص حتى إذا كان الإعرابي أفضل من الحضري والعبد من الحر، وولد الزنا من ولد الرشد، والأعمى من البصير، فالحكم بالضد كذا في الاختيار (و) لذا كره إمامة (الفاسق) العالم لعدم اهتمامه
And the imamate of a slave is disliked if he is not knowledgeable and pious (and the blind) because he cannot find the qibla and protect his clothes from filth, and if there is no one better than him, there is no dislike. (And the bedouin) ignorant, or the city-dweller ignorant, and the illegitimate child who has no knowledge and no piety. Therefore he qualified it earlier with his statement 'the ignorant', because if he were knowledgeable and pious, his imamate would not be disliked, because dislike is for deficiencies. So if the bedouin is better than the city-dweller, or the slave better than the free, or the illegitimate child better than the legitimate, or the blind better than the sighted, then the ruling is the opposite. Similarly in al-Ikhtiyar. (And) therefore the imamate of the open sinner who is knowledgeable is disliked due to his lack of care.
Source pages p. 302

Commentary
This passage clarifies rulings regarding the imamate of specific individuals: a slave (if not knowledgeable and pious), a blind person (due to difficulty finding qibla and avoiding filth), a bedouin (ignorant), an illegitimate child (ignorant), and a fasiq (open sinner). The key principle is that the dislike is due to deficiencies in knowledge or piety, not due to inherent attributes. Therefore, if a slave, blind person, bedouin, or illegitimate child is actually more knowledgeable and pious than the available alternatives, their imamate is not disliked and even preferable. The dislike for the fasiq remains even if knowledgeable because of lack of religious concern. The passage emphasizes that rulings are contextual and based on relative merit.

Key Terms
فاسق (fāsiq): An open sinner, one who commits major sins or persists on minor sins without repentance.
ولد الزنا (walad al-zinā): A child born out of wedlock.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, when is the imamate of a blind person not disliked?
A) If he has a guide to help him find the qibla.
B) If no better imam is available.
C) If he is wealthy.
D) If he is a free man.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi ruling on imamate is based on relative merit in knowledge and piety, not on personal status; defaults are lifted when the individual is the best available.

Disliked Imams in Congregational Prayer: Categories and Conditions
Rulings on disliked imams with conditions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions under which praying behind a slave, blind person, bedouin, or child of adultery is disliked, and identify when the ruling reverses.

Core Idea
Dislike in imamah arises from deficiencies; if the supposedly lowly imam is actually more virtuous, he is preferred.

This passage from Hashiyat al-Tahtawi clarifies the Hanafi rulings on who is disliked to lead congregational prayer. The text lists categories such as slaves, blind persons, bedouins, and children of adultery, emphasizing that the dislike is not intrinsic but contingent on ignorance or lack of piety. Understanding these conditions helps in selecting the best imam.

Guided Path
1
Identify the categories
List the categories of imams stated as disliked: slave, blind, bedouin (and city-dweller ignorant), child of adultery.
The text also mentions the sinful (fasiq) and innovator (mubtadi'), but we cover those in a separate lesson.
2
Note the condition for each category
For the slave: unless he is knowledgeable and pious. For the blind: due to difficulty in finding qibla and keeping clothes clean. For the bedouin and walad zina: due to ignorance.
The condition for the blind is waived if no better imam exists.
3
Understand the governing principle
Dislike is due to deficiency. If the imam is actually more virtuous (e.g., a knowledgeable slave vs. an ignorant free man), the ruling reverses.
The principle 'al-umur bi-maqasidiha' applies: the intention and actual virtue matter.
4
Apply the principle to the blind
The text cites that the Prophet appointed blind companions as governors, showing no dislike when no better imam exists.
This shows the dislike is tanzihi (non-prohibitive) and conditional.
5
Recognize the overall rule
The dislike for these categories is makruh tanzihi when a better imam is available; otherwise no dislike.
The hadith 'Let the best among you lead' supports choosing the most qualified.

ذلك بأن كان عالماً تقياً فلا كراة قوله : ( لعدم إهتدائه إلخ) هذا يقتضي كراهة إمامة الأعشى نهر وهو الذي لا يبصر ليلا. قوله: (وصون ثيابه عطف على اهتدائه أي ولعدم صونه ثيابه الخ. قوله : (فلا كراهة) لاستخلاف النبي ابن أم مكتوم، وعتبان بن مالك على المدينة حين خرج إلى غزوة تبوك وكانا أعمين. قوله : ( والأعرابي) بفتح الهمزة نسبة إلى الأعراب وهم سكان البادية من العرب وعمم الأزهري، والعرب العاربة هم الخلص منهم وهم الذين تكلموا بلغة يعرب بن قحطان ، وهو اللسان القديم لأنه أول من تكلم بالعربية والعرب المستعربة الذين تكلموا بلسان اسمعيل عليه السلام وهو لغة أهل الحجاز وما والاها والمراد هنا كل من سكن البادية عربياً كان أو أعجمياً كالتركمان والأكراد لغلبة الجهل عليهم لبعدهم عن مجالس العلم، ومن ثمة قيل أهل أهل القبور وهذا ظاهر في كراهة العامي الذي لا علم عنده كما في البحر والنهر، وحكى أن أعرابياً إقتدى بإمام فقرأ الإمام آية الأعراب أشد كفراً ونفاقاً فضربه الأعرابي وشج رأسه، ثم اقتدى به بعد مدة فرآه الإمام فقرأ آية ومن الأعراب من يؤمن بالله واليوم إلا آخر الآن نفعك العصا كذا في غاية البيان قوله بتقديمه للإمامة، وإذا تعذر منعه ينتقل عنه إلى غير مسجده للجمعة وغيرها وإن لم يقم الجمعة إلا هو تصلي معه (والمبتدع) بارتكابه ما أحدث على خلاف الحق المتلقى عن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم: من علم أو عمل أو مال بنوع شبهة، أو استحسان وروى محمد عن أبي حنيفة رحمه الله تعالى وأبي يوسف أن الصلاة خلف أهل الأهواء لا تجوز والصحيح أنها تصح مع الكراهة خلف من لا تكفره بدعته، لقوله : صلوا خلف كل بر وفاجر وصلوا على كل بر وفاجر وجاهدوا مع كل بر وفاجر» رواه الدارقطني كما في البرهان وقال في مجمع الروايات وإذا صلى خلف فاسق، أو مبتدع يكون محرزاً ثواب الجماعة لكن لا ينال ثواب من يصلي خلف إمام تقي (و) كره للإمام لعدم علمه بأحكام الصلاة قوله : (و) كره للإمام (المف) وقوله : (و) كره لإمامة (؟) ... على الصلاة خلف أمرد وسفيه ومفلوج، وأبرص شاع برصه ومراء ومتصنع ومجذوم، ولا خلف من أم بأجرة على
Your Lord, and in another narration: 'Let the best among you lead you in prayer.' Disliked is the imamah of a slave unless he is knowledgeable and pious; (the blind) because he cannot find the direction of the qibla nor keep his clothes clean, and if there is no one better than him, then there is no dislike; (the bedouin) the ignorant, or the city-dweller ignorant, and the child of adultery who has no knowledge nor piety. So he qualified it earlier with his saying 'the ignorant', because if he were knowledgeable and pious, his imamah would not be disliked, because the dislike is due to deficiencies. So if the bedouin is better than the city-dweller, and the slave better than the free, and the child of adultery better than the legitimate child, and the blind better than the sighted, then the ruling is the opposite. Thus in al-Ikhtiyar. (And) therefore disliked is the imamah of (the sinful person) even if learned, because he does not care... to Allah so that they may attain their needs and intercede for you, or in the sense of delegations, i.e., messengers between you and your Lord, and the speech is metaphorical. He said: (And disliked is the imamah of the slave and likewise the freed slave as in al-Durr due to prevalence of ignorance, and al-Hamawi stated that the dislike of following a slave and what is attached to it is tanzihi (disliked but not sinful) if there is someone else, otherwise no dislike, end. From the commentary of al-Sayyid, and later it will come that the imamah of a sinful person is makruh tahriman. He said: (If he is not knowledgeable and pious) he pointed thereby that the dislike regarding slaves is not due to their essence but because they are busy serving their master and do not have time for knowledge, so ignorance prevails among them, and due to rarity of piety among slaves. So if that is absent, i.e., he is knowledgeable and pious, then no dislike. He said: (From lack of guidance etc.) This necessitates dislike of imamah of the one who is blind at night (a'sha). He said: (And keeping his clothes clean) is conjunct to 'his guidance', meaning and due to his failure to keep his clothes clean etc. He said: (So no dislike) because the Prophet appointed Ibn Umm Maktum and 'Itban ibn Malik over Medina when he went out to the expedition of Tabuk, and they were blind. He said: (And the bedouin) with fatha on the hamza, relative to the bedouins, who are the desert-dwelling Arabs, and al-Azhari generalized; the pure Arabs (Arab 'aribah) are the pure ones who spoke the language of Ya'rub bin Qahtan, which is the ancient tongue because he was the first to speak Arabic; and the Arabized Arabs (Arab musta'ribah) who spoke the tongue of Isma'il (peace be upon him), which is the language of the Hijaz and its environs. What is meant here is everyone who lives in the desert, whether Arab or non-Arab like Turkomans and Kurds, due to the prevalence of ignorance among them because of their distance from gatherings of knowledge. Hence it was said: 'People of graves'. This is apparent in the dislike of the imamah of the commoner who has no knowledge, as in al-Bahr and al-Nahr. And it is narrated that a bedouin followed an imam, and the imam recited the verse 'The bedouins are the most severe in disbelief and hypocrisy', so the bedouin struck him and wounded his head. Then later he followed him again, and the imam recited the verse 'And among the bedouins are those who believe in Allah and the Last Day' to the end; the bedouin said: 'The stick benefited you now.' As mentioned in Ghayat al-Bayan. He said: (And the child of adultery) because he has no father... the ungrateful ones. So the bedouin said: 'It teaches him, so ignorance prevails over him.' If he had knowledge, there would be no dislike. Al-'Ayni chose the reasoning that people shun him because he is accused, and it was affirmed in al-Nahr. Based on this, dislike should be established absolutely if he is not ignorant. He said: (So he qualified it etc.) i.e., because of what he qualified with in his saying 'knowledgeable', and regarding the blind by his saying 'and if there is no one better than him, then no dislike', and regarding the bedouin by his saying 'the ignorant', and regarding the child of adultery by his saying 'who has no knowledge'. There is reflection regarding the blind. He said: (If any of those mentioned... then the ruling is the opposite) So dislike is for presenting the city-dweller and free, and the legitimate child and sighted, due to their ignorance, because the imamah of the ignorant is disliked in any case. ... due to religion, so it is obligatory to humiliate him legally, so he is not honored by being put forward for imamah. If preventing him is difficult, one should move away from him to another mosque for Friday and other prayers, even if Friday prayer is not established except with him, then you pray with him. (And the innovator) by committing what he innovates contrary to the truth received from the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him), in knowledge, action, or wealth, due to some kind of doubt or istihsan. Muhammad narrated from Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf that prayer behind people of desires is not permissible. The correct view is that it is valid with dislike behind one whose innovation does not render him a disbeliever, due to his saying: 'Pray behind every righteous and sinful person, and pray over every righteous and sinful person, and strive with every righteous and sinful person.' Narrated by al-Daraqutni as in al-Burhan. And he said in Majma' al-Riwayat: If one prays behind a sinful person or an innovator, he attains the reward of congregation but does not attain the reward of one who prays behind a pious imam. (And) disliked for the imam due to his lack of knowledge of the rulings of prayer. He said: (And) disliked for the imam (al-muff?) And he said: (And) disliked for imamah (?) ... upon prayer behind a beardless youth, a foolish person, a paralyzed person, a leper whose leprosy is notorious, a hypocritical person, an affected person, a leprous person, and not behind one who leads for a fee.
Source pages p. 302

Commentary
This passage from Hashiyat al-Tahtawi on Maraqi al-Falah is a critical refinement of the rulings on who is disliked (makruh) to lead congregational prayer. The text opens by citing a hadith that the best among you should lead. It then lists categories: a slave (unless knowledgeable and pious), a blind person (due to inability to find qibla and keep clothes clean), a bedouin (ignorant), a city-dweller ignorant, and a child of adultery (with no knowledge or piety). The key principle is: dislike arises from deficiencies; if the person is actually more virtuous than others, the ruling reverses. For the blind, if no better imam exists, there is no dislike, as evidenced by the Prophet appointing blind companions as governors. For the bedouin and child of adultery, dislike is conditional on ignorance; if they are knowledgeable, no dislike. A story illustrates the bedouin's ignorance. The text then covers the sinful person (fasiq): his imamah is disliked tahriman (prohibitively) because he must be humiliated, not honored. If possible, one should switch mosques. For the innovator (mubtadi'), there is an intra-Hanafi dispute: Muhammad and Abu Yusuf narrate that prayer behind such is invalid, but the relied-upon (sahih) position is that it is valid with dislike, as long as the innovation does not amount to disbelief. A hadith 'Pray behind every righteous and sinful person' supports this. However, the reward is less than behind a pious imam. The passage ends by listing other disliked imams: beardless youth, foolish, paralyzed, leprous, hypocritical, affected, and those who lead for a fee. The overall ruling is that imamah of these persons is disliked when better alternatives exist; otherwise, no dislike. The hashiya clarifies the conditions and balances hadith evidence with rational principles like istihsan.

Key Terms
كراهة تنزيهية (karahah tanzihiyyah): Dislike that is not prohibited; it is better to avoid but not sinful.
فاسق (fasiq): One who commits major sins or persists on minor sins, without valid interpretation.
مبتدع (mubtadi'): One who innovates in religion something contrary to the received truth, whether in knowledge, action, or wealth, based on doubt or istihsan.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, when is the imamah of a blind person disliked?
A) Always disliked, regardless of circumstances.
B) Disliked only if he cannot find the qibla and keep clothes clean, and a better imam exists.
C) Never disliked because the Prophet appointed blind imams.
D) Disliked only if he is also a fasiq.

Key Takeaway
The dislike for a slave, blind, bedouin, or child of adultery as imam is conditional on ignorance or the availability of a better imam.

The Ruling on Praying Behind a Fasiq and Mubtadi'
Critical refinement on fasiq and mubtadi' imamah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi ruling on praying behind a fasiq and mubtadi', including the degree of dislike and the intra-Hanafi dispute on the innovator.

Core Idea
The imamah of a fasiq is prohibitively disliked and must be avoided; that of a mubtadi' is valid with dislike, as per the relied-upon view.

This passage continues with the rulings on two serious categories: the open sinner (fasiq) and the religious innovator (mubtadi'). The Hanafi school holds that praying behind a fasiq is makruh tahrimi, requiring one to seek another mosque. For the mubtadi', there is a disagreement between the two senior disciples and Imam Abu Hanifa, with the latter's view becoming the fatwa. Understanding this distinction is crucial for community practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling for fasiq
The text states that imamah of a fasiq (even if learned) is disliked tahriman (prohibitively), because it is obligatory to humiliate him, not honor him.
This is a stronger degree of dislike than the previous categories.
2
Understand the practical consequence
If possible, one should move to another mosque for Friday and other prayers. If no other option, the prayer is still valid but disliked.
The community should not honor a fasiq by putting him forward.
3
Analyze the ruling for mubtadi'
The text mentions an intra-Hanafi dispute: Muhammad and Abu Yusuf narrate that prayer behind people of desires (ahl al-ahwa) is not permissible. The correct (sahih) view is that it is valid with dislike if the innovation does not amount to disbelief.
This is based on the hadith 'Pray behind every righteous and sinful person.'
4
Evaluate the evidence
The hadith is quoted: 'Sallu khalfa kulli birrin wa fajir...' which indicates permissibility, but the Hanafi school adds dislike for the fasiq and innovator based on other evidence.
The hadith is zanni in both transmission and meaning.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position is that prayer behind an innovator (whose innovation is not kufr) is valid with dislike, but the reward is less than behind a pious imam.
This is the view taken by later Hanafi authorities.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
