وولد الزنا) الذي لا علم عنده ولا تقوى، فلذا قيده قبله بقوله (الجاهل) إذ لو كان عالماً تقياً لا تكره إمامته لأنّ الكراهة للنقائص حتى إذا كان الإعرابي أفضل من الحضري والعبد من الحر، وولد الزنا من ولد الرشد، والأعمى من البصير، فالحكم بالضد كذا في الاختيار (و) لذا كره إمامة (الفاسق) العالم لعدم اهتمامه إلى الله تعالى ليحصل لهم مآربهم فيشفعون لكم، أو بمعنى الوفود أي الرسل بينكم، وبين ربكم، والكلام على التشبيه قوله : ( وكره إمامة العبد وكذا المعتق كما في الدر لغلبة الجهل، وأفاد الحموي أن كراهة الإقتداء بالعبد وما عطف عليه تنزيهية أن وجد غيرهم وإلا فلا اهـ من شرح السيد وسيأتي ما يفيد أن إمامة الفاسق مكروهة تحريماً . قوله : (إن لم يكن عالماً تقياً) أشار به إلى أن الكراهة في العبيد لا لذاتهم بل لأنهم لاشتغالهم بخدمة المولى لا يتفرغون للعلم فيغلب عليهم الجهل، ولندرة التقوى في العبيد فلو انتفى ذلك بأن كان عالماً تقياً فلا كراة قوله : ( لعدم إهتدائه إلخ) هذا يقتضي كراهة إمامة الأعشى نهر وهو الذي لا يبصر ليلا. قوله: (وصون ثيابه عطف على اهتدائه أي ولعدم صونه ثيابه الخ. قوله : (فلا كراهة) لاستخلاف النبي ابن أم مكتوم، وعتبان بن مالك على المدينة حين خرج إلى غزوة تبوك وكانا أعمين. قوله : ( والأعرابي) بفتح الهمزة نسبة إلى الأعراب وهم سكان البادية من العرب وعمم الأزهري، والعرب العاربة هم الخلص منهم وهم الذين تكلموا بلغة يعرب بن قحطان ، وهو اللسان القديم لأنه أول من تكلم بالعربية والعرب المستعربة الذين تكلموا بلسان اسمعيل عليه السلام وهو لغة أهل الحجاز وما والاها والمراد هنا كل من سكن البادية عربياً كان أو أعجمياً كالتركمان والأكراد لغلبة الجهل عليهم لبعدهم عن مجالس العلم، ومن ثمة قيل أهل أهل القبور وهذا ظاهر في كراهة العامي الذي لا علم عنده كما في البحر والنهر، وحكى أن أعرابياً إقتدى بإمام فقرأ الإمام آية الأعراب أشد كفراً ونفاقاً فضربه الأعرابي وشج رأسه، ثم اقتدى به بعد مدة فرآه الإمام فقرأ آية ومن الأعراب من يؤمن بالله واليوم إلا آخر الآن نفعك العصا كذا في غاية البيان قوله : (وولد الزنا) لأنه ليس له أب الكفور هم فقال الإعرابي: يعلمه فيغلب عليه الجهل فلو كان عنده علم لا كراهة واختار العيني التعليل بنفرة الناس عنه لكونه متهماً، وأقره في النهر، وعليه فينبغي ثبوت الكراهة مطلقاً إن لم يكن جاهلاً. قوله: (فلذا قيده إلخ) أي لأجل ما قيد به في قوله عالماً وفي الأعمى بقوله : وإن لم يوجد أفضل منه فلا كراهة وفي الأعرابي بقوله الجاهل. وفي ولد الزنا بقوله الذي لا علم عنده وفيه تأمل بالنظر للأعمى قوله : (إذ لو كان أي أحد من ذكر قوله فالحكم بالضد) فالكراهة في تقديم الحضري والحر، وولد الرشد والبصير لجهلهم لأن إمامة الجاهل مكروهة كيفما كان بالدين فتجب إهانته شرعاً، فلا يعظم بتقديمه للإمامة، وإذا تعذر منعه ينتقل عنه إلى غير مسجده للجمعة وغيرها وإن لم يقم الجمعة إلا هو تصلي معه (والمبتدع) بارتكابه ما أحدث على خلاف الحق المتلقى عن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم: من علم أو عمل أو مال بنوع شبهة، أو استحسان وروى محمد عن أبي حنيفة رحمه الله تعالى وأبي يوسف أن الصلاة خلف أهل الأهواء لا تجوز والصحيح أنها تصح مع الكراهة خلف من لا تكفره بدعته، لقوله : صلوا خلف كل بر وفاجر وصلوا على كل بر وفاجر وجاهدوا مع كل بر وفاجر» رواه الدارقطني كما في البرهان وقال في مجمع الروايات وإذا صلى خلف فاسق، أو مبتدع يكون محرزاً ثواب الجماعة لكن لا ينال ثواب من يصلي خلف إمام تقي (و) كره للإمام لعدم علمه بأحكام الصلاة قوله : (و) كره للإمام (المف) وقوله : (و) كره لإمامة (؟) ... على الصلاة خلف أمرد وسفيه ومفلوج، وأبرص شاع برصه ومراء ومتصنع ومجذوم، ولا خلف من أم بأجرة على
Your Lord, and in another narration: 'Let the best among you lead you in prayer.' Disliked is the imamah of a slave unless he is knowledgeable and pious; (the blind) because he cannot find the direction of the qibla nor keep his clothes clean, and if there is no one better than him, then there is no dislike; (the bedouin) the ignorant, or the city-dweller ignorant, and the child of adultery who has no knowledge nor piety. So he qualified it earlier with his saying 'the ignorant', because if he were knowledgeable and pious, his imamah would not be disliked, because the dislike is due to deficiencies. So if the bedouin is better than the city-dweller, and the slave better than the free, and the child of adultery better than the legitimate child, and the blind better than the sighted, then the ruling is the opposite. Thus in al-Ikhtiyar. (And) therefore disliked is the imamah of (the sinful person) even if learned, because he does not care... to Allah so that they may attain their needs and intercede for you, or in the sense of delegations, i.e., messengers between you and your Lord, and the speech is metaphorical. He said: (And disliked is the imamah of the slave and likewise the freed slave as in al-Durr due to prevalence of ignorance, and al-Hamawi stated that the dislike of following a slave and what is attached to it is tanzihi (disliked but not sinful) if there is someone else, otherwise no dislike, end. From the commentary of al-Sayyid, and later it will come that the imamah of a sinful person is makruh tahriman. He said: (If he is not knowledgeable and pious) he pointed thereby that the dislike regarding slaves is not due to their essence but because they are busy serving their master and do not have time for knowledge, so ignorance prevails among them, and due to rarity of piety among slaves. So if that is absent, i.e., he is knowledgeable and pious, then no dislike. He said: (From lack of guidance etc.) This necessitates dislike of imamah of the one who is blind at night (a'sha). He said: (And keeping his clothes clean) is conjunct to 'his guidance', meaning and due to his failure to keep his clothes clean etc. He said: (So no dislike) because the Prophet appointed Ibn Umm Maktum and 'Itban ibn Malik over Medina when he went out to the expedition of Tabuk, and they were blind. He said: (And the bedouin) with fatha on the hamza, relative to the bedouins, who are the desert-dwelling Arabs, and al-Azhari generalized; the pure Arabs (Arab 'aribah) are the pure ones who spoke the language of Ya'rub bin Qahtan, which is the ancient tongue because he was the first to speak Arabic; and the Arabized Arabs (Arab musta'ribah) who spoke the tongue of Isma'il (peace be upon him), which is the language of the Hijaz and its environs. What is meant here is everyone who lives in the desert, whether Arab or non-Arab like Turkomans and Kurds, due to the prevalence of ignorance among them because of their distance from gatherings of knowledge. Hence it was said: 'People of graves'. This is apparent in the dislike of the imamah of the commoner who has no knowledge, as in al-Bahr and al-Nahr. And it is narrated that a bedouin followed an imam, and the imam recited the verse 'The bedouins are the most severe in disbelief and hypocrisy', so the bedouin struck him and wounded his head. Then later he followed him again, and the imam recited the verse 'And among the bedouins are those who believe in Allah and the Last Day' to the end; the bedouin said: 'The stick benefited you now.' As mentioned in Ghayat al-Bayan. He said: (And the child of adultery) because he has no father... the ungrateful ones. So the bedouin said: 'It teaches him, so ignorance prevails over him.' If he had knowledge, there would be no dislike. Al-'Ayni chose the reasoning that people shun him because he is accused, and it was affirmed in al-Nahr. Based on this, dislike should be established absolutely if he is not ignorant. He said: (So he qualified it etc.) i.e., because of what he qualified with in his saying 'knowledgeable', and regarding the blind by his saying 'and if there is no one better than him, then no dislike', and regarding the bedouin by his saying 'the ignorant', and regarding the child of adultery by his saying 'who has no knowledge'. There is reflection regarding the blind. He said: (If any of those mentioned... then the ruling is the opposite) So dislike is for presenting the city-dweller and free, and the legitimate child and sighted, due to their ignorance, because the imamah of the ignorant is disliked in any case. ... due to religion, so it is obligatory to humiliate him legally, so he is not honored by being put forward for imamah. If preventing him is difficult, one should move away from him to another mosque for Friday and other prayers, even if Friday prayer is not established except with him, then you pray with him. (And the innovator) by committing what he innovates contrary to the truth received from the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him), in knowledge, action, or wealth, due to some kind of doubt or istihsan. Muhammad narrated from Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf that prayer behind people of desires is not permissible. The correct view is that it is valid with dislike behind one whose innovation does not render him a disbeliever, due to his saying: 'Pray behind every righteous and sinful person, and pray over every righteous and sinful person, and strive with every righteous and sinful person.' Narrated by al-Daraqutni as in al-Burhan. And he said in Majma' al-Riwayat: If one prays behind a sinful person or an innovator, he attains the reward of congregation but does not attain the reward of one who prays behind a pious imam. (And) disliked for the imam due to his lack of knowledge of the rulings of prayer. He said: (And) disliked for the imam (al-muff?) And he said: (And) disliked for imamah (?) ... upon prayer behind a beardless youth, a foolish person, a paralyzed person, a leper whose leprosy is notorious, a hypocritical person, an affected person, a leprous person, and not behind one who leads for a fee.
Source pages p. 302

Commentary
This passage from Hashiyat al-Tahtawi on Maraqi al-Falah is a critical refinement of the rulings on who is disliked (makruh) to lead congregational prayer. The text opens by citing a hadith that the best among you should lead. It then lists categories: a slave (unless knowledgeable and pious), a blind person (due to inability to find qibla and keep clothes clean), a bedouin (ignorant), a city-dweller ignorant, and a child of adultery (with no knowledge or piety). The key principle is: dislike arises from deficiencies; if the person is actually more virtuous than others, the ruling reverses. For the blind, if no better imam exists, there is no dislike, as evidenced by the Prophet appointing blind companions as governors. For the bedouin and child of adultery, dislike is conditional on ignorance; if they are knowledgeable, no dislike. A story illustrates the bedouin's ignorance. The text then covers the sinful person (fasiq): his imamah is disliked tahriman (prohibitively) because he must be humiliated, not honored. If possible, one should switch mosques. For the innovator (mubtadi'), there is an intra-Hanafi dispute: Muhammad and Abu Yusuf narrate that prayer behind such is invalid, but the relied-upon (sahih) position is that it is valid with dislike, as long as the innovation does not amount to disbelief. A hadith 'Pray behind every righteous and sinful person' supports this. However, the reward is less than behind a pious imam. The passage ends by listing other disliked imams: beardless youth, foolish, paralyzed, leprous, hypocritical, affected, and those who lead for a fee. The overall ruling is that imamah of these persons is disliked when better alternatives exist; otherwise, no dislike. The hashiya clarifies the conditions and balances hadith evidence with rational principles like istihsan.

Key Terms
كراهة تنزيهية (karahah tanzihiyyah): Dislike that is not prohibited; it is better to avoid but not sinful.
فاسق (fasiq): One who commits major sins or persists on minor sins, without valid interpretation.
مبتدع (mubtadi'): One who innovates in religion something contrary to the received truth, whether in knowledge, action, or wealth, based on doubt or istihsan.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on praying behind a mubtadi' (innovator) whose innovation does not lead to kufr?
A) The prayer is invalid.
B) The prayer is valid and not disliked.
C) The prayer is valid but disliked (makruh tanzihi).
D) The prayer is valid but prohibitively disliked (makruh tahrimi).

Key Takeaway
Praying behind a fasiq is makruh tahrimi; behind a mubtadi' (non-kufr innovation) it is valid with dislike, and this is the mufta bihi.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
8 min
Ruling on praying behind a fasiq or mubtadi' imam
Commentary on the ruling of imamah of fasiq and mubtadi'

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on praying behind a fasiq or mubtadi' imam, identify the primary evidence, and apply the distinction between fasiq bil-jariha and fasiq bil-aqida to determine validity and dislike.

Core Idea
Prayer behind a sinful or non-kafir innovator is valid but disliked; the imam's sin does not invalidate the follower's prayer.

This lesson explores the Hanafi position on leading prayer by a person who commits sins or holds innovative beliefs. The source passage, from al-Tahtawi's Hashiya, clarifies that such an imam's imamah is valid but makruh tahriman, supported by a prophetic command. You will learn the conditions, evidence, and practical implications of this ruling, including the important distinction between sin by action and sin by creed.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is praying behind an imam who is a fasiq (sinner) or mubtadi' (innovator). According to the text, the ruling is that the prayer is valid but disliked (makruh). Determine whether the dislike is prohibitive (tahrimi) or merely offensive (tanzihi).
The text specifies that the fasiq referred to is the one who sins with his limbs (major sins or persistence in minor sins), not the one whose beliefs are corrupt.
2
Locate the dalil
The primary evidence cited is the hadith: "Pray behind every righteous and sinful person..." reported by al-Daraqutni. This hadith is a general command that includes sinful individuals, indicating permissibility.
The hadith is classified as ahad, thus zanni al-thubut, but it is sufficient for establishing the ruling.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The imperative 'sallu' (pray) indicates permissibility (ibaha) or obligation, but in context it allows following such imams. The general phrase 'kulli barri wa fajir' (every righteous and sinful) includes all Muslims, establishing validity behind sinners as long as they are not disbelievers.
The text also uses this to override the earlier view of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf that it was not permissible.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
There is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf: initially Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf held that prayer behind ahl al-ahwa (people of desires) is not permissible. The correct view (as-Sahih) is permissibility with dislike. Also, the nature of the dislike is debated: whether it is tahrimi or tanzihi affects whether following such an imam is preferable to praying alone.
The text sides with the view that the dislike is tahrimi, following al-Zayla'i, and that following them is better than being alone if no righteous imam is available.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position is that prayer behind a fasiq or non-kafir mubtadi' is valid but makruh tahriman. Following such an imam is better than praying alone, especially if otherwise the congregation would be lost.
This is based on the research in al-Bahr and the principle of maintaining the obligation of congregation.

كتاب الصلاة بالدين فتجب إهانته شرعاً، فلا يعظم بتقديمه للإمامة، وإذا تعذر منعه ينتقل عنه إلى غير مسجده للجمعة وغيرها وإن لم يقم الجمعة إلا هو تصلي معه (والمبتدع) بارتكابه ما أحدث على خلاف الحق المتلقى عن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم: من علم أو عمل أو مال بنوع شبهة، أو استحسان وروى محمد عن أبي حنيفة رحمه الله تعالى وأبي يوسف أن الصلاة خلف أهل الأهواء لا تجوز والصحيح أنها تصح مع الكراهة خلف من لا تكفره بدعته، لقوله : صلوا خلف كل بر وفاجر وصلوا على كل بر وفاجر وجاهدوا مع كل بر وفاجر» رواه الدارقطني كما في البرهان وقال في مجمع الروايات وإذا صلى خلف فاسق، أو مبتدع يكون محرزاً ثواب الجماعة لكن لا ينال ثواب من يصلي خلف إمام تقي (و) كره للإمام لعدم علمه بأحكام الصلاة قوله : (ولذا كره إمامة (الفاسق أي لما ذكر من قوله : حتى إذا كان الأعرابي الخ فكراهته لأفضلية غيره عليه، والمراد الفاسق بالجارحة لا بالعقيدة، لأن ذا سيذكر بالمبتدع، والفسق لغة خروج عن الاستقامة وهو معنى قولهم خروج الشيء عن الشيء على وجه الفساد، وشرعاً، خروج عن طاعة الله تعالى بارتكاب كبيرة، قال القهستاني : أي أو إصرار على صغيرة، وينبغي أن يراد بلا تأويل وإلا فيشكل بالبغاة، وذلك كتمام ومراء وشارب خمر اهـ. قوله : ( فتجب إهانته شرعاً فلا يعظم بتقديمه للإمامة) تبع فيه الزيلعي، ومفاده كون الكراهة في الفاسق تحريمية. قوله : (من) (علم كمنكر الرؤية، أو عمل كمن يؤذن بحي على خير العمل، أو حال كأن يسكت معتقداً أن مطلق السكوت قربة قوله : (بنوع شبهة أو استحسان) وجعله ديناً قويماً وصراطاً مستقيماً، وهو متعلق بقوله بارتكاب قوله: (والصحيح) أي عنهما . قوله: (خلف من لا تكفره بدعته) فلا تجوز الصلاة خلف من ينكر شفاعة النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم أو الكرام الكاتبين أو الرؤية لأنه كافر وإن قال لا يرى لجلاله وعظمته فهو مبتدع والمشبه كأن قال الله يد أو رجل كالعباد كافر، وإن قال هو جسم لا كالأجسام فهو مبتدع، وإن أنكر خلافة الصديق كفر كمن أنكر الإسراء لا المعراج وألحق في الفتح عمر بالصديق في هذا الحكم، وألحق في البرهان عثمان بهما أيضاً ولا تجوز الصلاة خلف منكر المسح على الخفين، أو صحبة الصديق، أو من يسب الشيخين أو يقذف الصديقة، ولا خلف من أنكر بعض ما علم من الدين ضرورة لكفره ولا يلتفت إلى تأوله واجتهاده وتجوز خلف من يفضل علياً على غيره. قوله : يكون محرزاً ثواب (الجماعة أي مع الكراهة إن وجد غيرهم وإلا فلا كراهة كما في البحر بحثاً وفي السراج هل الأفضل أن يصلي خلف هؤلاء أم الأنفراد قيل أما في الفاسق فالصلاة خلفه أولى وهذا إنما يظهر على أن إمامته مكروهة تنزيهاً أما على القول بكراهة التحريم فلا وأما الآخرون فيمكن أن يقال الانفراد أولى لجهلهم بشروط الصلاة ويمكن إجراؤهم على قياس الصلاة خلف الفاسق وجزم في البحر بأن الاقتداء بهم أفضل من الإنفراد وتكره الصلاة خلف أمرد وسفيه ومفلوج، وأبرص شاع برصه ومراء ومتصنع ومجذوم، ولا خلف من أم بأجرة على
The Book of Prayer. Because of the religion, his humiliation is obligatory legally, so he is not honored by being put forward for imamah. If preventing him is difficult, one moves from his mosque to another for Friday and other prayers, and even if no one holds Friday but him, one prays with him. (And the innovator) by committing what he innovates contrary to the truth received from the Messenger of Allah, may Allah bless him and grant him peace: whether in knowledge, action, or wealth by way of doubt or approval. Muhammad narrated from Abu Hanifa, may Allah have mercy on him, and Abu Yusuf that prayer behind the people of desires is not permissible. The correct view is that it is valid with dislike behind one whose innovation does not make him a disbeliever, due to his statement: 'Pray behind every righteous and sinful person, pray over every righteous and sinful person, and fight jihad with every righteous and sinful person.' Ad-Daraqutni narrated it as in Al-Burhan. He said in Majma' al-Riwayat: 'If one prays behind a sinner or innovator, he attains the reward of congregation but not the reward of one who prays behind a pious imam.' (And it is disliked for the imam) due to his lack of knowledge of the rulings of prayer. His statement: (Thus the imamah of the sinner is disliked) i.e., because of what he mentioned of the statement 'until if the Bedouin...' so its dislike is due to the superiority of another over him. The intended meaning is the sinner by the limbs, not by creed, because the latter will be mentioned with the innovator. Linguistically, sin is deviation from uprightness, which is the meaning of their saying: 'the exiting of a thing from the thing in a corrupt manner.' Legally, it is deviation from obedience to Allah Almighty by committing a major sin. Al-Qahistani said: 'i.e., or persistence in a minor sin.' It should be understood without interpretation, otherwise it would be problematic with the rebels. That includes the perfect, the argumentative, and the wine drinker. His statement: (Thus his humiliation is obligatory legally, so he is not honored by being put forward for imamah) He follows Az-Zayla'i in that, and its implication is that the dislike regarding the sinner is prohibitive. His statement: (from) (knowledge like one who denies the vision, or action like one who calls to 'hayya 'ala khayr al-amal', or state like one who remains silent believing that absolute silence is a means of proximity. His statement: (by way of doubt or approval) and he makes it a upright religion and straight path. It is related to his statement 'by committing'. His statement: (And the correct view) i.e., from them (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf). His statement: (behind one whose innovation does not make him a disbeliever) For prayer is not permissible behind one who denies the intercession of the Prophet, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, or the noble scribes, or the vision, because he is a disbeliever. If he says 'He is not seen due to His majesty and greatness,' he is an innovator. The anthropomorphist, such as one who says 'Allah has a hand or foot like servants,' is a disbeliever. If he says 'He is a body not like bodies,' he is an innovator. If he denies the caliphate of Abu Bakr, he disbelieves, like one who denies the Night Journey but not the Ascension. In Al-Fath, Umar is joined to Abu Bakr in this ruling, and in Al-Burhan, Uthman is also joined to them. Prayer is not permissible behind one who denies wiping over the socks, or the companionship of Abu Bakr, or one who curses the two shaykhs or accuses Aisha, nor behind one who denies something known of the religion by necessity, due to his disbelief. No attention is paid to his interpretation and ijtihad. And it is permissible behind one who prefers Ali over others. His statement: (he attains the reward of congregation) i.e., with dislike if there is another, otherwise there is no dislike, as a research in Al-Bahr. In As-Siraj: 'Is it better to pray behind these or to pray alone?' It was said: 'As for the sinner, praying behind him is better.' This only appears if his imamah is disliked as a minor dislike. As for the view of prohibitive dislike, then not. As for the others, it can be said that praying alone is better due to their ignorance of the conditions of prayer, and they can be treated analogously to prayer behind a sinner. In Al-Bahr, it is decided that following them is better than praying alone. And prayer is disliked behind an adolescent boy, a foolish person, a paralyzed person, a leper whose leprosy has spread, an argumentative person, an affected person, a leprous person, and behind one who leads for a fee.
Source pages p. 303

Commentary
This passage is an expansion probe on the ruling of praying behind a fasiq (sinner) or mubtadi' (innovator) imam. The commentator begins by explaining that a fasiq must be humiliated legally because of his lack of religion, thus he should not be given honor by being put forward as imam. If one cannot prevent him from leading, one should move to another mosque. However, if no one else holds the Friday prayer, one should pray with him to maintain the obligation. The text then defines a mubtadi' as one who innovates in knowledge, action, or wealth, contrary to the received truth, based on doubt or approval. It reports that Imam Muhammad narrated from Imam Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf that prayer behind the 'people of desires' (ahl al-ahwa) is not permissible. However, the correct view (as-Sahih) is that it is valid with dislike (makruh tahriman) behind one whose innovation does not constitute disbelief. The proof is the hadith narrated by Ad-Daraqutni: 'Pray behind every righteous and sinful person, pray over every righteous and sinful person, and fight jihad with every righteous and sinful person.' The commentator clarifies that the fasiq referred to is the one who sins with his limbs (by committing major sins or persisting in minor sins), not the one who has corrupt beliefs, as that is the mubtadi'. The dislike is due to the superiority of a righteous imam. The ruling includes details about who is considered a disbeliever due to their innovation: denying the vision of Allah, the intercession of the Prophet, the noble scribes, the caliphate of Abu Bakr, the Night Journey, or the permissibility of wiping over socks. Those who merely hold anthropomorphic views (e.g., saying Allah has a hand like servants) are disbelievers, while those who say 'He is a body not like bodies' are innovators. The passage also discusses that if one prays behind a fasiq, he attains the reward of congregation but not the reward of praying behind a pious imam. The karahah is tahrimi (prohibitive) as per Az-Zayla'i. There is an intra-Hanafi dispute: on the view that the dislike is tanzihi (minor), praying behind a fasiq is better than praying alone; on the view of tahrimi, it is not. For other types like amrad (beardless youth), safih (fool), etc., the passage states it is disliked, and the preferred view in Al-Bahr is that following them is better than being alone.

Key Terms
فاسق (fasiq): One who deviates from obedience to Allah by committing major sins or persisting in minor sins, without justifiable interpretation.
مبتدع (mubtadi'): One who innovates in knowledge, action, or wealth contrary to the received truth based on doubt or approval.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the primary evidence for the ruling that prayer behind a fasiq is valid?
A) Analogical reasoning (qiyas) from a valid imam
B) The hadith 'Pray behind every righteous and sinful person'
C) The consensus of the sahabah
D) The statement of Abu Hanifa

Key Takeaway
Prayer behind a fasiq or non-kafir mubtadi' is valid but makruh tahriman; the follower attains congregation reward but not full reward of a pious imam.

Salah — Prayer

Makruh Acts for the Imam and Congregation
Commentary on three makruh acts related to leading prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on three makruh acts during congregational prayer and explain the evidence from hadith.

Core Idea
Prolonging prayer, naked congregation, and women-led congregation are prohibitively disliked due to underlying prohibitions.

In this lesson, we examine three situations that the Hanafi school classifies as makruh tahriman (prohibitively disliked) when performing or leading congregational prayer. Each stems from a core concern: avoiding hardship for the congregation, preventing exposure of 'awrah, and averting fitna (temptation). Understanding these rulings helps the imam and congregation preserve the sunnah and maintain proper adab in prayer.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three acts and their rulings
From the passage, list the three acts: prolonging prayer (tathil al-salat), congregation of naked people (jama'at al-'aratin), and women's congregation with a female imam (jama'at al-nisa). Note that each is ruled as makruh tahriman.
The text states 'kariha' (disliked) and the commentary specifies 'tahriman' (prohibitively).
2
Locate the primary dalil for each
The main proof for prolonging prayer is the hadith 'Whoever leads the people, let him lighten' (narrated by al-Shaykhan). For naked congregation, the dalil is the necessity of covering 'awrah and avoiding one of two prohibitions. For women's congregation, the proof is the command to stay in homes and the hadith that a woman's prayer in her house is better.
The passage uses multiple narrations to support each ruling.
3
Analyze the wajh al-dalalah for the hadith
The command 'falyukhaffif' (let him lighten) is an imperative. In Hanafi usul, the imperative indicates obligation, but here it is understood as indicating dislike because the primary concern is to avoid repelling the congregation. The hadith 'among you are those who repel others' shows that prolonging is a cause of repulsion.
The commentary explains that the imam should even omit sunnah amounts to accommodate the congregation's condition.
4
Understand the intra-Hanafi discussion
While some scholars may differentiate between makruh tanzihi and tahrimi, the relied-upon position in the later school is makruh tahrimi for all three. The passage quotes al-Badr al-Ayni and Allamah Nuh emphasizing the prohibition.
The mufta bihi position is that prolonging prayer is makruh; naked congregation should pray individually; women's congregation is makruh but valid.
5
Apply the mufta bihi position to new scenarios
For a modern imam, prolonging recitation unnecessarily is makruh. For a group of people without clothing, they should pray individually or, if they pray in congregation, do so sitting with gestures. For women, a female-led congregation is makruh, but if a man leads them, there is no dislike provided a mahram is present.
The passage also notes exceptions for funeral prayer and situations of necessity.

Commentary
This passage is an expansion probe on three matters that are makruh (disliked) for the imam or the congregation. First, prolonging the prayer (tathil al-salat) is makruh because it repels the congregation. The proof is the hadith 'Whoever leads the people, let him lighten' (narrated by Bukhari and Muslim). The commentator explains that the imam should even omit the sunnah amounts for the sake of the congregation, as evidenced by the Prophet's action in Fajr when he heard a child crying and shortened his recitation. Second, the congregational prayer of naked people (jama'at al-'aratin) is prohibitively makruh because it leads to either the imam not standing forward (which is a requirement for a non-mixed congregation) or the increase of exposure of private parts. The better option is for them to pray alone sitting with gestures. Third, the congregation of women (jama'at al-nisa) with one of them as imam is also prohibitively makruh because it requires either the imam standing in the first row or advancing, both of which are disliked. Women should not attend mixed congregations due to temptation and the command to stay in homes. However, if a woman leads, she must stand in the middle of the row (not in front). The passage also discusses exceptions: if a man leads women, there is no dislike unless there is no mahram present. For funeral prayer, women's congregation is not disliked because it is not repeated. The commentator also includes a discussion on following a mukhalif (one who differs in subsidiary matters), quoting Al-Badr al-Ayni that it is permissible as long as the imam is not a kafir innovator, and following such is better than praying alone.

Key Terms
تطويل الصلاة (tathil al-salat): Prolonging the prayer beyond the normal length, especially by the imam, causing hardship to the congregation.
جماعة العراة (jama'at al-'aratin): Congregational prayer performed by people who are naked (have no clothing to cover their 'awrah).
جماعة النساء (jama'at al-nisa): A congregation consisting solely of women led by a female imam.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school prohibits prolonging prayer, naked congregation, and women-led congregation to protect the congregation from hardship, exposure of 'awrah, and fitna.

Ruling on Prolonging Prayer in Congregation
Commentary on the ruling of prolonging prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on prolonging prayer in congregation and explain the dalil that prohibits it.

Core Idea
Prolonging prayer by the imam is makruh tahrimi because it repels the congregation.

This passage from Hashiya al-Tahtawi clarifies the ruling on an imam prolonging the prayer. The commentary emphasizes that the Prophet ﷺ commanded lightening the prayer, and the imam's duty is to consider the congregation's well-being, even if it means omitting some recommended recitations.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is prolonging prayer (tadwil) by recitation, tasbih, or other means. The ruling is makruh tahrimi (disliked to the degree of prohibition).
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is the hadith: 'Whoever leads the people, let him lighten it' (Sahih al-Bukhari and Muslim). The authority also cites the story of the Prophet shortening Fajr when he heard a baby crying.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The imperative 'falyukhaffif' indicates obligation in Hanafi usul (al-amr yufidu al-wujub). However, the ruling is not fard but makruh tahrimi because the act of shortening itself is not obligatory; rather, it is a directive to avoid causing hardship.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Some schools consider it permissible to prolong if the congregation consents, but Hanafis hold that the command is general regardless of consent.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(تطويل الصلاة) لما فيه من تنفير الجماعة لقوله عليه السلام من أم فليخفف قوله: (تطويل (الصلاة) بقراءة أو تسبيح أو غيرهما رضي القوم أم لا لإطلاق الأمر بالتخفيف قوله : (من أم فليخفف) ذكر الشيخ في كبيره حديث يا أيها الناس إن منكم منفرين من صلى بالناس فليخفف فإن منهم الكبير والضعيف وذا الحاجة رواه الشيخان، وهذا يفيد أن الإمام يترك القدر المسنون مراعاة لحال القوم اهـ يؤيده ما في الصحيحين أنه قرأ بالمعوذتين في الفجر فلما فرغ قالوا له : أوجزت قال: سمعت بكاء فخشيت أن تفتن .أمه
(Prolonging prayer) because it repels the congregation, due to his statement (peace be upon him): 'Whoever leads the people in prayer, let him lighten it.' His statement: (Prolonging prayer) with recitation, glorification, or other things, whether the people are pleased or not, due to the general command of lightening. Whoever leads the people in prayer, let him lighten it, for among them are the old, the weak, and those with needs.' Narrated by al-Bukhari and Muslim. This indicates that the imam should omit the Sunnah amount out of consideration for the congregation. Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the ruling that it is disliked (makruh) for an imam to prolong the prayer, as it drives people away from the congregation. The proof is the prophetic hadith commanding lightening. The hashia explains that this command is general, applying whether the congregation is pleased or not, and that the imam should even omit recommended (sunnah) recitations if necessary. The story from the Sahihain illustrates the Prophet's practice of shortening prayer when he heard a baby crying, showing that the well-being of the congregation takes precedence over supererogatory lengthening.

Key Terms
تطويل (tadwil): Prolonging the prayer beyond what is appropriate, whether by recitation, dhikr, or other means.
تنفير (tanfir): Causing people to leave or dislike attending the congregation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
An imam must lighten the prayer out of consideration for the congregation; prolonging it is makruh tahrimi even if the congregation consents.

Ruling on Congregation of Naked People (Jama'at al-Ura)
Commentary on the ruling of naked persons praying in congregation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for a congregation of naked persons and explain the legal reasoning behind the prohibition.

Core Idea
Congregation of naked persons is prohibitively disliked because it forces a choice between two wrongs.

This lesson examines the specific ruling of a group of people who have no clothing and wish to pray in congregation. While covering the awrah is an obligation for prayer, necessity may force people into this situation. The Hanafi school provides clear guidance: the congregation is makruh tahrimi, and the better option is for each to pray individually.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is forming a congregation while all are naked. The ruling is makruh tahrimi (prohibitively disliked).
2
Understand the reason
Two prohibited acts are necessarily involved: either abandoning the wajib of the imam standing forward, or increasing exposure of private parts.
This is a case of tazahum al-haramayn (conflict of two prohibitions).
3
Determine the better practice
The preferred method is for each to pray individually, sitting, with gestures (isharah), and spaced apart to avoid seeing each other's awrah.
Individual prayer avoids the conflict entirely.
4
Note the concession
If they do choose to congregate despite the dislike, they should still pray sitting with gestures.
The congregation remains makruh tahrimi, but this method minimizes additional exposure.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(وجماعة العراة) لما فيها من الاطلاع على عورات بعضهم قوله: (وجماعة العراة) أي تكره جماعة العراة تحريماً للزوم أحد المحظورين وهو إما ترك واجب التقدم، أو زيادة الكشف والأفضل صلاتهم منفردين قعوداً بالإيماء متباعدين عن بعض لئلا يقع بصرهم على عورة بعض كما أن الأفضل لهم إن صلوا جماعة أن يصلوا قعوداً بالإيماء.
(And the congregation of naked people) because it involves seeing each other's private parts. His statement: (And the congregation of naked people) meaning that the congregation of naked people is disliked to the degree of prohibition because it necessitates one of two prohibited things: either abandoning the obligatory forward positioning, or increasing exposure. It is better for them to pray individually, sitting, with gestures, distant from each other so that their eyes do not fall on each other's private parts. Similarly, if they do pray in congregation, it is better that they pray sitting with gestures.
Source pages p. 304

Commentary
This passage rules that it is makruh tahrimi for naked people to form a congregation. The reason is that it inevitably leads to one of two prohibitions: either they abandon the wajib of the imam standing forward, or they increase the exposure of private parts. The recommended course is for them to pray individually, sitting and using gestures (ishaarah), and positioned apart to avoid seeing each other's awrah. If they do pray together, the same method is preferable.

Key Terms
جماعة العراة (jama'at al-ura): A congregation of people whose private parts are necessarily exposed due to lack of clothing (e.g., in a disaster).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling for a group of naked people praying in congregation?
A) Permissible if they stand far apart.
B) Makruh tahrimi, better to pray individually.
C) Sunnah to pray in congregation.
D) Haram regardless of circumstances.

Key Takeaway
Congregation of naked persons is makruh tahrimi; the best practice is to pray individually, sitting, with gestures, and at a distance.
